The Meaning of Masih and the Descent of Jesus
Explanation of Masih and the second sign

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three explanations for why Jesus is called Masih and why his descent is the second major sign of the Hour.

Core Idea
Jesus is the Masih because of his healing, blessing, and journeying.

Dardeer begins the section on sam'iyyat (matters from revelation) by clarifying the title 'Masih' given to Jesus. He then introduces the second portent of the Last Day: the descent of Jesus to kill the Dajjal. This passage sets the stage for understanding the end-time events as taught by revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the meaning of Masih
Read the Arabic passage that explains why Jesus is called Masih. Note the three reasons given.
The Arabic may be incomplete; focus on the explanations provided.
2
Identify the second sign
Find where Dardeer states the second sign of the Hour: the descent of Jesus and his killing of the Dajjal.
3
Reflect on the Sahih hadith
Read the hadith from Sahih that describes Jesus' actions upon descent: breaking the cross, killing the pig, and abolishing the jizya.
This hadith is a key proof for the reality of this event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات

ما نزلت عاهة إلا بَرِئَ بِإِذْنِ اللهِ تعالى، وقيلَ: لأَنه مُمسوح بالبَرَكَةِ. وسُمّي عيسى مسيحا لمسحه الأرض، أي سياحته فيها، وقيل: لأنه ما مسح على

ثانيها: نُزول المسيح عيسى بنِ مَرْيَمَ عليه الصلاة والسلامُ مِنَ السماء، وقتله للدجال، ففي الصحيح (لينزلن) ابنُ مَرْيَمَ حكَمًا عدلًا فليكسرنَّ الصليب، وليقْتُلنَّ الخنزير، وليضَعَنَّ الجزية) الحديثُ.

وفي مُسندِ أحمدَ مِنْ حديث جابر: (يخرُجُ الدجّالُ في خفقة مِنَ الدين وإدبار منَ العِلم، وله أربعون ليلة يسيحُها في الأرضِ اليَومُ منها كالسَّنةِ، واليَومُ كالشهر، واليومُ منها كالجمعة، ثُمَّ سائرُ أَيَّامَه كأيَّامِكُم هذه، وله حمارٌ يركبه، عرْضُ جانب أذنيه أربعون ذراعًا، فيقول للناس: أنا ربُّكم، وهو أعورُ، وإِنَّ رَبَّكم لَيسَ بأَعُورَ، مكتوبٌ بَينَ عَيْنَيْه كافر، يقرؤه كُلّ مؤمن كاتب وغَيْرِ كاتب، يَرِدُ كُلَّ ماءٍ ومنهل إلا المدينة ومكةَ حرَّمهما الله عليه، وأقامت الملائكةُ بأبوابها، ومعَه جَبالٌ مِنْ خُبز، والناسُ في جَهدِ إلا مَنْ تبعه، ومعه نهران أنا أَعْلَمُ بهما منه، نهرٌ يقولُ الجنَّةُ ونهر يقولُ النار، فمَنْ أُدْخِلَ الذي يُسمّيه الجنّةَ فهو في النار، ومن أُدْخِلَ الذي يُسمّيهِ النار فهو في الجنة.

قال: وتُبْعَثُ معه شياطينُ تِلكم، ومعَه فتنةٌ عظيمةٌ، يَأمُرُ السماءَ تُمطِرُ فيمطر، ويقتُلُ نفْسًا ثُمَّ يُحييها فيما يرى الناسُ، فيقولُ للناس: أيها الناسُ فهل يفعَلُ مِثلَ هذا إلا الربُّ، فيفرُّ الناسُ إلى جبَلِ الدُّخانِ بالشام، فيأتيهم فيُحاصِرُهم، فيشتد حصارُهم ويُجهِدُهم جَهدًا شديدًا، ثُمَّ يَنزِلُ عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ فيأتي في السَّحَر فيقولُ: أَيُّها الناسُ ما يمْنعُكم أنْ تَخرُجوا إلى هذا الكذاب الخبيث، فينطلقون فإذا هم بعيسى فتقام الصلاةُ، فيُقالُ له: تقدَّم يا رُوحَ الله، فيقولُ: ليَتَقَدَّمْ إمامُكُم فليصل بكم، فإذا صلوا صلاةَ الصُّبْح خرجوا إليه، فحين يراه الكذاب فينماعُ -أي: يذوبُ - كما ينماعُ الملح في الماء، فيقتله حتى إنَّ الشجَرَ والحَجَرَ يُنادي يا روح الله هذا يهودي، فلا يترك ممن كان يتبَعُه أَحَدًا إلا قتَلَه. وفي الصحيح أحاديثُ بمعنى ذلك. انتهى، ذكره السيوطي.
The third section: matters heard from revelation. No ailment descended except it was cured by Allah's permission, and it was said: because he is anointed with blessing. And Jesus was called Messiah because he traversed the earth, meaning his journeying in it, and it was said: because he wiped over... Second matter: The descent of the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace and blessings be upon him, from heaven, and his killing of the Dajjal. In the Sahih: 'The son of Mary will surely descend as a just judge; he will break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya' the hadith. And in the Musnad of Ahmad from the hadith of Jabir: 'The Dajjal will emerge in a lapse of religion and a turning away from knowledge. He will have forty nights during which he will traverse the earth; one day will be like a year, one day like a month, one day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days. He will ride a donkey with a distance of forty cubits between its ears. He will say to the people: I am your Lord, and he is one-eyed, but your Lord is not one-eyed. Between his eyes it is written 'disbeliever', which every believer, literate or illiterate, will read. He will visit every watering place except Medina and Mecca, which Allah has forbidden to him, and the angels stand at their gates. He will have mountains of bread, while the people are in severe hunger except those who follow him. He will have two rivers—I know them better than he—one river appears as Paradise and one as Fire. Whoever enters what he calls Paradise will be in the Fire, and whoever enters what he calls Fire will be in Paradise. He will send with him devils of those times, and there will be a great trial. He will command the sky to rain and it will rain, and he will kill a soul and then revive it in the sight of the people. He will say to the people: O people, does anyone except the Lord do such things? Then the people will flee to the Mountain of Smoke in Syria. He will come to them and besiege them, and the siege will become severe and he will afflict them severely. Then Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, will descend and come at dawn, saying: O people, what prevents you from going out against this lying wicked one? They will set out and behold, they will be with Jesus. The prayer will be established, and it will be said to him: Step forward, O Spirit of Allah. He will say: Let your imam step forward and lead you in prayer. When they have prayed the morning prayer, they will go out to him. When the liar sees him, he will dissolve like salt dissolves in water, and he will kill him until the tree and the stone call out: O Spirit of Allah, this is a Jew. He will not leave anyone who followed him except he kills him. In the Sahih there are hadiths to that effect. End. Mentioned by Suyuti.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the discussion on sam'iyyat (matters known from revelation) concerning the signs of the Hour. It begins with an explanation of why Jesus is called Masih, offering three reasons: because no ailment descended upon him except it was cured by Allah's permission (i.e., he healed by God's will), because he is anointed with blessing, and because he traveled the earth. Then it proceeds to the second sign: the descent of Jesus from heaven and his killing of the Dajjal. The author cites the Sahih hadith that Jesus will descend as a just judge, break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya. Then a lengthy hadith from Ahmad describes the Dajjal in detail: his emergence during a lapse of religion, his forty days of unusual length, his one-eyed appearance, the writing 'disbeliever' on his forehead, his false miracles including providing bread while causing hunger, his two rivers that appear as Paradise and Fire but are actually the opposite, his ability to command rain and revive a dead person. The people flee to the Mountain of Smoke. Jesus descends, refuses to lead the prayer deferring to the Muslim imam, then after prayer goes out to confront the Dajjal. The Dajjal melts like salt, and Jesus kills him, while trees and stones help identify Jews. The passage concludes with Suyuti's note that authentic hadith support this.

Key Terms
المسيح
السمعيات
نزول عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second sign of the Hour?
A) The emergence of the Dajjal
B) The descent of Jesus
C) The rising of the sun from the west
D) The smoke

Key Takeaway
Jesus is called Masih because of his healing, blessing, and traveling, and his descent is a major portent of the Last Day.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Jesus will descend as a just judge? How does that certainty affect your actions today? Are you living as if the Hour is near?
?
The Prophet ﷺ described Jesus as breaking the cross and killing the pig. What false practices or beliefs have you clung to that need to be 'broken' in your life? Commit to one change this week.
?
Jesus was called Masih because he healed and blessed others. In what ways can you be a source of healing and blessing to those around you? What is one concrete step you will take today?

The Detailed Description of the Dajjal and Its Defeat by Jesus
Detailed narrative of the Dajjal from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific attributes, false miracles, and ultimate defeat of the Dajjal as narrated in the hadith.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's false miracles are exposed by Jesus, who kills him.

This lesson covers a lengthy hadith from the Musnad of Ahmad that provides a vivid and detailed account of the Dajjal's emergence, his deceptive powers, and the decisive victory of Jesus. Understanding this narrative fortifies faith in the unseen and prepares believers to remain steadfast in the face of trials.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith on the Dajjal
Read the long hadith from Ahmad. Pay attention to the Dajjal's duration, physical description, and the writing on his forehead.
The hadith includes unusual time scales and detailed descriptions.
2
Identify the Dajjal's false miracles
Note the miracles he performs: commanding rain, reviving the dead, and his two rivers. Understand their deceptive nature.
3
Follow the believers' response
See how the people flee to the Mountain of Smoke and how Jesus descends to lead them.
4
Learn how the Dajjal is defeated
Observe that the Dajjal melts like salt when he sees Jesus, and Jesus kills him with the help of creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات

ما نزلت عاهة إلا بَرِئَ بِإِذْنِ اللهِ تعالى، وقيلَ: لأَنه مُمسوح بالبَرَكَةِ. وسُمّي عيسى مسيحا لمسحه الأرض، أي سياحته فيها، وقيل: لأنه ما مسح على

ثانيها: نُزول المسيح عيسى بنِ مَرْيَمَ عليه الصلاة والسلامُ مِنَ السماء، وقتله للدجال، ففي الصحيح (لينزلن) ابنُ مَرْيَمَ حكَمًا عدلًا فليكسرنَّ الصليب، وليقْتُلنَّ الخنزير، وليضَعَنَّ الجزية) الحديثُ.

وفي مُسندِ أحمدَ مِنْ حديث جابر: (يخرُجُ الدجّالُ في خفقة مِنَ الدين وإدبار منَ العِلم، وله أربعون ليلة يسيحُها في الأرضِ اليَومُ منها كالسَّنةِ، واليَومُ كالشهر، واليومُ منها كالجمعة، ثُمَّ سائرُ أَيَّامَه كأيَّامِكُم هذه، وله حمارٌ يركبه، عرْضُ جانب أذنيه أربعون ذراعًا، فيقول للناس: أنا ربُّكم، وهو أعورُ، وإِنَّ رَبَّكم لَيسَ بأَعُورَ، مكتوبٌ بَينَ عَيْنَيْه كافر، يقرؤه كُلّ مؤمن كاتب وغَيْرِ كاتب، يَرِدُ كُلَّ ماءٍ ومنهل إلا المدينة ومكةَ حرَّمهما الله عليه، وأقامت الملائكةُ بأبوابها، ومعَه جَبالٌ مِنْ خُبز، والناسُ في جَهدِ إلا مَنْ تبعه، ومعه نهران أنا أَعْلَمُ بهما منه، نهرٌ يقولُ الجنَّةُ ونهر يقولُ النار، فمَنْ أُدْخِلَ الذي يُسمّيه الجنّةَ فهو في النار، ومن أُدْخِلَ الذي يُسمّيهِ النار فهو في الجنة.

قال: وتُبْعَثُ معه شياطينُ تِلكم، ومعَه فتنةٌ عظيمةٌ، يَأمُرُ السماءَ تُمطِرُ فيمطر، ويقتُلُ نفْسًا ثُمَّ يُحييها فيما يرى الناسُ، فيقولُ للناس: أيها الناسُ فهل يفعَلُ مِثلَ هذا إلا الربُّ، فيفرُّ الناسُ إلى جبَلِ الدُّخانِ بالشام، فيأتيهم فيُحاصِرُهم، فيشتد حصارُهم ويُجهِدُهم جَهدًا شديدًا، ثُمَّ يَنزِلُ عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ فيأتي في السَّحَر فيقولُ: أَيُّها الناسُ ما يمْنعُكم أنْ تَخرُجوا إلى هذا الكذاب الخبيث، فينطلقون فإذا هم بعيسى فتقام الصلاةُ، فيُقالُ له: تقدَّم يا رُوحَ الله، فيقولُ: ليَتَقَدَّمْ إمامُكُم فليصل بكم، فإذا صلوا صلاةَ الصُّبْح خرجوا إليه، فحين يراه الكذاب فينماعُ -أي: يذوبُ - كما ينماعُ الملح في الماء، فيقتله حتى إنَّ الشجَرَ والحَجَرَ يُنادي يا روح الله هذا يهودي، فلا يترك ممن كان يتبَعُه أَحَدًا إلا قتَلَه. وفي الصحيح أحاديثُ بمعنى ذلك. انتهى، ذكره السيوطي.
The third section: matters heard from revelation. No ailment descended except it was cured by Allah's permission, and it was said: because he is anointed with blessing. And Jesus was called Messiah because he traversed the earth, meaning his journeying in it, and it was said: because he wiped over... Second matter: The descent of the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace and blessings be upon him, from heaven, and his killing of the Dajjal. In the Sahih: 'The son of Mary will surely descend as a just judge; he will break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya' the hadith. And in the Musnad of Ahmad from the hadith of Jabir: 'The Dajjal will emerge in a lapse of religion and a turning away from knowledge. He will have forty nights during which he will traverse the earth; one day will be like a year, one day like a month, one day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days. He will ride a donkey with a distance of forty cubits between its ears. He will say to the people: I am your Lord, and he is one-eyed, but your Lord is not one-eyed. Between his eyes it is written 'disbeliever', which every believer, literate or illiterate, will read. He will visit every watering place except Medina and Mecca, which Allah has forbidden to him, and the angels stand at their gates. He will have mountains of bread, while the people are in severe hunger except those who follow him. He will have two rivers—I know them better than he—one river appears as Paradise and one as Fire. Whoever enters what he calls Paradise will be in the Fire, and whoever enters what he calls Fire will be in Paradise. He will send with him devils of those times, and there will be a great trial. He will command the sky to rain and it will rain, and he will kill a soul and then revive it in the sight of the people. He will say to the people: O people, does anyone except the Lord do such things? Then the people will flee to the Mountain of Smoke in Syria. He will come to them and besiege them, and the siege will become severe and he will afflict them severely. Then Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, will descend and come at dawn, saying: O people, what prevents you from going out against this lying wicked one? They will set out and behold, they will be with Jesus. The prayer will be established, and it will be said to him: Step forward, O Spirit of Allah. He will say: Let your imam step forward and lead you in prayer. When they have prayed the morning prayer, they will go out to him. When the liar sees him, he will dissolve like salt dissolves in water, and he will kill him until the tree and the stone call out: O Spirit of Allah, this is a Jew. He will not leave anyone who followed him except he kills him. In the Sahih there are hadiths to that effect. End. Mentioned by Suyuti.

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the discussion on sam'iyyat (matters known from revelation) concerning the signs of the Hour. It begins with an explanation of why Jesus is called Masih, offering three reasons: because no ailment descended upon him except it was cured by Allah's permission (i.e., he healed by God's will), because he is anointed with blessing, and because he traveled the earth. Then it proceeds to the second sign: the descent of Jesus from heaven and his killing of the Dajjal. The author cites the Sahih hadith that Jesus will descend as a just judge, break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya. Then a lengthy hadith from Ahmad describes the Dajjal in detail: his emergence during a lapse of religion, his forty days of unusual length, his one-eyed appearance, the writing 'disbeliever' on his forehead, his false miracles including providing bread while causing hunger, his two rivers that appear as Paradise and Fire but are actually the opposite, his ability to command rain and revive a dead person. The people flee to the Mountain of Smoke. Jesus descends, refuses to lead the prayer deferring to the Muslim imam, then after prayer goes out to confront the Dajjal. The Dajjal melts like salt, and Jesus kills him, while trees and stones help identify Jews. The passage concludes with Suyuti's note that authentic hadith support this.

Key Terms
الدجال
المسيح
نزول عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Dajjal's miracles are genuine divine signs, indicating he is a true god or prophet.
Correction: The hadith clarifies that the Dajjal is a one-eyed liar; his rivers are illusions, his revival is only apparent, and he is ultimately defeated by the true Messiah, Jesus.

Checkpoint
What happens to the Dajjal when he sees Jesus?
A) He fights valiantly
B) He dissolves like salt in water
C) He repents and converts
D) He flees to the mountains

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is a one-eyed deceiver who performs false miracles, but Jesus will descend, kill him, and save the believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Dajjal were to appear today, would the writing 'kafir' on his forehead be clear to you? What is the state of your faith that would allow you to see it?
?
The Dajjal offers mountains of bread while people starve. What worldly temptations are you willing to reject for the sake of truth, even when they appear beneficial?
?
Jesus refuses to lead the prayer out of respect for the Muslim imam. How does your humility compare when given authority? Are you quick to put others before yourself?

The Third Major Sign: Gog and Magog
Dardeer explains the third sign: the emergence of Gog and Magog.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Gog and Magog are human tribes descended from Adam through Japheth, and that their emergence is a major sign after the Dajjal, as narrated in authentic hadith.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are human, not supernatural, and will appear after Dajjal.

In this lesson, we examine the third sam'iyyat sign: the emergence of Gog and Magog. Imam Dardeer clarifies their lineage as human tribes from the descendants of Adam, dispelling myths, and then presents a prophetic hadith describing the sequence of events after Jesus kills the Dajjal. This sign underscores the reality of eschatological events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the content.
Notice the linguistic note about the hamza in Ya'juj and Ma'juj.
2
Understand the lineage and linguistic note
Identify the two tribes as descendants of Japheth, and thus of Adam. Note that they are human, not supernatural.
This corrects a common misconception.
3
Analyze the hadith from Muslim
The hadith describes the revelation to Jesus after killing the Dajjal, commanding him to take believers to Mount Tur, and then the outpouring of Gog and Magog.
The word 'yansilun' means they come swiftly from every high place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثها: خروجُ يأجوج ومأجوج - بالهمز ودونَه-، وهما قبيلتانِ مِنْ وَلَدِ يافث ابنِ نُوحِ عليه السلام، فهُما مِنْ ذُرِّيةِ آدَمَ عليه السلام مِنْ غَيْرِ خِلافٍ.

روى مُسلِمٌ مِنْ حَدِيثِ النُّواس بن سَمْعَانَ: إِنَّ اللهَ تعالى يوحي إلى عيسى عليه السلام بعْدَ قتلِه الدجّالَ: أني قدْ أَخْرَجتُ عِبادا لي لا يَدان لأحَدٍ بقتالهم فحرِّزْ عِبادي إلى الطُّورِ. ويبعث الله يأجوج ومأجوج وهم مِنْ كُلِّ حَدَبٍ ينسِلون - أي: مِنْ كُلِّ نَشْرِ
Third matter: The emergence of Gog and Magog – with and without hamza – and they are two tribes from the offspring of Japheth son of Noah, peace be upon him, so they are from the descendants of Adam, peace be upon him, without dispute. Muslim narrated from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an: 'Indeed Allah, exalted, reveals to Jesus, peace be upon him, after he kills the Dajjal: I have brought forth servants of Mine that none can fight, so secure My servants to the mountain. And Allah will send Gog and Magog, and they will pour down from every elevated place – i.e., from every hill.'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage addresses the third matter of the sam'iyyat section: the emergence of Gog and Magog (Ya'juj and Ma'juj). The author notes that the name can be pronounced with or without hamza. He states that these are two tribes from the progeny of Yafith (Japheth), son of Noah, thus from the lineage of Adam – a point on which there is no disagreement. Then a hadith from Muslim is cited, where after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Allah reveals to him that He has brought forth a group of people whom no one can fight, so Jesus is commanded to take the believers to Mount Tur. Allah will send Gog and Magog, who will come quickly from every high place, pouring down swiftly. The explanation of 'yansilun' is given: they move rapidly. The passage ends abruptly here due to the page break, but the description continues in the subsequent text.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
يافث
نوح
الطور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Gog and Magog are supernatural creatures or not from the lineage of Adam.
Correction: The text explicitly states they are two human tribes from the offspring of Japheth, son of Noah, thus from Adam's descendants.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, from whom are Gog and Magog descended?
A) From Adam directly, not through Noah.
B) From Shem, son of Noah.
C) From Japheth, son of Noah.
D) From Ham, son of Noah.

Key Takeaway

Definition of Tasawwuf as Knowledge and Practice
Dardeer defines tasawwuf in two complementary ways: as a science and as a practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-fold definition of tasawwuf: as a science of principles and as a practice of precaution.

Core Idea
Tasawwuf is both knowledge and practice, rooted in shariah.

Imam Dardeer introduces the discipline of tasawwuf after creed, because spiritual journeying depends on correct belief. He then defines tasawwuf in two complementary ways: as a science and as a practice. This lesson unpacks that definition.

Guided Path
1
Place tasawwuf in context
Notice that Dardeer places tasawwuf after the study of creed. He says spiritual journey to Allah is not possible without correct belief. This shows the foundational role of aqidah.
Creed comes first, then spiritual practice.
2
Understand the definition as science
Read the definition of tasawwuf as a science: 'a science of principles by which the soundness of the heart and all the senses is known.' Ask yourself what kind of knowledge this is.
It is a practical science, not just theory.
3
Understand the definition as practice
Examine the practical definition: taking the most precautionary in commands, avoiding prohibitions, and limiting permissible things to necessities. This is the behavioral aspect.
Precaution is key.
4
Review other sayings
Dardeer mentions two other sayings: earnestness in journeying to God, and guarding the senses and observing breaths. Note that the meanings are close.
These reinforce the idea of vigilance.

The Interconnection of Shariah, Tariqah, and Haqiqah
Dardeer distinguishes shariah, tariqah, and haqiqah as three interconnected aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how shariah, tariqah, and haqiqah are interconnected aspects of Islamic practice, with haqiqah being the inner reality achieved through following the shariah and tariqah.

Core Idea
Shariah, tariqah, and haqiqah are three layers of one reality, not separate paths.

Dardeer clarifies three key spiritual terms often misunderstood as separate or contradictory. He shows that shariah provides the rulings, tariqah is the practice, and haqiqah is the inner knowledge that results from sincere practice. This lesson unpacks their sequential and complementary relationship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's definitions.
2
Identify the definitions of each term
Look for how Dardeer defines shariah, tariqah, and haqiqah. Note that tariqah is action, shariah is rulings, and haqiqah is the secrets and result.
Pay attention to the sequence: shariah → tariqah → haqiqah.
3
Reflect on the role of dhikr
Notice that Dardeer emphasizes abundant remembrance of 'La ilaha illa Allah' with proper etiquettes as the means to purify the heart and achieve haqiqah. Consider why etiquettes matter.
This connects practice (tariqah) to inner reality (haqiqah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن التصرف بمعنى العمل هو الطريقة، وأما الشريعة فهي الأحكام التي وردت عن الشارع المعبر عنها بالدين، وأما الحقيقة فهي أسرار الشريعة ونتيجة الطريقة، فهي علوم ومعارف تحصل لقلوب السالكين بعد صفائها من كدرات الطبائع البشرية. ولا شيء أقرب لصفاء القلب من كثرة ذكر «لا إله إلا الله» مع الآداب التي ذكرها أهل الله رضي الله عنه، ومتى ترك السالك الآداب أو أكثرها بعد عليه الوصول إلى مطلوبه.
And know that tasarruf (behavior) in the sense of action is the path (tariqah). As for the shariah, it is the rulings that came from the Lawgiver, expressed as religion. As for the haqiqah, it is the secrets of the shariah and the result of the tariqah, and it is knowledge and gnosis that occurs in the hearts of the wayfarers after their purification from the turbidity of human natures. And nothing is closer to the purification of the heart than abundant remembrance of 'there is no god but Allah' with the etiquettes mentioned by the people of Allah, may Allah be pleased with them. And whenever the wayfarer abandons the etiquettes or most of them, the attainment of his goal becomes distant.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage explains the relationship between shariah, tariqah, and haqiqah. Dardeer identifies tariqah as practice or action. Shariah is the revealed rulings that constitute the religion. Haqiqah is the inner secrets and ultimate realities that are the result of following the tariqah. These are spiritual knowledge and experiences that arise in the heart after it is purified from the turbidity of human nature. He then stresses that the most effective means of heart purification is frequent dhikr of 'La ilaha illa Allah' performed with the proper etiquettes as taught by the saints. Abandoning these etiquettes hinders the wayfarer from reaching his goal.

Correction: Dardeer presents them as sequential and complementary: haqiqah is the secret of shariah and the result of tariqah, not an alternative.

The Etiquettes of Dhikr: Classification and Pre-Dhikr Adab
Dardeer classifies dhikr etiquettes into three types and begins explaining the pre-dhikr type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of dhikr etiquettes and the specific preparatory practices required before engaging in dhikr.

Core Idea
Proper dhikr requires intentional preparation before it begins.

Imam Dardeer opens the discussion on adab al-dhikr by first giving a clear three-part classification: etiquettes that come before, during, and after the remembrance. He then begins detailing the pre-dhikr stage, outlining concrete actions that ready the heart and body for focused worship. This lesson covers the classification and the initial pre-dhikr requirements as far as the available text allows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

The passage is incomplete; it cuts off mid-sentence in the pre-dhikr section.

These categories set the structure for the entire discussion on dhikr adab.
3
List the pre-dhikr requirements

Preliminary Etiquettes of Dhikr
Dardeer lists the preparatory actions before beginning dhikr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four preparatory etiquettes that should be observed before beginning dhikr.

Core Idea
Proper dhikr begins with seeking forgiveness, sending blessings, facing qibla, and bringing your shaykh to mind.

Imam Dardeer outlines essential etiquettes that prepare the heart for the practice of dhikr. These actions are not merely optional additions but integral steps that align the seeker with the spiritual journey. In this lesson, we will explore each of these preparatory actions and understand their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Dardeer frames this as a conclusion on tasawwuf. The etiquettes are listed in a specific order.
Pay attention to the sequence: seeking forgiveness, then sending blessings, then facing qibla, then bringing shaykh.
2
Identify each etiquette
Extract each of the four actions mentioned. Make sure you can list them: 1) dhikr itself (implied), 2) seeking forgiveness, 3) sending blessings on the Prophet, 4) facing qibla, and 5) bringing shaykh to mind. Note that dhikr is the main act, but the others are precursors.
The passage says 'the dhikr, and that he seek forgiveness...' meaning the dhikr is the goal, and the etiquettes are before it.
3
Understand the reasons
The passage gives a reason only for facing the qibla: because it is the best direction. For the other etiquettes, consider why they are beneficial. The commentary helps explain.
4
Reflect on the role of the shaykh
Why is bringing the shaykh to mind important? The text says 'to be his companion'. Think about how spiritual guidance accompanies the seeker even in private practice.
This connects to the broader theme of reliance on a spiritual guide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة: في التصوف. الذكر، وأن يستغفر الله تعالى بما تيسر، بأي صيغة كانت، وأن يصلي على النبي في السير، ثم يشرع في الذكر. كذلك، وأن يستقبل القبلة؛ لأنها أفضل الجهات، وأن يستحضر شيخه ليكون رفيقه.
Conclusion: on Sufism. The dhikr, and that he seek forgiveness from Allah the Exalted with what is easy, in any formula, and that he send blessings upon the Prophet in the journey, then he begins the dhikr. Likewise, and that he face the qibla, because it is the best of directions, and that he bring to mind his shaykh to be his companion.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a list of preliminary etiquettes for dhikr (remembrance of Allah). The author, Imam Dardeer, begins by framing this as a conclusion on tasawwuf (Sufism). He then enumerates four preparatory actions: first, the dhikr itself is mentioned; second, one must seek forgiveness from Allah (istighfar) in any easy formula; third, send blessings upon the Prophet (salawat) while on the spiritual journey; fourth, begin the dhikr proper. Additionally, one should face the qibla because it is the most virtuous direction, and one should bring the shaykh (spiritual guide) to mind so that he may be a companion in the journey. These actions are meant to prepare the heart and align the seeker before engaging in the core practice of dhikr.

شيخ

Correction: Dardeer presents them as integral preparatory actions that should be observed before engaging in dhikr. They are not mere recommendations but essential etiquettes.

The Art of Stillness After Dhikr
Dardeer enumerates post-dhikr etiquettes and types of spiritual influxes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of post-dhikr stillness and how different spiritual influxes transform the practitioner.

Core Idea
Stillness after dhikr is the womb where spiritual influxes are born.

After the intensity of dhikr, the seeker is not to immediately rush into worldly affairs. Instead, there is a sacred pause—a stillness that allows the spiritual influxes (wāridāt) to settle into the heart. This lesson from Imam Dardeer explains the etiquettes of that pause and how different influxes reshape the believer's inner state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the words of Imam Dardeer and Imam al-Ghazali sink in.
Notice the shift from the rule to examples to additional etiquettes.
2
Understand why stillness is necessary
The passage states that dhikr produces influxes that cannot establish themselves in the heart without stillness. Reflect on this cause-and-effect relationship.
Stillness here is not passive but a disciplined openness.
3
Explore the three influx examples
Identify the influxes of zuhd, tawakkul, and sabr. For each, note the effect on the practitioner’s heart and behavior.
The pattern 'when the influx is X, the person becomes Y' shows the transformative power.
4
Study Ghazali's four etiquettes
Imam al-Ghazali adds four inner and outer disciplines for the silence. List them and consider how they deepen the stillness.
These etiquettes turn silence into active worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الآداب البعدية: فإنه يسكت ويسكن بخشوع، فإن للذكر واردات ترد على قلب الذاكر، ولا يتمكن الوارد من القلب إلا بذلك، فإذا كان الوارد وارد زهد وجب التمهل حتى يتم ويتمكن من القلب، فتستوي عنده الدنيا، أقبلت أم أدبرت، وإذا كان وارد توكل صار بعد ذلك مفوضا أمره إلى ربه في كل شيء، وإذا كان وارد صبر صار بعد ذلك لا ينزعج من تفاقم الأهوال، وهكذا من الواردات. قال الإمام الغزالي رض الله عنه: ولهذه السكتة آداب: مراقبة الله تعالى، وإجراء معنى الذكر على قلبه، ونفي الخواطر كلها، وجمع حواسه كلها بحيث لا تتحرك منه شعرة.
As for the post-dhikr etiquettes: then he falls silent and becomes still with humility, for dhikr has spiritual influxes that descend upon the heart of the rememberer, and the influx does not become established in the heart except by that. So if the influx is one of zuhd (asceticism), he must pause so that it is completed and becomes established in the heart, then the world becomes equal in his sight, whether it approaches or turns away. And if the influx is one of tawakkul (reliance), he becomes after that one who entrusts his affairs to his Lord in everything. And if the influx is one of sabr (patience), he becomes after that not disturbed by the aggravation of terrors. And so on from the influxes. Imam al-Ghazali, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'For this silence there are etiquettes: observing Allah the Exalted, running the meaning of dhikr upon his heart, negating all thoughts, and gathering all his senses such that not a hair of him moves.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage discusses the etiquettes to be observed after completing dhikr. The author emphasizes that after dhikr, one must fall silent and remain still with humility (khushūʿ). This stillness is crucial because dhikr generates spiritual influxes (wāridāt) that descend upon the heart. These influxes can only take root in the heart if the practitioner remains silent and composed. The author then illustrates three types of spiritual influxes and their effects: 1) The influx of zuhd (asceticism): when this descends, the person must wait patiently until it fully settles. As a result, the world becomes equal in his eyes—whether it comes or goes—indicating detachment. 2) The influx of tawakkul (reliance): after this, the person entrusts all affairs to Allah. 3) The influx of sabr (patience): after experiencing this, the person is no longer disturbed by severe hardships. The category continues similarly for other influxes. The author then quotes Imam al-Ghazali, who specifies further etiquettes for this post-dhikr silence: watching over Allah’s presence, keeping the meaning of dhikr running in the heart, negating all distracting thoughts, and collecting all one’s senses so that even a hair does not move. This stillness is not passive but active preparation for receiving divine favors.

واردات

زهد
توكل
صبر
مراقبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The stillness after dhikr is simply resting or doing nothing.
Correction: It is an active posture of spiritual receptivity, requiring discipline of the heart and senses as outlined by Imam al-Ghazali.

Checkpoint
What does the influx of tawakkul (reliance) produce in the practitioner?
A) Equality of worldly matters
B) Entrusting all affairs to Allah
C) Patience in hardship
D) Negation of thoughts

Key Takeaway
Post-dhikr stillness is essential for spiritual influx to take root, transforming the practitioner's relationship with the world and with Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After you finish your daily dhikr, do you immediately get up or do you sit still with humility? What distracts you from being present in that moment? Will you commit to practicing these four etiquettes of stillness starting tomorrow?
?
Of the three spiritual influxes mentioned—zuhd, tawakkul, sabr—which one do you feel you need most in your life right now? Are you willing to pause and remain still after dhikr to allow that influx to take root?
?
Al-Ghazali says to gather your senses so that 'not a hair of you moves.' In your last prayer or dhikr, was even a single part of you restless? How can you train yourself to be physically and mentally still for the sake of receiving from Allah?

The Fruit of Dhikr: Understanding the Spiritual Ranks
Dardeer defines spiritual ranks and describes the lowest rank of self-reproach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of spiritual ranks (rutab) in Islam, the lowest rank of self-reproach, and how consistent dhikr elevates the believer through these ranks.

Core Idea
Persistence in dhikr lifts you from blaming yourself to the highest divine stations.

This passage reveals the immediate fruit of consistent dhikr: a journey upward through spiritual ranks. Dardeer defines what a 'rank' is and identifies the lowest Islamic rank—self-reproach—as the starting point. Understanding this foundation prepares you to appreciate the ultimate goal, the rank of siddiqiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the fruit of dhikr
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Dardeer calls this the 'fruit' (thamara) of dhikr.
The passage starts with 'ثمرة' and includes a grammatical note about the alif in 'ترقى'.
2
Understand the definition of 'rank' (rutba)
Dardeer defines 'rank' as a good praiseworthy trait with a commendable end. This is important because it shows that spiritual progress is about character transformation.
The term 'رتبة' is explained as الخليقة الحسنة المحمودة عاقبتها.
3
Identify the lowest Islamic rank
The lowest rank is 'blaming the soul' (lawm al-nafs) for sins. This is the first step of ascent—being aware of one's shortcomings.
This rank is a form of self-accountability and repentance.
4
Reflect on the upward journey
Consider that the fruit of dhikr is not just a feeling but a real elevation through ranks. The path starts with self-reproach and leads higher.
The rest of the passage will describe the highest rank, siddiqiyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمرة. فإن داومت على الذكر بهذه الآداب ترقى أي تصعد - وإثبات الألف ضرورة المداومة على حد: «ولا ترضاها ولا تلقي» - (بهذا الذكر) المشتمل على الآداب، أي: بسببه، (أعلى الرتب) جمع «رتبة»، وهي: الخليقة الحسنة المحمودة عاقبتها. وأدنى الرتب الإسلامية لوم النفس على ما صدر منها من المخالفات، وأعلاها رتبة الصديقية ينالها العبد بعد دخوله في مقام الإحسان، وهو أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه. ورتبة الصديقية في نفسها مراتب متفاوتة، بعضها أعلى من بعض، وأعلاها رتبة أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه، ولا يعلو مقام الصديقية إلا مقام النبوة، فصاحب مقام الصديقية لو تخطى مقامه لنزل في مقام النبوة، إلا أن النبوة قد ختمت بنبينا محمد، والصديقية لم تختم. فمقام الصديقية مقام الولاية الكبرى والخلافة العظمى. وهذا المقام تترادف فيه الفتوحات، وتعظم التجليات، وتتم المشاهدات.
Fruit. If you persist in dhikr with these etiquettes, you will ascend (tarqā i.e. rise—and the alif is necessary due to persistence, on the model of 'wa lā tarḍāhā wa lā talqī')—by this dhikr that encompasses the etiquettes, i.e. because of it, (to the highest of ranks), plural of 'rutba', which is the good praiseworthy trait whose end is commendable. The lowest of the Islamic ranks is blaming the soul for the acts of disobedience that emanated from it, and its highest is the rank of siddiqiyyah (truthfulness), which the servant attains after entering the station of iḥsān, which is to worship Allah as if you see Him. The rank of siddiqiyyah itself has varying levels, some higher than others, and its highest is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. No station surpasses the station of siddiqiyyah except the station of prophethood. So the possessor of the station of siddiqiyyah, were he to transcend his station, would descend into the station of prophethood, except that prophethood has been sealed with our Prophet Muhammad, while siddiqiyyah has not been sealed. So the station of siddiqiyyah is the station of the greater walāyah (sainthood) and the supreme khilāfah (vicegerency). In this station, divine openings are successive, theophanies are magnified, and spiritual witnesses are perfected.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is the final fruit (thamara) of the discussion on dhikr. It explains the spiritual results of persisting in dhikr with the accompanying etiquettes. The author states that such persistence causes the practitioner to ascend (tarqā) to the highest ranks (aʿlā al-rutab). He clarifies that 'rutba' means a praiseworthy trait with a commendable outcome. He then describes the lowest Islamic rank: self-reproach (lawm al-nafs) for sins. The highest rank is that of siddiqiyyah (truthfulness), attained after entering the station of iḥsān (worshipping Allah as if seeing Him). Notably, the rank of siddiqiyyah itself has internal gradations, with Abu Bakr al-Siddiq occupying its zenith. The author then makes an important theological point: only prophethood (nubuwwa) is above siddiqiyyah. If a person at the siddiqiyyah rank were to transcend it, he would have to descend into prophethood—but prophethood is sealed with Muhammad (ﷺ), while siddiqiyyah remains open. Consequently, siddiqiyyah is the station of the greater wilayah (sainthood) and the supreme khilafah (vicegerency). In this station, divine openings (futūḥāt) come successively, theophanies (tajalliyāt) are magnified, and spiritual witnesses (mushāhadāt) are perfected. This passage underscores that the ultimate spiritual goal attainable after the Prophet's seal is the rank of siddiqiyyah, which is the pinnacle of sainthood.

Key Terms
رتبة
لوم النفس
إحسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, what is the lowest Islamic rank?
A) Siddiqiyyah
B) Ihsan
C) Blaming the soul for sins
D) Successive divine openings

Key Takeaway
Persistent dhikr with etiquettes initiates a spiritual ascent that begins with self-reproach, the lowest rank, understood as a praiseworthy trait.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you catch yourself committing a sin, do you quickly move on, or do you truly blame yourself and use that feeling to persist in dhikr? What would change if you treated that self-reproach as a blessed starting point rather than a burden?
?
This lesson says the lowest Islamic rank is blaming yourself for wrongdoings. Have you ever considered that your guilt could be the first rung on a ladder to the highest station? If you actually believed that, how would you respond the next time you slip?
?
You have been given a definition: a spiritual rank is a praiseworthy character trait with a good outcome. What trait are you building right now through your daily habits? Is it truly moving you upward, or are you stuck in a lower state without even realizing it? Commit today to one small act of dhikr that turns your self-reproach into ascent.

The Highest Rank: Siddiqiyyah and Its Sublime Station
Dardeer describes the rank of siddiqiyyah, its attainment, levels, relation to prophethood, and its spiritual characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rank of siddiqiyyah—its attainment after ihsan, its internal gradations, its relation to prophethood, and its characteristics as the greater wilayah and supreme khilafah.

Core Idea
Siddiqiyyah is the highest open rank, below only the sealed prophethood, and has levels culminating in Abu Bakr.

Having described the lowest rank, Dardeer now unveils the pinnacle: the rank of siddiqiyyah (truthfulness). This station is attained after entering the level of ihsan (worshipping Allah as if seeing Him). The passage explains that siddiqiyyah itself has many levels, with Abu Bakr at the summit, and that only prophethood is above it—but prophethood is sealed, leaving siddiqiyyah as the ultimate open rank. Dardeer concludes by describing the extraordinary spiritual experiences in this station.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on siddiqiyyah
Read the Arabic source and its translation carefully. This passage describes the highest rank and its properties.
The passage begins with 'وأعلاها رتبة الصديقية'.
2
Understand how siddiqiyyah is attained
The passage states it is attained after entering the station of ihsan, which is defined as worshipping Allah as if you see Him.
Ihsan is a key concept connecting faith and spiritual excellence.
3
Note the internal gradations of siddiqiyyah
Siddiqiyyah is not a single rank but a category with varying levels, the highest being that of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.
This shows that even within the highest rank, there is room for further ascent.
4
Compare siddiqiyyah with prophethood
Only prophethood is above siddiqiyyah, but it is sealed with Muhammad (PBUH). Therefore, siddiqiyyah remains open as the highest attainable rank.
This is a key theological point distinguishing the end of prophethood from the continuation of sainthood.
5
Reflect on the characteristics of this station
The station of siddiqiyyah is described as the greater wilayah and supreme khilafah, where divine openings are successive, theophanies magnified, and spiritual witnesses perfected.
These are the fruits of reaching this station.

In this station, divine openings are successive, theophanies are magnified, and spiritual witnesses are perfected.

Commentary

The Etiquette of Dhikr: Holding the Breath and Avoiding Water
Simile and practical guidelines for dhikr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific physical etiquettes of dhikr as taught by Imam Dardir, including the cat simile, breath control, and abstention from water.

Core Idea
Spiritual dhikr requires disciplined physical posture like a cat stalking its prey.

This passage opens with a vivid simile: the state of a cat catching a mouse. It then prescribes concrete physical actions for dhikr: concealing the breath, repeating the invocation multiple times, and refraining from water. These etiquettes are not arbitrary; they maximize the spiritual influx that dhikr generates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about dhikr etiquette
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the cat simile and the three instructions that follow.
The cat's focus and subtlety are key.
2
Reflect on the cat simile
Why compare dhikr to a cat catching a mouse? Consider the qualities of alertness, patience, and silent movement.
3
Analyze the three instructions
Identify the three commands: conceal breath, repeat 3-7 times, avoid water immediately after. Understand the purpose of each.
4
Connect to spiritual outcome
The passage implies that these etiquettes ensure the spiritual light (al-warid) circulates in the body and is not extinguished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمرة
شرح الخريدة البهية - كحال الهرة عِندَ اصطيادِ الفأرة وأنْ يكتُمَ نفَسَه بِقَدْرِ الطاقةِ مِرارًا، أقلها ثلاثةُ إلى سبعة، حتى يدور الوارد في جميع أركانه، وأن لا يبادِرَ بِشُرِبِ الماءِ عَقِبَ الذِّكْرِ، فإنه يُطفئ ما تحصَّلَ مِنْ أنواره.
فإِنْ داوَمتَ على الذكر بهذه الآداب (ترقى) أي: تصعد - وإثباتُ الألف ضرورةٌ المداومة على حد: «ولا ترضاها ولا تلقي - (بهذا الذكر) المشتمل على الآداب، أي: بسببه، (أعلى الرُّتَبِ) جمع «رتبة»، وهي: الخليقة الحسَنةُ المحمودة عاقبتها.
وأدنى الرتب الإسلاميةِ لَومُ النفْسِ على ما صدَرَ منها مِنَ المخالفات، وأعلاها رُتبةُ الصِّدِّيقية ينالها العبد بعد دخوله في مقام الإحسان، وهو أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه. ورتبةُ الصدّيقية في نفْسِها مراتب متفاوتة، بعضُها أعلى مِنْ بَعْضٍ، وأعلاها رُتبةُ أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه ، ولا يعلو مَقامَ الصدّيقيةِ إِلا مَقامُ النُّبوّة، فصاحب مقام الصِّدِّيقية لو تخطّى مَقامَه لَنَزَلَ في مَقام النُّبوّة، إلا أنَّ النُّبوَّةَ قد خُتمتْ بنَبيِّنا مُحمَّد ، والصدّيقية لم تُختَمْ. فَمَقامُ الصِّدِّيقيَّةِ مَقامُ الوِلايةِ الكُبرى والخِلافةِ العُظمى.
Fruit. Explanation of the Luminous Pearl - Like the state of the cat when catching the mouse, and that he conceal his breath as much as possible repeatedly, at least three to seven times, until the incoming (divine influx) circulates in all his limbs, and that he refrain from drinking water immediately after the dhikr, for it extinguishes what he has obtained of its lights. So if you persevere in dhikr with these manners, you will ascend—and making the alif is necessary for perseverance, according to the verse: 'And do not be pleased with it nor throw it away'—(by this dhikr) which includes the manners, that is, because of it, (the highest ranks) plural of 'rutha', which is the good nature praised in its outcome. And the lowest of the Islamic ranks is blaming the soul for its acts of disobedience, and its highest is the rank of siddiqiyya, which the servant attains after entering the station of ihsan, which is to worship Allah as if you see Him. And the rank of siddiqiyya in itself has varying levels, some higher than others, and its highest is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him). And no rank surpasses the rank of siddiqiyya except the rank of prophethood. So the possessor of the rank of siddiqiyya, if he were to exceed his rank, he would descend into the rank of prophethood, except that prophethood has been sealed with our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), while siddiqiyya has not been sealed. So the rank of siddiqiyya is the rank of the greater wilayah and the supreme khilafa.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage begins by describing the etiquette of dhikr with a simile: like a cat catching a mouse, one should hold their breath and repeat the dhikr three to seven times until its effect permeates all limbs. Then it advises against drinking water immediately after dhikr, as it extinguishes the lights acquired. It then explains that if one persists in dhikr with these manners, one ascends (tarqa) to the highest ranks. The passage then defines 'rutha' as a good nature with a praiseworthy outcome. It outlines the ranks: the lowest Islamic rank is self-reproach for sins, and the highest is the rank of siddiqiyya, attained after entering the station of ihsan (worship as if seeing Allah). It notes that within siddiqiyya there are degrees, the highest being that of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. Only prophethood is above siddiqiyya, and prophethood has been sealed with Muhammad (peace be upon him), while siddiqiyya remains open. Thus the rank of siddiqiyya is the greatest wilayah and supreme khilafa.

Key Terms
ذكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Drinking water after dhikr is a harmless act.
Correction: The passage teaches that water extinguishes the spiritual lights obtained through dhikr, so it should be avoided immediately after.

Checkpoint
How many times should one repeat the dhikr according to this passage?
A) At least once
B) At least three to seven times
C) Exactly seven times
D) As many times as possible

Key Takeaway
The physical etiquettes of dhikr are vital for preserving its spiritual fruits: conceal breath, repeat, and delay water.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in dhikr, do you treat it as a casual activity or as a focused spiritual exercise? What would change if you held your breath and concentrated like a cat stalking its prey? Are you willing to adopt that posture starting today?
?

?
The dhakir is instructed to repeat the dhikr until the divine influx circulates in all limbs. Is your dhikr only on your tongue, or does it transform your actions? What one limb can you consciously engage in your next dhikr session?

The Ranks of Spiritual Ascension: From Self-Reproach to Siddiqiyya
Defines spiritual ranks and explains the supreme rank of siddiqiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ladder of Islamic spiritual ranks, from the lowest (blaming the soul) to the highest attainable after prophethood (siddiqiyya), and its relation to ihsan.

Core Idea
Siddiqiyya is the supreme rank open to believers after the seal of prophethood.

Having described the etiquette of dhikr, Imam Dardir now explains the result: ascension through spiritual ranks. He defines what a 'rank' is, then describes the lowest Islamic rank (self-reproach) and the highest (siddiqiyya), which is attained through ihsan. He further explains that siddiqiyya has internal degrees, topped by Abu Bakr, and is only surpassed by prophethood—which is sealed. Thus siddiqiyya is the greatest station of sainthood and vicegerency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on ranks
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the definition of 'rutha' and the progression from Islamic to siddiqiyya.
Note the key terms: رتبة, صدّيقية, إحسان.
2
Understand the two ends of the ladder
Identify the lowest rank (blaming the soul) and the highest rank (siddiqiyya). Ask: what is the middle?
3
Learn about ihsan as the gateway
Siddiqiyya is attained after entering the station of ihsan (worship as if seeing Allah). Ponder the connection.
4
Compare siddiqiyya with prophethood
Only prophethood is higher, but it is sealed. Siddiqiyya remains open. This makes it the highest attainable rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمرة
شرح الخريدة البهية - كحال الهرة عِندَ اصطيادِ الفأرة وأنْ يكتُمَ نفَسَه بِقَدْرِ الطاقةِ مِرارًا، أقلها ثلاثةُ إلى سبعة، حتى يدور الوارد في جميع أركانه، وأن لا يبادِرَ بِشُرِبِ الماءِ عَقِبَ الذِّكْرِ، فإنه يُطفئ ما تحصَّلَ مِنْ أنواره.
فإِنْ داوَمتَ على الذكر بهذه الآداب (ترقى) أي: تصعد - وإثباتُ الألف ضرورةٌ المداومة على حد: «ولا ترضاها ولا تلقي - (بهذا الذكر) المشتمل على الآداب، أي: بسببه، (أعلى الرُّتَبِ) جمع «رتبة»، وهي: الخليقة الحسَنةُ المحمودة عاقبتها.
وأدنى الرتب الإسلاميةِ لَومُ النفْسِ على ما صدَرَ منها مِنَ المخالفات، وأعلاها رُتبةُ الصِّدِّيقية ينالها العبد بعد دخوله في مقام الإحسان، وهو أن تعبد الله كأنك تراه. ورتبةُ الصدّيقية في نفْسِها مراتب متفاوتة، بعضُها أعلى مِنْ بَعْضٍ، وأعلاها رُتبةُ أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه ، ولا يعلو مَقامَ الصدّيقيةِ إِلا مَقامُ النُّبوّة، فصاحب مقام الصِّدِّيقية لو تخطّى مَقامَه لَنَزَلَ في مَقام النُّبوّة، إلا أنَّ النُّبوَّةَ قد خُتمتْ بنَبيِّنا مُحمَّد ، والصدّيقية لم تُختَمْ. فَمَقامُ الصِّدِّيقيَّةِ مَقامُ الوِلايةِ الكُبرى والخِلافةِ العُظمى.
Fruit. Explanation of the Luminous Pearl - Like the state of the cat when catching the mouse, and that he conceal his breath as much as possible repeatedly, at least three to seven times, until the incoming (divine influx) circulates in all his limbs, and that he refrain from drinking water immediately after the dhikr, for it extinguishes what he has obtained of its lights. So if you persevere in dhikr with these manners, you will ascend—and making the alif is necessary for perseverance, according to the verse: 'And do not be pleased with it nor throw it away'—(by this dhikr) which includes the manners, that is, because of it, (the highest ranks) plural of 'rutha', which is the good nature praised in its outcome. And the lowest of the Islamic ranks is blaming the soul for its acts of disobedience, and its highest is the rank of siddiqiyya, which the servant attains after entering the station of ihsan, which is to worship Allah as if you see Him. And the rank of siddiqiyya in itself has varying levels, some higher than others, and its highest is the rank of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him). And no rank surpasses the rank of siddiqiyya except the rank of prophethood. So the possessor of the rank of siddiqiyya, if he were to exceed his rank, he would descend into the rank of prophethood, except that prophethood has been sealed with our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), while siddiqiyya has not been sealed. So the rank of siddiqiyya is the rank of the greater wilayah and the supreme khilafa.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage begins by describing the etiquette of dhikr with a simile: like a cat catching a mouse, one should hold their breath and repeat the dhikr three to seven times until its effect permeates all limbs. Then it advises against drinking water immediately after dhikr, as it extinguishes the lights acquired. It then explains that if one persists in dhikr with these manners, one ascends (tarqa) to the highest ranks. The passage then defines 'rutha' as a good nature with a praiseworthy outcome. It outlines the ranks: the lowest Islamic rank is self-reproach for sins, and the highest is the rank of siddiqiyya, attained after entering the station of ihsan (worship as if seeing Allah). It notes that within siddiqiyya there are degrees, the highest being that of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. Only prophethood is above siddiqiyya, and prophethood has been sealed with Muhammad (peace be upon him), while siddiqiyya remains open. Thus the rank of siddiqiyya is the greatest wilayah and supreme khilafa.

Key Terms
رتبة
صدّيقية
إحسان
ولاية
خلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Siddiqiyya is a single, fixed rank equal to prophethood.
Correction: Siddiqiyya has multiple degrees, is below prophethood, and is still attainable after the seal.

Checkpoint

A) Ihsan
B) Siddiqiyya
C) Prophethood

Key Takeaway
Siddiqiyya is the highest attainable spiritual rank after the seal of prophethood, and it is the station of supreme sainthood and vicegerency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the lowest Islamic rank is simply blaming yourself for disobedience. Are you even at that rank, or do you feel no remorse when you sin? What would it take for you to honestly reproach your own soul tonight?
?
The highest rank open to you is siddiqiyya, which requires worshipping Allah as if you see Him. When was the last time you prayed with that awareness? If you cannot imagine it, what is standing in the way?
?
Siddiqiyya is the rank of Abu Bakr, but it remains open. If you were to die tonight, would you be closer to the low rank of self-reproach (if that) or to the rank of the truthful? And what are you willing to change to ascend?

The Station of Siddiqiyya: Divine Openings and Perfections
Describes the characteristics and cause of the siddiqiyya station.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the defining features of the station of siddiqiyya: successive divine openings, magnified epiphanies, and completed visions and unveilings, and how these flow from the soul's perfection.

Core Idea
The station of siddiqiyya is marked by unceasing divine openings and perfected soul-attributes.

This lesson introduces the sublime station of siddiqiyya, a rank of profound spiritual realization. The text describes it as a state where divine openings multiply, tajalliyat become immense, and witnessing and unveilings are completed. All of this arises from the perfection and goodness of the soul's attributes. Let's explore these features together.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the station
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice the flow: first the characteristics, then the cause.
The passage uses a semi-colon to link the effects to their cause.
2
Identify the three features of the station
Find the three key terms: successive openings (futuhat), magnification of tajalliyat, and completion of musha hadat and kushufat. Understand each one.
These are the experiential signs of the station.
3
Understand the cause: soul's perfection
The passage explicitly connects these features to the soul's perfection (kamal al-nafs) and goodness of its attributes. Reflect on why this is the source.
This shows the station is a result of inner purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا المقامُ تتَرادَفُ فيه الفتوحات، وتعظُم التجلياتُ، وتتم المشاهدات والكشوفات؛ لكَمالِ النَّفْسِ وحُسْنِ صفاتها، ولا يُمكِنُ الوصول إليه إِلا بَعْدَ الفَناءِ، وهو زَوالُ صِفاتِ النفْس المذمومة بالكلّيّة، حتى لا تصيرَ مُلْتَفِتةٌ إلى شَيءٍ منها بلْ تَزَهَدُها كما تَزْهَدُ أَكُلَ الجيفة مَثَلًا.
And this station is characterized by successive openings, the magnification of epiphanies (tajalliyat), the completion of visions (mushahadat) and unveilings (kushufat); due to the perfection of the soul and the goodness of its attributes. And it is not possible to arrive at it except after annihilation (fana'), which is the complete removal of the blameworthy attributes of the soul, until it is no longer attracted to any of them, but rather shuns them just as one would shun carrion.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage describes the station of siddiqiyya, saying that it is characterized by repeated divine openings (futuhat), great tajalliyat (self-disclosures of the Divine), and the completion of mushahadat (spiritual witnessing) and kushufat (unveilings). All this is due to the perfection of the soul and its good attributes. However, one cannot reach this station without first undergoing fana, which is the complete removal of all blameworthy attributes of the soul, meaning the soul becomes completely disinterested in them and rejects them much like one would reject carrion.

The Necessity of Fana: Annihilating Blameworthy Attributes
States the necessity of fana and defines it as complete removal of blameworthy attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what fana means in the context of the siddiqiyya station: the complete removal of blameworthy soul-attributes such that the soul shuns them completely.

Core Idea
Fana is the complete removal of blameworthy soul-attributes, not of existence itself.

This lesson focuses on the essential precondition for reaching the station of siddiqiyya: annihilation (fana). The text defines fana as the complete removal of blameworthy attributes of the soul, to the point where the soul no longer inclines toward them but rejects them like carrion. Let's unpack this crucial teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on fana
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the strong negation: 'not possible except after fana.'
Fana is presented as an absolute precondition.
2
Understand the definition of fana
Fana is defined as the complete removal (zawal) of blameworthy soul-attributes. It is not the destruction of the soul itself.
Blameworthy attributes include pride, envy, greed, etc.
3
Grasp the effect of fana on the soul
After fana, the soul is no longer attracted to any blameworthy trait; it shuns them with disgust, like one shuns carrion.
This is a total transformation of inclinations.

Source Text

And it is not possible to arrive at it except after annihilation (fana'), which is the complete removal of the blameworthy attributes of the soul, until it is no longer attracted to any of them, but rather shuns them just as one would shun carrion.

Correction: The passage clearly defines fana as the complete removal of blameworthy attributes of the soul, not the soul itself. The soul continues to exist but with purified traits.

The Blameworthy Attributes of the Soul
Enumerates blameworthy soul-attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the blameworthy attributes of the soul that a seeker must strive to eliminate.

Core Idea
Blameworthy attributes are inner obstacles that must be removed for spiritual purification.

In this passage, Imam Dardier enumerates the vices of the soul that block closeness to Allah. These attributes are not just external actions but ingrained traits. Understanding them is the first step toward transformation.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of blameworthy attributes
The passage lists multiple attributes. Read each one carefully and consider its meaning.
2
Reflect on the harm of each attribute
Think about how each attribute corrupts the soul and distances from Allah.
The list includes envy, pride, hypocrisy, etc.
3
Recognize that these must be annihilated
The context of spiritual wayfaring (fana) requires removing these negative traits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفاتها المذمومة هي:
الحسد والحقد، وحبُّ الجاه والصيت والمحمَدة والرئاسة والشهوات، والكبر، والرياءُ ، والعُجْبُ، والنفاق، والغُرورُ، وَيُعْضُ أَحَدَ منَ الخَلْقِ لغَيرِ غرَض شَرعي، ونحو ذلك. فإذا زالت عنه هذه الأوصافُ القبيحةُ أَنصَفَ بأضدادها مِنَ الصفات الحميدة، كالشفقة والرأفة على الخَلْقِ، حتى يُحِبَّ لغَيْرِه ما يُحِبُّ لنفسه، والإخلاص، وحُسْن الخلق، والسّخاءِ، والمسكنة التي طلبها النبيُّ بقوله: (اللهم أحيني مِسْكينًا، وأمتني مسكينًا، واحشرني في زمرة المساكين).
And its blameworthy attributes are: envy and rancor, love of status, reputation, praise, leadership, and desires, and pride, and ostentation, and vanity, and hypocrisy, and delusion, and harming someone from creation without a legal purpose, and the like. So when these ugly attributes depart from him, he is invested with their opposites of praiseworthy attributes, such as compassion and mercy towards creation, so that he loves for others what he loves for himself, and sincerity, and good character, and generosity, and lowliness (miskina) which the Prophet (peace be upon him) sought in his words: 'O Allah, give me life as a miskeen, cause me to die as a miskeen, and raise me in the company of the miskeen.'
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage enumerates the blameworthy attributes of the soul (al-nafs) that must be annihilated through fana. They include envy (hasad), rancor (hiqd), love of status, reputation, praise, leadership, and worldly desires, pride, hypocrisy, delusion, and causing harm to others without a legitimate reason. Once these ugly traits are removed, they are replaced by their opposites: compassion, mercy, loving for others what one loves for oneself, sincerity, good character, generosity, and the quality of being a miskeen (humble lowliness), which is demonstrated by the Prophet's hadith asking Allah to let him live and die as a miskeen. This serves as a model for the seeker to adopt these praiseworthy traits.

Key Terms

كبر
رياء
عجب
نفاق
غرور

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Generosity
D) Pride (kibr)

Key Takeaway
The blameworthy attributes are the inner diseases that must be removed for spiritual progress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage includes 'harming someone without a legal purpose.' Reflect on your daily interactions: Do you cause harm, even unintentionally, for reasons that are not legitimate? What can you change starting tomorrow?

The Praiseworthy Attributes and the Model of Miskin
Lists praiseworthy attributes and the hadith on miskeen.

Core Idea
Praiseworthy attributes are fruits of purification, with humility (miskina) as the highest ideal.

After listing the vices, Imam Dardier explains that once they are removed, the soul is adorned with virtuous traits. Among these is the special quality of miskina, which the Prophet himself asked for.

The Prophet asked to die as a miskeen—humble and lowly. Are you willing to give up your reputation and status for the sake of Allah? What is one thing you cling to for pride that you need to let go?
?
Which of the ugly attributes—pride, selfishness, harshness—still dwells in you? What is its opposite praiseworthy attribute, and how will you actively cultivate it starting this hour?

Fana: Blameworthy Traits of the Soul
Defines fana and enumerates blameworthy soul traits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that fana (annihilation) is the total removal of blameworthy attributes of the soul, and you will be able to list those attributes and their opposites.

Core Idea
Fana is not self-destruction, but purification from blameworthy traits.

This passage presents a core concept in Islamic spirituality: fana. Before diving into the source, note that fana is often misunderstood. The author carefully defines it and then lists the specific traits that must be removed. As you read, focus on the transition from blameworthy to praiseworthy qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of fana
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify how the author defines fana—notice the phrase 'total removal' and the disgust analogy.
The author uses the example of being disgusted by a carcass to illustrate the soul's attitude toward blameworthy traits after fana.
2
Identify the blameworthy traits
Scan the list of blameworthy attributes. Count them and notice their variety from internal vices (envy, pride) to social ones (hypocrisy, love of status).
There is also an unclear word 'يُعْضُ' which may mean 'biting' or 'harming'—our commentary will address it.
3
See the transformation to praiseworthy traits
After the list, the author describes how the soul becomes adorned with opposite praiseworthy attributes. Find the hadith about humility (maskanah) and reflect on its connection.
The hadith 'O Allah, cause me to live as a poor person...' emphasizes the virtue of humility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة في التصوف والكشوفات)؛ لكَمالِ النَّفْسِ وحُسْنِ صفاتها، ولا يُمكِنُ الوصول إليه إِلا بَعْدَ الفَناءِ، وهو زَوالُ صِفاتِ النفْس المذمومة بالكلّيّة، حتى لا تصيرَ مُلْتَفِتةٌ إلى شَيءٍ منها بلْ تَزَهَدُها كما تَزْهَدُ أَكُلَ الجيفة مَثَلًا. وصفاتها المذمومة هي: الحسد والحقد (٢)، وحبُّ الجاه والصيت والمحمَدة والرئاسة والشهوات، والكبر، والرياءُ ، والعُجْبُ، والنفاق، والغُرورُ، وَيُعْضُ أَحَدَ منَ الخَلْقِ لغَيرِ غرَض شَرعي، ونحو ذلك. فإذا زالت عنه هذه الأوصافُ القبيحةُ أَنصَفَ بأضدادها مِنَ الصفات الحميدة، كالشفقة والرأفة على الخَلْقِ، حتى يُحِبَّ لغَيْرِه ما يُحِبُّ لنفسه، والإخلاص، وحُسْن الخلق، والسّخاءِ، والمسكنة التي طلبها النبيُّ بقوله: (اللهم أحيني مِسْكينًا، وأمتني مسكينًا، واحشرني في زمرة المساكين).
Conclusion on Sufism and unveilings; for the perfection of the soul and the beauty of its attributes, and it is not possible to reach it except after fana (annihilation), which is the total removal of the blameworthy attributes of the soul, so that it does not turn to any of them, but rather becomes disgusted with them as one disgusted with eating a carcass, for example. And its blameworthy attributes are: envy, malice, love of status, fame, praise, leadership, desires, pride, hypocrisy, self-admiration, dissimulation, delusion, and biting anyone from creation without a legitimate purpose, and the like. So when these ugly attributes leave him, he becomes adorned with their opposites of praiseworthy attributes, such as compassion and mercy towards creation, so that he loves for others what he loves for himself, sincerity, good character, generosity, and the humility (maskanah) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked for in his saying: 'O Allah, cause me to live as a poor person, cause me to die as a poor person, and gather me among the poor.'
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines fana (spiritual annihilation) and enumerates the blameworthy traits of the soul. The author begins by stating that perfection of the soul and beauty of its attributes cannot be attained except after fana, which he defines as the total removal of blameworthy traits, to the point that the soul becomes disgusted with them. He then lists these traits: envy, malice, love of status, fame, praise, leadership, desires, pride, hypocrisy, self-admiration, delusion, and harming others without legitimate reason. He then explains that when these ugly traits are removed, one is adorned with their opposite praiseworthy attributes: compassion, mercy, loving for others what one loves for oneself, sincerity, good character, generosity, and the humility (maskanah) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed for in the famous hadith.

Key Terms
فناء
صفات النفس المذمومة
المسكنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fana is sometimes misunderstood as self-annihilation or loss of consciousness.
Correction: This passage clarifies that fana is the total elimination of blameworthy traits, not the soul itself. The soul remains but is purified.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the definition of fana (annihilation) in this passage?
A) A trance-like state of unconsciousness
B) The total removal of the soul's blameworthy attributes
C) Freedom from all religious obligations
D) A physical death of the body

Key Takeaway
Fana is the total removal of blameworthy traits of the soul, leading to the acquisition of their opposite praiseworthy attributes, especially humility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet ﷺ asked to live and die as a miskin (humble). Are you willing to forgo recognition, praise, and status to be among the humble? What is holding you back from loving that state as the Prophet did?

The Definition of Maskanah (Humility)
Defines maskanah and its spiritual importance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual meaning of maskanah (humility) as submission to God and its role in purifying the soul from the love of leadership.

Core Idea
True humility means you don't even sense the scent of leadership.

The text defines maskanah not as poverty or weakness, but as a profound spiritual state of submission to God and gentleness with creation. It warns that without this quality, the soul inevitably contends with God's exclusive attributes. The passage reveals that the deepest-rooted vice, love of leadership, is only uprooted through spiritual struggle.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of maskanah
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two components: submission to God's lordship and lowering the wing to creation.
2
Understand the consequence of lacking maskanah
The author says that without maskanah, the soul will contest God in His specific attributes. Reflect on why love of leadership is seen as a form of rivalry with God.
3
Reflect on the difficulty of removing love of leadership
The passage states that love of leadership is deeply rooted and only leaves through mujahada (spiritual striving). Ponder why it is the last vice to leave the truthful.
This connects to the idea that true servitude (ubudiyya) is a gift from God.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Many think maskanah means being weak or poor. The text clarifies it is a spiritual quality of humility before God and others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه المشكنةُ هى: خُضوعُ النفس لمقام الألوهية، وخفض الجناح للبرية حتى لا يسمَّ صاحبها للرئاسة رائحةً، وصاحبها هو العبد الحقيقي الصدّيقي، فمَنْ لَم يتَّصِف بها لم تخلُ نفسُه مِنْ مُنازعةِ الحقِّ تعالى في أخص أوصافه؛ لأن الرئاسة إنهما تكون للفاعل المختار الغنيّ على الإطلاق، وهي لا تُفارِقُ الإنسان إلا بعد المجاهدة فعِرقُها لا ينقَطِعُ عنْ أَحَدٍ إِلا مَنْ حَصَّه الله بالعُبوديّة المحضة، ولذا قالوا: الكُبرى، في آخرُ ما يخرُجُ مِنْ قلب الصديقين حُبُّ الرئاسة.
And this 'maskanah' (humility) is: the soul's submission to the station of lordship, and lowering the wing to creation, so that its owner does not even smell a scent of leadership. Its owner is the true, siddiq (truthful) servant. So whoever is not characterized by it, his soul will not be free from contesting with the Truth Most High in His most specific attributes; because leadership belongs only to the free agent, the absolutely independent. And it does not leave a person except after striving (mujahada); its root is not cut off from anyone except whom God has singled out with pure servitude. Therefore they said: pride (al-kubra), the last thing that comes out of the hearts of the truthful ones is love of leadership.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage defines maskanah (humility). It is described as submission of the soul to God's lordship and being gentle with creation, so much so that one does not even perceive leadership. The possessor of maskanah is the true servant of God. The author warns that without this trait, one's soul will inevitably contend with God over His exclusive attributes, because leadership belongs solely to God as the Independent Agent. This love of leadership is deeply rooted and only removed through spiritual struggle (mujahada), and it is the last thing to leave the heart of the truthful ones.

Correction: Maskanah is a spiritual quality of humility before God and being gentle with others, not a state of worldly deprivation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage says that lack of maskanah leads to contesting God in His attributes. Ask yourself honestly: do you ever feel frustrated when others are chosen over you? That frustration is a sign of competing with God's sovereignty. Can you name a specific situation where you felt that? How can you practice maskanah in that situation starting today?
?
Maskanah means lowering the wing to creation. Think of one person you find difficult to be humble towards. What would it cost you to treat them with the same gentleness you show to those you admire? Will you do it today?
