The Station of Humility and the Path of Struggle
Dardeer defines al-maskanah and outlines the practice of mujahadah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of al-maskanah (spiritual humility) and the practices of mujahadah required to attain it.

Core Idea
True humility empties the heart of the love of leadership, which is the last vice to leave the truthful.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer defines the noble station of al-maskanah—the soul's submission to Allah and gentleness with creation. He then reveals the surprising truth that the last thing to leave the heart of the truthful is love of leadership, and describes the spiritual struggle (mujahadah) needed to uproot it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm and terminology come through.
Notice the key terms: al-maskanah, al-mujahadah, al-suluk.
2
Identify the definition and its implication
Find how Dardeer defines al-maskanah and why lacking it leads to contending with Allah's attributes.
The definition includes both submission to Allah and lowering the wing to creation.
3
List the means of mujahadah
Extract the practices mentioned: constant dhikr, heart attachment to Allah, hunger, night-vigil, withdrawal from people, silence except for dhikr, and the remaining pillars of the path.
These are the practical steps to uproot the love of leadership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه المشكنةُ هى: خُضوعُ النفس لمقام الألوهية، وخفض الجناح للبرية حتى لا يسمَّ صاحبها للرئاسة رائحةً، وصاحبها هو العبد الحقيقي الصدّيقي، فمَنْ لَم يتَّصِف بها لم تخلُ نفسُه مِنْ مُنازعةِ الحقِّ تعالى في أخص أوصافه؛ لأن الرئاسة إنهما تكون للفاعل المختار الغنيّ على الإطلاق، وهي لا تُفارِقُ الإنسان إلا بعد المجاهدة فعِرقُها لا ينقَطِعُ عنْ أَحَدٍ إِلا مَنْ حَصَّه الله بالعُبوديّة المحضة، ولذا قالوا: الكُبرى، في آخرُ ما يخرُجُ مِنْ قلب الصديقين حُبُّ الرئاسة. ولا يسهل الوصول إليها عادةً إلا بمُداومة ذكرِ «لا إله إلا الله» ليلا ونهارًا، معَ تعلق القلب بالله وحده، والجوع والسهر والاعتزال عن الناس، والصمت إلا عن ذكر الله تعالى، ومُلاحظة بقيّة أركان الطريق التي سيأتي بيانها إن شاء الله تعالى، وهو المسمّى بـ «المجاهدة»، قال تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ جَاهَدُوا فِينَا لَنَهْدِيَنَّهُمْ سُبُلَنَا﴾، وهذا الترقي هو المُسَمّى بـ السُّلوكِ إلى مَلِكِ المُلوكِ عِندَ الطائفة.
And this station of humility (al-maskanah) is: the soul's submission to the station of divinity, and lowering the wing to creation, so that its possessor does not smell the scent of leadership. And its possessor is the true servant, the veracious (siddīqī). Whoever is not characterized by it, his soul is not free from contending with the Truth (al-Ḥaqq), Exalted, in His most specific attributes; because leadership only befits the absolutely independent, free-acting agent. And it (leadership) does not leave a person except after struggling (mujāhadah); its vein does not cease from anyone except whom Allah has granted pure servitude. Therefore they said: the major (al-kubrā) — the last thing that leaves the heart of the truthful is love of leadership. And it is not usually easy to reach it except by constant remembrance of 'There is no god but Allah' night and day, with the heart's attachment to Allah alone, and hunger, night-vigil, withdrawal from people, silence except from remembrance of Allah, and observing the remaining pillars of the path which will be explained later, God willing. This is called 'struggle' (mujāhadah). He said, Exalted: {And those who strive for Us, We will surely guide them to Our ways} (Quran 29:69). And this ascension is called 'wayfaring (sulūk) to the King of kings' according to the group.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage defines the spiritual station called 'al-maskanah' (humility/self-abasement) and explains the means to attain it. The author describes it as the soul's submission to the divine station and the lowering of one's wing (i.e., being gentle) to creation, so that the person does not even smell the scent of leadership (al-ri'āsah). The possessor of this station is the true servant, the siddīq (veracious). Without this attribute, the soul inevitably competes with Allah in His most specific attributes—namely, absolute independence and free choice, which belong solely to the Creator. Leadership does not depart from a person except through mujāhadah (struggle). Its 'vein' remains in everyone except those whom Allah has granted pure servitude. This is why the scholars say: 'The last thing to leave the hearts of the truthful is love of leadership.' The passage then outlines the usual means to reach this station: constant dhikr (remembrance) of 'Lā ilāha illallāh' night and day, with the heart attached solely to Allah, along with hunger, night-vigil, withdrawal from people, silence except for dhikr, and observing the other 'pillars of the path' (arkān al-ṭarīq). This entire practice is called 'mujāhadah', and the Quranic verse (29:69) is cited as its basis. The author concludes that this ascension (taraqqī) is called 'sulūk' (wayfaring) to the King of kings according to the Sufi tradition.

Key Terms
المشكنة (al-maskanah)
المجاهدة (mujāhadah)
السُّلوك (al-sulūk)
الرئاسة (al-ri'āsah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is about avoiding political leadership or positions of authority in society.
Correction: The passage addresses the spiritual vice of seeking prominence over others (ri'āsah), which is an inner attachment to status and self-importance—not the outer role of leadership. It is about purifying the heart from the love of being above others.

Checkpoint
What is the last thing that leaves the heart of the truthful according to this passage?
A) Love of wealth
B) Love of leadership
C) Love of family
D) Love of food

Key Takeaway
Al-maskanah is the soul's submission to Allah that eliminates the love of leadership, truly achieved only through sustained mujahadah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself feeling pleased when others depend on you for leadership, but reluctant to serve in a lowly position? What does that feeling reveal about the 'vein of leadership' in your heart, and what practice will you adopt today to cut it?

The passage says that the last thing to leave the truthful is love of leadership. Imagine your own deathbed—if you had to name one position or recognition you would be reluctant to let go of, what would it be? Write it down now, and commit to a specific act of humility this week that contradicts that attachment.
?
Which of the listed practices (hunger, night-vigil, withdrawal, silence) do you avoid the most? Why? And if you were to start one tomorrow, what concrete step will you take to make it a consistent part of your life?

The Distinction Between al-Sayr and al-Suluk
Dardeer defines al-sayr and distinguishes it from al-suluk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between al-sayr (spiritual journeying) and al-suluk (wayfaring) and their causal relationship according to Imam Dardeer.

Core Idea
Al-Sayr is the cause; al-Suluk is the path.

Imam Dardeer begins by defining a key term in Islamic spirituality: al-sayr (spiritual journeying). He carefully distinguishes it from al-suluk (wayfaring), showing that they are not synonymous but intimately connected. This passage lays the foundation for understanding the spiritual path as taught by the Sufi masters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the definition of al-sayr and how it involves both the heart's turning and opposition to the self.
Pay attention to the phrase 'with opposing the self in its desires—even if permissible'.
2
Identify the relationship
Find the phrase 'al-sayr is like a cause for al-suluk'. Reflect on what this causal relationship implies for the spiritual journey.
Think about how the cause (sayr) leads to the effect (suluk).
3
Note the broader context
The passage mentions that al-suluk is the way of prophets, the truthful, and the learned, but it varies. Consider how this fits with the definition of sayr.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to test your grasp of the relationship between sayr and suluk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السَّيرُ إلى الله تعالى فهو تَوجُهُ القَلْبِ إلى الربِّ مَعَ مُخالفة النفْسِ في شَهَواتِها - ولو مُباحةً - طلبًا لمرضاة الله تعالى، وإيثارا له على ما سواه، فالسَّيرُ كالسبب في السلوكِ، وقد يُطلَقُ السُّلوك على المعنى الثاني أيضًا. والسُّلوك إلى الله تعالى طريقةً النبيين والصدّيقين والعُلَماء العاملين إلا أنه مُختلفٌ :
As for spiritual journeying (al-sayr) to Allah, Exalted, it is the heart's turning to the Lord while opposing the self in its desires—even if permissible—seeking Allah's pleasure, and preferring Him over others. So the spiritual journeying (al-sayr) is like a cause for wayfaring (al-sulūk), and sometimes wayfaring (al-sulūk) is applied to the second meaning as well. And wayfaring (al-sulūk) to Allah, Exalted, is the way of the prophets, the truthful, and the learned who act, but it varies:
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage defines 'al-sayr' (spiritual journeying) and distinguishes it from 'al-sulūk' (wayfaring). The author states that sayr is the heart's orientation towards the Lord while opposing the soul in its desires—even permissible ones—seeking Allah's pleasure and preferring Him over everything else. Sayr is described as 'like a cause' (ka al-sabab) for sulūk. Additionally, the term 'sulūk' is sometimes applied to this same meaning (i.e., the heart's turning). The passage then notes that sulūk to Allah is the path of the prophets, the truthful (ṣiddīqīn), and the learned who act upon their knowledge, but this path varies—implying different degrees or forms, which the author does not elaborate in this sentence (the text continues in the next lesson).

Key Terms
السَّير (al-sayr)
السُّلوك (al-sulūk)
مخالفة النفس (mukhālafat al-nafs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-sayr and al-suluk are synonymous terms for the same spiritual practice.
Correction: Imam Dardeer clarifies that al-sayr is the cause (the heart's turning and self-opposition) that leads to al-suluk (the actual wayfaring). They are distinct but causally connected.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relationship between al-sayr and al-suluk?
A) They are identical
B) Sayr is a cause for suluk
C) Suluk is a cause for sayr
D) They are unrelated

Key Takeaway
Al-sayr (the heart's turning and self-opposition) is the cause that leads to al-suluk (the spiritual wayfaring), which varies among different people.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you denied yourself a permissible desire (like a favorite food or entertainment) solely to seek Allah's pleasure? What is stopping you from doing so today?
?
Your heart's orientation defines your sayr. Honestly examine your heart right now: is it truly turned toward Allah, or is it captivated by worldly attachments? What one concrete action can you take this week to redirect your heart?
?
The passage says sulūk is the path of the prophets and the truthful. Are you on that path? If not, what specific barrier—laziness, pride, or distraction—keeps you from committing to daily spiritual wayfaring? Decide now one step you will take to enter that path.

The Seven Types of Souls and the Soul Commanding Evil
Dardeer contrasts spiritual wayfaring and introduces the first of seven souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of souls in Sufi cosmology, particularly the first soul (al-nafs al-ammārah), and the principle that spiritual ends depend on beginnings.

Core Idea
The first soul commands evil; spiritual perfection depends on purifying the beginning.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's commentary introduces spiritual wayfaring (sulūk) and the seven states of the soul. It contrasts the pure starting point of prophets with the dark beginnings of others, establishing a key spiritual law: the end reflects the beginning. It then lists the first of the seven souls, which commands evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's own words set the context before you analyze.
The passage is from the conclusion on Sufism (taṣawwuf).
2
Notice the two types of wayfaring
Identify the wayfaring of prophets (beginning from purified souls) versus that of others (beginning from dark souls). Notice how the Prophet Muhammad's beginning is described as the end of others.
The term 'ūlū al-ʿazm' refers to the resolute prophets.
3
Grasp the principle of beginnings and ends
Dardeer states: 'The ends differ in luminosity according to the difference of beginnings; by burning out the beginning comes the luminosity of the end.' This is a crucial spiritual law.
This principle applies to all spiritual wayfaring.
4
Identify the first soul
The passage lists seven souls by attributes but only gives the first: al-nafs al-ammārah bil-sūʾ (the soul commanding evil). Note its defining characteristic: it does not command its owner to good.
This refers to Quran 12:53.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة : في التصوف - فسُلوكُ الأنبياء - عليهم الصلاة والسلام - مبدؤه الترقي مِنْ نُفوسِ مُطَهَّرة كمالية إلى ما لا نهاية له مِنَ المقامات الإحْسانية، وهو في نفْسه متفاوت، فسلوك أولي العزم منه أعلى وأجَلُّ مِنْ سُلوكِ غَيرهم، وسُلوكُ سيّدِ أُولي العزم - عليه وعليهم أفضل الصلاة والسلام - أعلى مِنْ غَيْرِه، إذ مُبْدَوْهِ نِهايَةُ غَيره. وأمّا سُلوكُ غيرهم فمِنْ نُفوس أمارة أو لوّامة ظُلْمانيّة، إلى نفس كاملة صِدِّيقية. والنهايات تختلفُ في الإشراق بحسَبِ اختلاف البدايات، فبإحراق البداية يكونُ إشراقُ النّهاية. والنفوس سبعة بحسب أوصافها، وإلا فهي واحدة: ١ - الأولى النفْسُ الأمارة بالسوء، وهي التي لا تأمُرُ صاحبَها بخير.
Conclusion on Sufism (taṣawwuf): The wayfaring (sulūk) of the prophets—peace be upon them—its beginning is ascension from perfectly purified souls to endless stations of excellence (iḥsān), and it is in itself differentiated: the wayfaring of the resolute (ūlū al-ʿazm) is higher and greater than that of others; and the wayfaring of the chief of the resolute—upon him and them the best prayer and peace—is higher than others, since his beginning is the end of others. As for the wayfaring of others, it is from souls that are commanding (ammārah) or blaming (lawwāmah), dark, to a perfect, veracious (ṣiddīqī) soul. The ends differ in luminosity according to the difference of beginnings; by burning out the beginning comes the luminosity of the end. The souls are seven according to their attributes, otherwise they are one: 1 – The first: the soul commanding evil (al-nafs al-ammārah bil-sūʾ), which does not command its owner to good.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion on Sufism that discusses the types of souls in relation to spiritual wayfaring (sulūk). It first contrasts the wayfaring of the prophets with that of others. The prophets' wayfaring begins from perfectly purified souls and ascends to endless stations of excellence; it varies in degree, with the wayfaring of the resolute prophets (ūlū al-ʿazm) being higher, and that of the Prophet Muhammad (the chief of the resolute) being the highest, as his beginning is the end of others. In contrast, the wayfaring of others begins from dark souls (either commanding or blaming) and proceeds toward a perfect, veracious soul. The author then states a principle: the ends differ in luminosity according to the differences of beginnings—by 'burning out' the base beginning, one attains the luminous end. Finally, the passage introduces the classification of souls: they are seven according to their attributes, though essentially one. It lists the first type: the soul commanding evil (al-nafs al-ammārah bil-sūʾ), which does not command its owner to any good—a direct reference to Quran 12:53.

Key Terms
النفس الأمارة بالسوء
السلوك
المقامات الإحسانية
النفوس السبعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The seven souls are separate independent entities in a person.
Correction: They are different states of the same single soul, distinguished by attributes.

Checkpoint

A) It commands its owner to do good
B) It is perfectly purified
C) It does not command its owner to good
D) It is the soul at rest

Key Takeaway
The first soul (al-nafs al-ammārah) commands evil and does not command good; spiritual wayfaring begins by recognizing and purifying this state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the first soul (al-nafs al-ammārah) does not command its owner to any good. In your own life, when you feel a strong urge to do something you know is wrong, do you recognize that as the command of this soul? Are you honest enough to admit that your soul sometimes commands you to evil, or do you rationalize it? What concrete step will you take this week to resist one such command?
?
The passage says that the ends differ in luminosity according to the difference of beginnings; by burning out the beginning comes the luminosity of the end. What is the 'beginning' in your own spiritual state that you need to burn out? What dark habit or thought pattern do you need to incinerate so that your end may be luminous? Be specific.
?
The prophets began their wayfaring from purified souls, whereas others start from dark souls. Recognizing that you are not a prophet, you must acknowledge your starting point. How does it feel to know that your journey begins from a soul that commands evil? Does this humble you or motivate you? What will you do today to take the first step from that state?

The Commanding Soul: al-Ammara bi al-Su'
Definition and evidence for the commanding soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the commanding soul (al-ammara bi al-su') and why struggling against it is the greater jihad.

Core Idea
Your worst enemy is the soul between your sides.

This passage introduces the first category of the soul, al-ammara bi al-su'. It explains its defining characteristic—that it never commands good—and supports this with scriptural evidence from the Quran and hadith. The author also clarifies why combating this soul is considered the greater jihad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the three proofs the author cites.
2
Identify the definition and proofs
Find the definition of al-ammara and then identify the three scriptural proofs: one Quranic verse and two hadiths. Write them down.
The author uses: verse 12:53, the hadith about the soul as worst enemy, and the hadith about greater jihad.
3
Understand why jihad against the soul is greater
Read the explanation: the soul is in the darkness of nature, cannot distinguish good from evil, and Satan uses it as a vehicle. That makes the internal struggle harder and greater.
This connects to the core idea.
4
Reflect on the soul's role
Consider the implication: Satan can only overcome a person through his own soul. This highlights the importance of self-struggle.
This is a key lesson in Islamic spirituality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأولى النفس الأمارة بالسوء، وهي التي لا تأمر صاحبها بخير. إشارة إلى قوله تعالى: {إِنَّ النَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّي} وقوله: (أعدى عدوك نفسك التي بين جنبيك)، وقوله: (قدمتم من الجهاد الأصغر إلى الجهاد الأكبر) فسمى جهاد الكفار أصغر، وسمى جهاد النفس أكبر، وذلك لأنها واقعة في ظلمة الطبيعة، فلا فرق لها بين الحق والباطل، ولا تميز بين الخير والشر، ولا يقدر الشيطان اللعين على الإنسان إلا بواسطتها.
The first is the commanding soul to evil, and it is that which does not command its owner to good. An indication of His saying, the Exalted: {Indeed, the soul is a persistent enjoiner of evil, except those upon which my Lord has mercy} and His saying: (Your worst enemy is your soul which is between your sides), and His saying: (You have come from the lesser jihad to the greater jihad). So he called jihad against the disbelievers the lesser, and called jihad against the soul the greater, and that is because it is situated in the darkness of nature, so it does not distinguish between truth and falsehood, nor does it differentiate between good and evil, and the accursed Satan cannot overpower man except through it.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage defines and provides evidence for the first soul, al-ammara bi al-su' (the commanding soul to evil). The author states that this soul never commands its owner to do any good. He then cites three scriptural proofs: first, the Quranic verse from Surah Yusuf (12:53) that the soul is indeed prone to evil, unless God grants mercy; second, a hadith that a person's worst enemy is his own soul; third, a hadith about returning from the lesser jihad (against external enemies) to the greater jihad (against the soul). The author explains that the Prophet called jihad against the soul greater because the soul dwells in the darkness of physical nature, unable to distinguish truth from falsehood or good from evil. Satan can only reach man through this soul. This passage emphasizes the inherent evil tendency of the lower soul and the need to struggle against it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'al-ammara' is an entirely separate entity from the self.
Correction: It is a state of the same soul that can be transformed through struggle and divine mercy.

Checkpoint

C) Because the soul is inherently good.
D) Because it requires more physical strength.

Key Takeaway
The commanding soul (al-ammara) is inherently inclined to evil, making the struggle against it the greatest form of jihad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time your soul commanded you to do something you knew was wrong, and you obeyed? What specific lie did it whisper to make that action seem acceptable? Now, what will you do tomorrow to catch that same deception before you act?
?
The Prophet said your worst enemy is your soul between your sides. Think of a person or situation you blame for your spiritual struggles. Could it be that your own soul is the real enemy, and you have been fighting the wrong battle? Write down one way you will redirect your effort this week from blaming others to confronting your own nafs.
?
If jihad against the soul is greater than jihad against the disbelievers, then the internal battle you avoid—the small compromises, the lazy prayers, the hidden pride—is more significant than any external threat. What is one internal battle you have been postponing, and what is the first step you will take today to engage it?

The Second Soul: al-Lawwama
Definition of the blaming soul's behavior and naming.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the blaming soul (al-lawwama) and its place in the spiritual journey between the commanding soul and the peaceful soul.

Core Idea
The blaming soul struggles but still falls; its blame is a sign of spiritual awakening.

After describing the commanding soul (al-ammara), Imam Dardir now introduces the second stage of the soul: al-lawwama, the blaming soul. This soul has begun to resist its lower desires but is still dominated by them. Its distinctive feature is that when it sins, it returns to blame itself—a sign of nascent moral consciousness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the description of the soul's behavior sink in.
Notice the conditional structure: 'When... it is called...'
2
Understand the process
The passage describes a sequence: struggle, submission to truth, acceptance of obligation, but still being overcome in most states, then blame. Identify each stage.
3
Reflect on the name
'Lawwama' comes from 'lawm' (blame). The soul is named after its characteristic of blaming itself. Connect this to the Quranic oath in Surah al-Qiyama.
Quran 75:2: 'I swear by the blaming soul.'
4
Place in the spiritual journey
Compare this to the first soul (ammara) which commands evil without regret, and anticipate the third soul (mutma'inna) which is at peace. The lawwama is an intermediate stage of moral awakening.
It is the second of three souls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا جاهدها صاحبها وخالفها في شهواتها حتى أذعنت لاتباع الحق، وسكنت تحت الأمر التكليفي، ولكنها تغلب صاحبها في أكثر أحوالها، ثم ترجع إليه باللوم على ما وقع سميت لوامة، وهي الثانية.
When its owner struggles against it and opposes it in its desires until it submits to following the truth, and settles under the command of obligation, but it overcomes its owner in most of its states, then returns to him with blame for what happened, it is called al-lawwama, and it is the second.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the second soul, al-lawwama (the blaming soul). When a person struggles against the lower soul and opposes its desires, the soul eventually submits to the truth and follows religious obligations. However, it still dominates its owner in most situations. After committing a sin, it returns to blame him. This soul is characterized by this alternation between obedience and blame. The name is derived from the Quranic oath 'by the blaming soul' (al-qiyama 75:2). The author presents this as a step of spiritual development.

Key Terms

Correction: The passage explicitly states that the lawwama still overcomes its owner in most states, and its blame comes after disobedience, so it is an intermediate stage, not the final one.

Checkpoint

A) It never disobeys Allah.
B) It always overcomes desires.
C) It blames itself after sinning despite often being overcome by desires.
D) It is the same as the peaceful soul.

Key Takeaway
The blaming soul represents a stage where the person struggles against desires and feels remorse after sin, though he still often succumbs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin and feel blame, do you use that blame as a motivation to truly struggle against your desires, or do you simply feel guilty and move on without change? What would it take for your blame to become a force that transforms your behavior?
?

?
If you truly believed that the blame you feel after sin is a sign that your soul is alive and fighting, how would that change the way you respond to your failures? What one desire will you commit to opposing today, even if you know you may fall again?

The Inspired Soul: al-Mulhama
Definition and sign of the inspired soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the inspired soul (al-mulhama) is and how it is recognized by its awareness of subtle spiritual deceptions.

Core Idea
The inspired soul knows its own hidden faults—a sign of spiritual progress.

Having struggled and exerted effort, the soul begins to turn toward holiness and becomes illuminated. At this stage it is called al-mulhama (the inspired soul), and its key sign is self-knowledge of subtle inner flaws like ostentation and self-admiration. This passage defines that state and its distinguishing mark.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once, then the literal translation. Notice the compact definition and the single sign that follows.
The passage is brief but dense.
2
Understand how the soul reaches this stage
The passage says the soul achieves this through 'struggle and effort' (مجاهدة وكد) until it inclines to the holy realm and becomes illuminated. This is a progression from earlier soul states.
3
Identify the sign of al-mulhama
The sign is that its owner knows its 'subtle hidden deceptions' (دسائسها الخفية الدقيقة). The passage gives examples: ostentation and self-admiration.
This shows that the soul is not yet perfect, but aware.
4
Reflect on the transitional nature of this soul
Al-mulhama is the third soul, not the final one. Those at this stage can still have hidden flaws, but the key is that they recognize them.
This guards against thinking it is the ultimate goal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أخذ في المجاهدة والكد، حتى مالت إلى عالم القدس، واستنارت بحيث أهمت فجورها وتقواها، سميت ملهمة، وهي الثالثة، وعلامتها أن يعرف صاحبها دسائسها الخفية الدقيقة، من الرياء والعجب وغير ذلك.
When he continues in struggle and effort until it inclines to the world of holiness, and is illuminated such that it becomes inspired with its wickedness and its piety, it is called al-mulhama, and it is the third. Its sign is that its owner knows its subtle hidden deceptions, such as ostentation, self-admiration, and other things.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the third soul, al-mulhama (the inspired soul). Through continued spiritual struggle and exertion, the soul begins to incline towards the holy realm and becomes illuminated. It reaches the state mentioned in the Quran: 'He inspired it with its wickedness and its piety' (al-shams 91:8). The distinguishing sign of this level is that the person becomes aware of the soul's subtle hidden deceptions (dasa'is), such as showing off (riya') and self-admiration ('ujb). This is the first stage where the soul gains spiritual insight and can recognize its own inner faults.

Misconception: One might think al-mulhama is the final spiritual goal, or that it is sinless.
Correction: Al-mulhama is a transitional stage where hidden faults remain but become known to the person. Awareness of flaws does not mean they are absent.

C) The owner performs miracles.

Key Takeaway
The inspired soul (al-mulhama) is recognized by its owner's awareness of the soul's hidden deceptions, such as ostentation and self-admiration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
The path to mulhama requires struggle and effort. What is one specific area of your character you have been avoiding struggling against? Will you start today?

The Fourth Soul: al-Mutma'innah and Its Hidden Deceptions
Definition of the tranquil soul and its hidden subtle deceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the tranquil soul (al-mutma'innah), how it is attained through struggle, and the subtle deceptions that can affect even those who reach this high spiritual station.

Core Idea
The tranquil soul is not immune to hidden deceptions, including hidden shirk and love of leadership.

In this lesson, Imam Dardir explains the fourth and highest stage of the soul: al-mutma'innah (the tranquil soul). While this stage marks the beginning of true nearness to Allah, it also carries extremely subtle dangers. Only those with illumined insight can perceive these hidden deceptions. Let's explore the characteristics of this soul and the traps that lie within.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Let the author's own description of the soul's transformation come through.
Notice the contrast between the outward virtues and the hidden deceptions.
2
Identify the characteristics of al-mutma'innah
List the praiseworthy attributes mentioned: compassion, mercy, generosity, etc. Also note that this soul experiences unveilings and miracles.
These outward virtues make the deception harder to detect.
3
Understand the hidden deceptions
The passage mentions 'hidden shirk' and 'love of leadership' as subtle deceptions. Ask yourself why these are particularly dangerous at this stage.
The person may not recognize them because they appear righteous.
4
Reflect on the warning
The author warns that the owner of this soul may think he is the greatest leader. Realize that this pride itself is a deception.
This lesson guards against spiritual complacency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا لزم المجاهدة حتى زالت عنها الشهوات، وتبدلت الصفات المذمومة بالمحمودة، وتخلقت بأخلاق الله تعالى الجمالية، من الرأفة والرحمة واللطف والكرم والود، سميت مطمئنة، وهي الرابعة، وهذا المقام هو مبتدأ الوصول إلى الله تعالى، ولكنها لا تخلو من دسائس خفية جدا، كالشرك الخفي وحب الرئاسة، إلا أنها لخفائها ودقتها لا يدركها إلا أهلها الذين نور الله بصائرهم؛ لأن ظاهرها الصلاح والاتصاف بالصفات الحميدة، من الكرم والحلم والتوكل والزهد والورع والشكر والصبر والتسليم والرضا بالقضاء، مع انكشاف بعض أسرار، وانخراق بعض عادات، وظهور بعض كرامات، فلربما ظن صاحبها أنه الإمام الأعظم، وأن مقامه هو المقام الأفخم، وهذا من جملة الدسائس.
When he continues in struggle until desires depart from it, and the blameworthy characteristics are replaced by praiseworthy ones, and it is adorned with the beautiful attributes of Allah the Exalted—compassion, mercy, gentleness, generosity, and affection—it is called al-mutma'inna, and it is the fourth. This station is the beginning of reaching Allah the Exalted, but it is not free of very hidden deceptions, like hidden polytheism and love of leadership. However, because of their concealment and subtlety, only those whose insights Allah has illumined perceive them, for its outward appearance is righteousness and being characterized with praiseworthy attributes—generosity, forbearance, trust, asceticism, scrupulousness, gratitude, patience, submission, and contentment with divine decree—along with disclosure of some secrets, breaking of some habits, and appearance of some miracles. So perhaps its owner thinks that he is the greatest leader and that his station is the most splendid station, and this is among the deceptions.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth soul, al-mutma'inna (the tranquil soul). Through persistent struggle, desires vanish, blameworthy traits are replaced with good ones, and the soul acquires divine attributes like compassion and generosity. This stage marks the beginning of true arrival to Allah. However, it still harbors extremely hidden deceptions (dasa'is) such as hidden shirk (associating partners with God in a subtle way) and love of leadership. These are so subtle that only those with divinely illumined insight can detect them. The outward appearance is one of complete righteousness and virtue, including generosity, trust, asceticism, etc. The person may even experience spiritual unveilings and miracles, leading him to mistakenly believe he has reached the highest station. The author warns that this very pride is itself a hidden deception. This lesson highlights the danger of spiritual complacency at this level.

Key Terms
النفس المطمئنة
دسائس خفية
الشرك الخفي
حب الرئاسة
كرامات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the mutma'innah soul is infallible and free from all faults.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that it is not free from hidden deceptions like hidden shirk and love of leadership, which can lead to self-deception.

Checkpoint
What hidden deception is specifically mentioned in relation to the mutma'innah soul?
A) Open disobedience
B) Hidden polytheism and love of leadership
C) Physical pleasures
D) Doubt in God's existence

Key Takeaway
The tranquil soul (al-mutma'innah) is a high station, but it contains hidden deceptions like hidden shirk and love of leadership that only the spiritually discerning can detect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you experienced a spiritual miracle or felt you had attained a high rank, would you be confident that you are not falling into the deception of thinking yourself the greatest? How would you distinguish genuine closeness to Allah from subtle pride? What does this lesson demand you to change in your self-assessment?

The Fifth Stage: The Soul in Fana and Rida
Description of the soul that attains annihilation and contentment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics and stages leading to the soul's annihilation (fana') and contentment (rida) as described by Imam Dardir.

Core Idea
The contented soul sees God's decree in everything, achieving true peace.

This passage from the Sharh al-Kharidat al-Bahiyyah describes the final stage of the soul's purification. After the soul becomes tranquil, it is reached by divine care and guided through spiritual struggle under a master. The ultimate goal is the station of annihilation and complete contentment with all that happens. This lesson unpacks each step of that journey.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the sequence of conditions and outcomes.
2
Identify the key milestones
The passage lists several achievements: divine care, reliance on shaykh, struggle, mastery of attributes, cutting hypocrisy, humility, indifference to praise/blame, entering fana, contentment. Mark each one.
These are not arbitrary; they build on each other.
3
Understand fana' and rida
Reflect on what it means to be content with everything that occurs. This is not passivity but a state of seeing divine wisdom in all events.
The common misunderstanding is that fana' means annihilation of existence; it means annihilation of ego.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه فإذا أدركته العناية الإلهية، واستند إلى شيخه بالكلية، ولازم المجاهدة، حتى تمكن من الصفات المحمودة، وانقطع عنه عرق الرياء، وصارت نفسه ذليلة، واستوى عنده المدح والذم، ودخلت في مقام الفناء، ورضيت بكل ما يقع في الكون.
Then when divine care reaches it, it relies completely upon its shaykh, continues the struggle until it masters the praiseworthy attributes, the vein of hypocrisy is cut off, its soul becomes humble, praise and blame become equal to it, it enters the station of annihilation (fana'), and it becomes content with everything that occurs in the universe.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage describes the next stage after the mutma'inna soul. The soul is now reached by divine care (inaya ilahiyya). The seeker relies wholly upon his spiritual master (shaykh) and persists in the struggle until he fully embodies praiseworthy qualities. The root of hypocrisy is severed, and the soul becomes utterly humble. He becomes indifferent to praise and blame. He enters the station of annihilation (fana'), which is the negation of self-will. Finally, he attains complete contentment (rida) with all that happens in creation, because he sees God's decree in everything. This is the stage of the radiyya (contented) soul, as it is content with divine decree. The author implies this is the fifth level, though not explicitly numbered here.

Key Terms
عناية إلهية
مقام الفناء
رضا
شيخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fana' means the complete annihilation of the soul's existence.
Correction: Fana' is the annihilation of the ego and selfish desires, not the soul itself. It leads to contentment with divine decree.

Checkpoint
What does the soul achieve after entering the station of annihilation (fana')?
A) It becomes completely passive.
B) It becomes content with everything that occurs.
C) It loses all will.
D) It attains prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The soul that reaches fana' and rida is one that has fully surrendered its ego, becoming content with all divine decrees.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says praise and blame become equal to the contented soul. In which area of my life am I most dependent on others' approval? What would it cost me to let go of that need today?
?
I have read that the seeker relies completely on the shaykh. But have I ever truly submitted my understanding to someone wiser? What is one decision I am making today where I trust my own judgment over seeking counsel?
?
The 'vein of hypocrisy' is cut off at this stage. When I perform good deeds, how often do I check my intention? Name one specific act I did this week that was tainted by a desire for recognition. What will I do to purify it?

The Third Stage: al-Nafs al-Mulhama
Defines the third stage of the soul and its distinguishing sign.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics of the inspired soul (al-nafs al-mulhama) and its distinguishing sign of awareness of hidden faults.

Core Idea
The inspired soul is aware of its hidden faults, not yet perfect.

In the spiritual journey, the soul passes through stages. This lesson introduces the third stage, the inspired soul, where through struggle the soul gains illumination and awareness of its inner deceits. The passage from Imam Dardir defines this stage and its sign.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the key terms and the structure.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the condition for this stage
Look for what leads the soul to become mulhama: it engages in struggle (mujahada) and exertion until it inclines to holiness.
The word 'hatta' indicates a gradual process.
3
Understand 'inspiration'
The soul is illuminated and 'inspires' its wickedness and piety. This means it becomes aware of both its faults and virtues.
Inspiration here is not divine revelation but a heightened self-knowledge.
4
Recognize the sign
The sign of this stage is that the person knows their hidden, subtle deceits like hypocrisy and vanity.
Awareness of these deceits is a key milestone, not yet elimination.
5
Address the common misunderstanding
People may think inspiration means sinlessness. Actually, the soul still has faults, but the person now sees them clearly.
This stage requires continued vigilance.

Source Text

Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the third stage, the inspired soul. Through struggle, the soul gains inclination toward holiness and illumination, but still harbors subtle deceits (dasa'is) like hypocrisy and vanity, which the person becomes aware of. The ability to recognize these inner faults is the sign of this stage.

Key Terms
مُلْهَمَة (mulhama)
دَسَائِس (dasa'is)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the inspired soul is sinless and free of faults.
Correction: The passage explicitly states the soul still has hidden deceits (dasa'is) like hypocrisy and vanity; the sign is awareness, not absence.

Checkpoint
What is the distinguishing sign of the inspired soul (al-nafs al-mulhama)?
A) It never commits sins
B) Its owner knows its hidden deceits

Key Takeaway
The inspired soul is marked by the owner's awareness of its hidden subtle deceits, not by sinlessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Fourth Stage of the Soul: al-Nafs al-Mutma'inna
Describes the fourth stage of the soul and its hidden deceits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics of the tranquil soul and the hidden spiritual dangers that accompany this stage.

Core Idea
The tranquil soul is a high station, but even it can harbor subtle traps of spiritual pride.

We now reach the fourth stage of the soul's journey: the tranquil soul (nafs mutma'inna). At this point, the soul has been purified and adorned with divine attributes. Yet, as valuable as this stage is, it comes with its own hidden pitfalls. Imam Dardir warns that the very signs of spiritual achievement can become sources of delusion if not recognized.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition for reaching this stage
Note the process: persistent struggle until desires cease and attributes are replaced with praiseworthy ones. This is not passive but active transformation.
2
Identify the outward virtues and hidden dangers
The passage lists many beautiful qualities like generosity and patience, but also warns of hidden shirk and love of leadership. These can exist beneath the surface.
3
Reflect on the ultimate warning
The most subtle deceit is when the person thinks they are the greatest imam. This shows that no stage is immune from self-delusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - فإذا لزمَ المُجاهَدةَ حتى زالت عنها الشهَواتُ، وتبدَّلت الصفاتُ المذمومة بالمحمودة، وتخلقت بأخلاق الله تعالى الجماليّةِ، مِنَ الرأفة والرحمة واللطف والكرم والوُدَّ سُمّيتْ مُطْمئنَةٌ (۳)، وهي الرابعةُ ، وهذا المقامُ هو مُبْتَدَأَ الوصولِ إلى اللهِ تعالى، ولكنَّها لا تخلو من دسائس خفيّة جدًّا، كالشِّرك الخفيّ وحُبِّ الرئاسة، إلا أنها لخفائها ودقتها لا يُدركها إلا أهلُها الذين نوَّرَ الله بصائرهم؛ لأنَّ ظاهرها الصلاحُ والاتصافُ بالصَّفاتِ الحميدة، مِنَ الكرم والحِلْم والتَّوَكُلِ والزهد والورع والشُّكْرِ والصبر والتسليم والرضا بالقضاء، معَ انكِشافِ بعض أسرار ، وانخِراقِ بعض عادات، وظهور بعض كرامات، فلرُبَّما ظنَّ صاحبها أنه الإمامُ الأَعْظَمُ، وأنَّ مقامه هو المقام الأفخم، وهذا مِنْ جُملة الدسائس.
Then when it persists in struggle until desires cease, blameworthy attributes are replaced with praiseworthy ones, and it is characterized by the beautiful attributes of Allah, such as compassion, mercy, kindness, generosity, and love, it is called the tranquil soul (al-nafs al-mutma'inna), and it is the fourth. This station is the beginning of reaching Allah, but it is not free from very hidden deceits, like hidden shirk and love of leadership, except that due to their subtlety only its people perceive them, those whose hearts Allah has illuminated. Because its outward is righteousness and being described with praiseworthy attributes, such as generosity, forbearance, trust, asceticism, piety, gratitude, patience, submission, satisfaction with decree, along with unveiling of some secrets, breaking of some habits, and appearance of some miracles. Perhaps its owner thinks he is the greatest imam, and that his station is the most magnificent, and this is among the deceits.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth stage, the tranquil soul. It describes how through continued struggle, desires vanish and the soul takes on divine attributes. This station is the beginning of true spiritual arrival, yet it still conceals very subtle deceits, such as hidden shirk and desire for leadership. The outward signs of this stage (generosity, patience, etc.) can mislead the person into thinking they have reached the highest rank, which is itself a deceit.

Key Terms
مُطْمَئِنَّة (mutma'inna)
دَسَائِس (dasa'is)
شِرْك خَفِيّ (hidden shirk)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The tranquil soul is the final, perfect stage free from faults.
Correction: The passage states it is only the beginning of reaching Allah and still contains hidden deceits like hidden shirk and love of leadership.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a hidden deceit that may afflict the tranquil soul?
A) Open sin
B) Hidden shirk and love of leadership
C) Lack of generosity
D) Anger

Key Takeaway
Even in the high station of the tranquil soul, one must remain vigilant against hidden spiritual pride and subtle shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you secretly proud of your spiritual progress? The lesson warns that even in the tranquil soul, one can think they are the greatest imam. In what area of your life are you most vulnerable to this hidden pride?
?
The passage says that the outward signs of piety can be deceiving. Is there a virtue you display (generosity, patience, etc.) that you use to avoid addressing a deeper spiritual flaw? What might that flaw be?
?
The lesson says the tranquil soul is only the beginning of reaching Allah. Have you acted as if you have already arrived? What would change in your worship if you truly believed you are still at the beginning?

The Fifth Stage: al-Nafs al-Radiya
Describes the fifth stage of the soul (nafs radiya).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics and spiritual station of the satisfied soul (al-nafs al-radiya), the fifth stage of the soul's journey.

Core Idea
The satisfied soul accepts everything without objection.

After passing through earlier stages of struggle and purification, the soul reaches a state of complete satisfaction with divine decree. This lesson describes the fifth stage, where the soul becomes fully content with everything that occurs, relying entirely on the shaykh and achieving annihilation. Read the passage to see how this state is defined.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequence of conditions leading to the satisfied soul.
2
Identify key phrases
Identify phrases like 'استند إلى شيخه بالكلية', 'استوى عنده المدح والدم', 'دخلت في مقام الفناء', and 'رضيت بكل ما يقع'. These capture the essence of the stage.
3
Connect conditions to meaning
Each condition contributes to the soul's satisfaction. Reflect on how reliance on the shaykh, humility, and indifference to praise/blame lead to annihilation and acceptance.
4
Address common misunderstanding
Satisfaction is not passivity. It is an active spiritual state reached through effort and guidance. Contrast this with fatalism.
The text says 'without any objection at all' but this follows struggle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه فإذا أدركته العناية الإلهية، واستند إلى شَيخه بالكُلّيّة، ولازَمَ المجاهدة، حتى تمكَّنَ مِنَ الصِّفاتِ المحمودة، وانقَطَعَ عنه عرقُ الرّياء، وصارت نفسه ذليلةً، واستوى عِندَه المدْحُ والدم، ودخَلَتْ في مَقام الفَناءِ، ورضيتُ بكُلِّ ما يقعُ فِي الكَونِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اعتراض أصلا، سُمّيت راضية) وهي الخامسة.
Then when divine care reaches it, and it relies completely on its shaykh, and continues struggle until it becomes established in praiseworthy attributes, the vein of hypocrisy is cut off, its soul becomes humble, praise and blame become equal to it, it enters the station of annihilation, and it is satisfied with everything that occurs in existence without any objection at all, it is called the satisfied soul (al-nafs al-radiya), and it is the fifth.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth stage, the satisfied soul. Key features include complete reliance on the shaykh, attainment of praiseworthy qualities, cutting off hypocrisy, humility, indifference to praise or blame, entering the station of annihilation (fana'), and total satisfaction with everything that happens in the universe without objection.

Key Terms
رَاضِيَة (radiya)
فَنَاء (fana')
شَيْخ (shaykh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Satisfaction (rida) means passivity and fatalism.
Correction: Satisfaction is an active spiritual state achieved through struggle and reliance on a guide; it does not mean inaction but inner acceptance of divine will.

Checkpoint

A) It objects to negative events
B) It is satisfied with everything without objection
C) It seeks to change all events
D) It is indifferent to good and bad

Key Takeaway
The satisfied soul is characterized by complete acceptance of divine decree, achieved through struggle and reliance on a guide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you genuinely accepted a painful event without any objection, anger, or despair? What does your lack of satisfaction reveal about the state of your soul?
?
Do you still seek praise from others for your good deeds? If praise and blame were truly equal to you, how would your worship and daily actions change right now?
?
You rely on many things—your skills, your plans, your reputation. But do you rely completely on a shaykh and divine care, as the passage demands? What fear holds you back from that total surrender?

The Sixth Stage: al-Nafs al-Mardiyya
Describes the sixth stage of the soul (nafs mardiyya).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth stage of the soul (nafs mardiyya), the danger of self-admiration in spiritual progress, and the role of divine grace and the shaykh.

Core Idea
The sixth stage of the soul is attained by divine care, not self-effort.

In this passage, Imam Dardir concludes his discussion of the spiritual stages by describing the sixth and highest stage, the pleasing soul (al-nafs al-mardiyya). He first warns of a subtle danger that can cause regression, then describes the soul's transformation when it reaches this station. This lesson will unpack that journey.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the warning
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the warning about the vision of annihilation and sincerity leading to self-admiration. Ask yourself why even high spiritual states can be dangerous.
The warning is against 'seeing' one's own sincerity or annihilation.
2
Understand the transformation
The passage describes a process: annihilating from annihilation, purifying from seeing sincerity, then being manifested with divine satisfaction. Reflect on how this removes all traces of self.
This is a deeper stage beyond ordinary fana' and ikhlas.
3
Identify the characteristics of the sixth stage
List the outcomes: forgiveness of past sins, transformation of evil deeds to good, opening of spiritual tastes, immersion in tawhid. Why is it called 'pleasing'? Because it is cared for by Allah.
The name mardiyya indicates divine pleasure and care.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة في التصوف ولكن رؤية الفناء والإخلاص ربّما أوقعَ في شَيْءٍ مِنَ الإِعْجَابِ، فيرجع به القهقرى، فليستعذ باللهِ مِنْ ذلك معَ مُداوَمَةِ الذِّكْرِ والالتجاء إلى اللهِ ومُلاحظة أنه لا يتم له الخلاص إلا بمدَدِ الشَّيخِ.

فإذا فني عنِ الفناء، وخلَصَ مِنْ رؤية الإخلاص، تجلّى عليها بالرضا، وعفا عنْ كُلِّ ما مضى، وتبدَّلتُ سيّئاتها حسَناتٍ، وانفتح لها أبواب الأذواق والتجلياتِ، فصارت غريقة في بحارِ التَّوحيد، وآنستها بلابل الأسرار بالتغريد، ولذا سُمّيت مرضيّة (٢)؛ لأنها بعناياتِ الله مرعيّةً، وهي السادسة.
Conclusion on Sufism: But the vision of annihilation and sincerity may sometimes lead to something of self-admiration, so it withdraws backward. Let it seek refuge with Allah from that while continuing remembrance, turning to Allah, and observing that it cannot achieve salvation except through the support of the shaykh.

Then when it annihilates from annihilation and purifies from the vision of sincerity, it is manifested with satisfaction, forgiveness of all past, its evil deeds are transformed into good deeds, the doors of tastes and manifestations open for it, so it becomes drowned in the oceans of tawhid, and the nightingales of secrets entertain it with singing. Therefore it is called the pleasing soul (al-nafs al-mardiyya), because it is cared for by Allah's attentions, and it is the sixth.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage begins by warning that even the vision of annihilation and sincerity can lead to self-admiration, which causes regression. The seeker is advised to seek refuge and rely on the shaykh. Then it describes the sixth stage, where the soul annihilates from the very concept of annihilation, purifies from seeing its own sincerity, and is manifested with divine satisfaction. Evil deeds transform into good, and the soul experiences spiritual tastes and manifestations, becoming immersed in the ocean of tawhid. This is the pleasing soul (mardiyya), which is cared for by Allah.

Key Terms
مَرْضِيَّة (mardiyya)
فَنَاء (fana')
إِخْلَاص (ikhlas)
تَوْحِيد (tawhid)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sixth stage is achieved solely through personal effort and spiritual practices.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that salvation (al-khalas) is not achieved except through the support of the shaykh, and the stage is reached by divine care (bi'inayat Allah).

Checkpoint
What danger is associated with the vision of annihilation and sincerity?
A) It leads to disbelief
B) It may cause self-admiration
C) It makes one neglectful of dhikr
D) It weakens the connection with the shaykh

Key Takeaway
The sixth stage of the soul is the pleasing soul (nafs mardiyya), attained by divine care after purifying from the very vision of annihilation and sincerity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt proud of your spiritual efforts, like the vision of sincerity mentioned? How can you guard against that self-admiration that leads to regression? What specific practice from this passage can you implement today?
?
Do you rely on a spiritual guide or shaykh, or do you think you can achieve salvation alone? What is the passage saying about the necessity of support? How willing are you to submit to guidance?
?
The passage says that at the stage of the pleasing soul, even evil deeds are transformed into good deeds. Does your understanding of divine forgiveness include such a radical transformation? How should this change the way you view your past mistakes and your hope for the future?

The Seventh Stage: Return to Allah with High Aspiration
Describes the final stage beyond stations: return to Allah with aspiration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the final stage of the spiritual journey where the seeker of high aspiration moves beyond all stations to return to Allah and attain complete union.

Core Idea
The highest aspiration is to return to Allah, leaving all else behind.

This lesson presents the culmination of the spiritual path as described by Imam Dardir. Having traversed various stations, the seeker of high aspiration is not satisfied with any intermediate state but presses on toward the ultimate goal: complete return to Allah. The passage describes this journey from annihilation to subsistence and the honored reception that awaits the one who answers the divine call.

Guided Path
1
Understand the seeker's dissatisfaction
Notice that the one of high aspiration is not content even with lofty stations. They seek something beyond.
This sets the stage for the entire passage.
2
Trace the journey to subsistence
The seeker travels from annihilation (fana') to subsistence (baqa'), and then seeks complete union (wusul).
These are key spiritual terms.
3
Heed the warning and the call
The realities of the worlds warn not to be deceived, and then Allah calls the tranquil soul with the verse from Surah al-Fajr.
The call is a direct address from Allah.
4
Appreciate the final honor
The seeker is entered into Paradise, given robes of contentment, and seated near the King.
This is the ultimate reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۷ - إلّا أنَّ صاحبَ الهِمَةِ العليّةِ، لا يرضى بالوقوف عند هذه المقامات وإن كانت سنيّة، بلْ يسيرُ مِنَ الفناء إلى البقاء، ويطلُبُ وصْلَ الوصْلِ بتمام اللقاء، فتناديه حقائقُ الأكوان إنما نحن فتنة فلا تكفُرْ، وأنَّ إلى ربِّكَ المنتهى.

فإذا سار إلى منازل الأبطال، وخلَّفَ الدُّنيا وراء ظهره، ناداه ربُّه بأحسن مقال يأَيَّتُهَا النَّفْسُ الْمُطْمَئَةُ : ارْجِعِي إِلَى رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةٌ مَّرْضِيَّةً * فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَادِي وَادْخُلِي جَنَّتِي ) (۳) فيُدْخِلُها ربُّها في عِبادِ الإحْسانِ، ويَخْلَعُ عليها خَلَعَ الرّضوانِ، ويُدْخِلُها جنّاتِ الشُّهود، ويُجلِسُها في مقْعَدِ صِدْقٍ عِندَ الملك المعبودِ.
7 - But the one of high aspiration is not satisfied with stopping at these stations, even if they are high; rather he travels from annihilation to subsistence, and seeks the union of union with complete meeting. The realities of the worlds call out to him: 'We are but a trial, so do not disbelieve, and to your Lord is the final destination.'

When he travels to the abodes of champions and leaves the world behind him, his Lord calls him with the best speech: 'O tranquil soul, return to your Lord, satisfied and pleasing, and enter among My servants and enter My Paradise.' So his Lord enters him into the servants of excellence, bestows upon him the robes of contentment, enters him into the gardens of witnessing, and seats him in a seat of truth near the Sovereign, the Worshipped.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage describes the ultimate stage for those with high aspiration (himma). They do not rest content with even lofty stations but move from annihilation (fana') to subsistence (baqa'), seeking complete union. The realities of the created worlds warn them not to be deceived. When they leave the world completely, Allah calls them with the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Fajr, addressing the tranquil soul to return. They are then honored among the servants of excellence, given robes of contentment, and seated in a seat of truth near the King.

Key Terms
هِمَّة (himmah)
بَقَاء (baqa')
فَنَاء (fana')
وَصْل (wusul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Anyone who follows the spiritual path will automatically reach the final return to Allah without special effort.
Correction: The text emphasizes that only the one of high aspiration who completely abandons worldly stations and travels from annihilation to subsistence attains this stage.

Checkpoint
What does the one of high aspiration seek beyond the earlier stations?
A) To stay in the station of annihilation
B) To travel from annihilation to subsistence and seek complete union
C) To become a shaykh
D) To accumulate spiritual knowledge

Key Takeaway
The seeker of high aspiration travels from annihilation to subsistence, answers the divine call, and is honored with entry into Paradise and a seat near the King.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truly content with the spiritual progress you have made, or do you feel an ache in your soul that nothing but the Lord Himself can satisfy? What would it take for you to leave every station and achievement behind and pursue only His face?
?
What worldly attachments—positions, relationships, comforts—are you still holding onto that silence the call 'Return to your Lord' in your heart? Name one specific thing you can release today to hear that call more clearly.
?
When you imagine being seated 'in a seat of truth near the Sovereign, the Worshipped,' does your heart leap with longing, or does it shrink in fear? What is holding you back from making that return the single passion of your life starting now?

The Fifth and Sixth Stages: The Contented and Well-Pleasing Soul
Describes the fifth and sixth stages of the soul with warnings and remedies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the fifth and sixth stages of the soul in Sufi terminology and the spiritual dangers one might encounter in these stations.

Core Idea
True spiritual progress requires annihilation of even the awareness of one's own sincerity.

This passage from Imam Dardir's commentary takes us into the advanced stations of the soul. After describing the earlier stages, he now presents the fifth and sixth stations, where the soul attains contentment and becomes well-pleasing to Allah. However, he also warns about a subtle danger: even after reaching annihilation and sincerity, one may fall into self-admiration. Let us explore these final stages and the path to true spiritual realization.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the names of the stages and the description of their characteristics.
2
Identify the two stages
Find where the fifth stage (rāḍiya) is described and where the sixth stage (marḍiyya) is described. Note the transition and the warning about self-admiration.
3
Understand the danger of self-admiration
The text warns that even after attaining annihilation (fanā') and sincerity (ikhlāṣ), one may be overtaken by self-admiration. Why is this dangerous? The text explains it causes regression.
4
Reflect on the remedy
The passage offers a remedy: continuous remembrance (dhikr), seeking refuge in Allah, and reliance on the shaykh. Consider why these are necessary.
5
Appreciate the outcome
When one transcends self-admiration, Allah manifests contentment, transforms evil deeds to good, and opens spiritual tastes. This is the state of the soul in the sixth stage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مِنْ غَيْرِ اعتراض أصلا، سُمّيت راضية وهي الخامسة. خاتمة في التصوف. ولكن رؤية الفناء والإخلاص ربّما أوقعَ في شَيْءٍ مِنَ الإِعْجَابِ، فيرجع به القهقرى، فليستعذ باللهِ مِنْ ذلك معَ مُداوَمَةِ الذِّكْرِ والالتجاء إلى اللهِ ومُلاحظة أنه لا يتم له الخلاص إلا بمدَدِ الشَّيخِ. فإذا فني عنِ الفناء، وخلَصَ مِنْ رؤية الإخلاص، تجلّى عليها بالرضا، وعفا عنْ كُلِّ ما مضى، وتبدَّلتُ سيّئاتها حسَناتٍ، وانفتح لها أبواب الأذواق والتجلياتِ، فصارت غريقة في بحارِ التَّوحيد، وآنستها بلابل الأسرار بالتغريد، ولذا سُمّيت مرضيّة؛ لأنها بعناياتِ الله مرعيّةً، وهي السادسة.
Without any objection at all, it is called the contented soul, and it is the fifth. Conclusion on Sufism. But the vision of annihilation and sincerity may sometimes cause something of self-admiration, so he retreats backwards. So let him seek refuge with Allah from that while continuing remembrance, seeking refuge in Allah, and observing that he cannot attain deliverance except through the support of the shaykh. When he becomes annihilated from annihilation, and purifies from the vision of sincerity, He manifests Himself to him with contentment, and pardons all that has passed, and his evil deeds are transformed into good deeds, and the doors of spiritual tastes and unveilings are opened for him, so he becomes drowned in the seas of divine unity, and the nightingales of secrets cheer him with their singing. Therefore it is called the well-pleasing soul; because it is cared for by Allah's favors, and it is the sixth.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a continuation describing the stages of the soul, specifically the fifth (rāḍiya) and sixth (marḍiyya). It begins by stating that the fifth stage is called contented because it involves no objection. Then a new section, 'Conclusion on Sufism', warns that even after attaining annihilation and sincerity, one may fall into self-admiration, which causes regression. The remedy is to persist in dhikr, rely on Allah, and depend on the shaykh's spiritual support. When one becomes annihilated from the very awareness of annihilation and purifies from seeing his own sincerity, Allah manifests contentment, forgives past sins, transforms them into good deeds, and opens spiritual tastes and unveilings. The soul becomes immersed in tawḥīd and is called marḍiyya because it is under Allah's care. This is the sixth stage.

Key Terms
راضية
مرضية
فناء
إخلاص
تجلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that spiritual stages are attained by personal effort alone.
Correction: The text emphasizes that reliance on Allah and the shaykh's support are essential, and that self-admiration can negate progress.

Checkpoint
What is the prescribed remedy for the danger of self-admiration after annihilation?
A) Increasing asceticism
B) Continuing remembrance, seeking refuge in Allah, and relying on the shaykh's support
C) Isolating oneself completely
D) Abandoning all spiritual practices

Key Takeaway
The fifth and sixth stages represent the soul's attainment of contentment and being well-pleasing, but only after overcoming the subtle trap of self-admiration through reliance on Allah and the shaykh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt proud of your own sincerity or devotion? How does the warning that even the 'vision of annihilation and sincerity' can cause self-admiration expose a hidden pride in your spiritual life? What specific step will you take today to seek refuge in Allah from that pride?
?
The text promises that for the contented soul, evil deeds are transformed into good deeds. Is there a sin from your past that still weighs on you? Will you accept that Allah can transform it, and then release the shame to Him? What would it mean for you to live as if that transformation has already happened?
?
Why does the passage insist that you cannot attain deliverance except through the support of a shaykh? If you do not have a spiritual guide, what is preventing you from seeking one? How does your independence in spiritual matters actually hinder your progress?

The Seventh Stage: The Soul at Peace
Describes the seventh stage and the call of the soul at peace

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh stage of spiritual development, where the soul at peace returns to its Lord and attains the highest reward of divine proximity and witnessing.

Core Idea
The soul at peace returns to its Lord, well-pleased and pleasing.

This passage from Imam Dardir's commentary describes the culmination of the spiritual journey. The seeker of high aspiration moves beyond all stations, even the lofty ones, to reach the direct presence of God. The soul at peace is called back to its Lord and is granted the ultimate reward: nearness to the Divine and the vision of His beauty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the progression from high aspiration to the final reward.
2
Identify the key phases
Trace the journey: high aspiration → moving from fana to baqa → warning of cosmic realities → call of the soul at peace → reward of divine pleasure and gardens of witnessing.
The warning 'We are but a trial' is a reminder not to become attached to creation.
3
Reflect on the soul at peace
Consider what it means for the soul to be well-pleased and well-pleasing. This is the state of complete harmony with the divine will.
4
Understand the final reward
The reward includes entering among the servants of excellence, robes of pleasure, gardens of witnessing, and a seat of truth near Allah. This is the highest station.
The 'gardens of witnessing' refer to direct vision of God in the hereafter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلّا أنَّ صاحبَ الهِمَةِ العليّةِ، لا يرضى بالوقوف عند هذه المقامات وإن كانت سنيّة، بلْ يسيرُ مِنَ الفناء إلى البقاء، ويطلُبُ وصْلَ الوصْلِ بتمام اللقاء، فتناديه حقائقُ الأكوان إنما نحن فتنة فلا تكفُرْ، وأنَّ إلى ربِّكَ المنتهى. فإذا سار إلى منازل الأبطال، وخلَّفَ الدُّنيا وراء ظهره، ناداه ربُّه بأحسن مقال يأَيَّتُهَا النَّفْسُ الْمُطْمَئَةُ : ارْجِعِي إِلَى رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةٌ مَّرْضِيَّةً * فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَادِي وَادْخُلِي جَنَّتِي ) فيُدْخِلُها ربُّها في عِبادِ الإحْسانِ، ويَخْلَعُ عليها خَلَعَ الرّضوانِ، ويُدْخِلُها جنّاتِ الشُّهود، ويُجلِسُها في مقْعَدِ صِدْقٍ عِندَ الملك المعبودِ.
However, the possessor of high aspiration is not satisfied with stopping at these stations even if they are lofty, but rather he travels from annihilation to subsistence, and seeks the union of union through complete meeting. So the realities of the cosmos call to him: 'We are but a trial, so do not disbelieve, and to your Lord is the final return.' When he travels to the stations of the heroes, and casts the world behind his back, his Lord calls him with the best speech: 'O soul at peace! Return to your Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing! So enter among My servants, and enter My Paradise.' So his Lord admits him among the servants of excellence, and clothes him with the robes of pleasure, and admits him into the gardens of witnessing, and seats him in a seat of truth near the Sovereign, the Worshipped.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage explains the transition from the lower stations to the highest. The person of high aspiration does not stop at even the lofty stations of rāḍiya and marḍiyya, but moves from fanā' (annihilation) to baqā' (subsistence in God). He seeks complete union. However, the realities of the cosmos warn him that they are but a trial, so he must not be distracted from God. When he leaves the world behind, Allah calls the 'soul at peace' (nafs muṭma'inna) to return to Him, content and pleasing. Then Allah admits him into the company of His excellent servants, bestows the robes of divine pleasure, and grants him entry into the gardens of direct witnessing, seating him in a seat of truth near God. This is the seventh stage (al-kāmila) described later.

Key Terms
همة عليّة
فناء
بقاء
وصل
نفس مطمئنة
جنة الشهود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The warning 'We are but a trial' might be interpreted as a command to reject or disbelieve in the created world entirely.
Correction: The warning is a caution against becoming attached to or distracted by creation; it does not mean one should disbelieve in its existence or its signs of God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the soul at peace hear when it returns to its Lord?
A) 'You have failed the test'
B) 'Return to your Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing'
C) 'You have attained perfection'
D) 'Enter the fire of purification'

Key Takeaway
The seventh stage culminates in the soul at peace returning to Allah, entering the gardens of witnessing, and being seated in truth near the King.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard the call 'O soul at peace'—but are you truly at peace with God's decree? Or is there a part of you that still resists His will? If you were called today to return, would you be 'well-pleased' with what you find?
?
The possessor of high aspiration does not stop even at lofty stations. What station in your life have you become complacent with—perhaps your current level of prayer, charity, or knowledge? Are you still striving for complete annihilation and subsistence in God, or have you settled for comfort in your religious practice?
?
The realities of the cosmos warn that they are but a trial. What worldly attachment—a relationship, a possession, a status—is still holding you back from casting the world entirely behind? When will you decide to leave it for the sake of the gardens of witnessing?

The Three Degrees of Certainty and Direct Witnessing
Explains the three degrees of certainty and the nature of witnessing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three degrees of certainty (ʿilm al-yaqīn, ʿayn al-yaqīn, ḥaqq al-yaqīn) and how direct witnessing of God is understood without incarnation or union, using the mirror analogy.

Core Idea
Certainty deepens from knowledge to direct witnessing, yet remains free of incarnation.

In this passage, Imam Dardīr explains the pinnacle of spiritual journey—the perfect soul and its ever-ascending witnessing. He distinguishes three levels of certainty that build upon each other: knowledge through proofs, direct vision, and witnessing God in all things. Crucially, this witnessing is not pantheistic; it is like seeing your face in a mirror without the face entering the mirror.

Guided Path
1
Understand the station of the perfect soul
Read the first part about the soul called 'al-kāmila' where attributes of perfection become natural. Notice that even this soul continues to ascend because the perfect accepts perfection.
This sets the context for the levels of certainty.
2
Identify the three degrees of certainty
Find the phrases 'ʿilm al-yaqīn', 'ʿayn al-yaqīn', and 'ḥaqq al-yaqīn' in the text. Understand the progression: rational proof, direct witnessing before everything, and witnessing in everything.
These are technical terms in Sufi epistemology.
3
Reflect on the mirror analogy
Examine the mirror analogy used to explain ḥaqq al-yaqīn. The author explicitly denies incarnation (ḥulūl) and union (ittiḥād). Consider how this guards against misunderstanding.
This analogy is key to avoiding pantheistic interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي هذا المقام قد تمتِ المُجاهَدةُ والمُكابَدةُ؛ لأنَّ صِفاتِ الكمالِ صارت لها طبعا وسجيّةً، وتُسَمّى النفْسُ فيه بالكاملة، وهي السابعة، وهي أعظمُ النُّفوس قدْرًا، وأكملها فخرًا، ومع ذلك لا ينقطعُ ترقيها أبدًا؛ لأنَّ الكامل يقبل الكمال، فَلَمْ تَزَلْ تترقى حتى تشهد الحقِّ تعالى قبل الأكوان. ومشاهدتُه تعالى قبلَ كُلِّ شَيءٍ هو المُسمّى عِندَهم بالمعاينة، وهذا هو عَينُ اليقين، بعد أن حازت علم اليقين، الذي هو معرفتُه تعالى بالبراهين، ثُمَّ حق اليقين، وهي مُشاهَدتُه تعالى في كُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِنْ غَير حُلولٍ ولا اتحاد، ولا اتصال ولا انفصال، كالمرآة ترى فيها وجهَكَ مِنْ غَيرِ حُلولِ الوَجْهِ فِيهَا وَلا اتحادِ، وَهَذَا مَشْهَدُ ذَوقِيَّ لَا يُدْرِكُهُ إلا أهله.
In this station, striving and hardship have been completed; because the attributes of perfection have become for it [the soul] natural and ingrained, and the soul in this state is called the perfect soul, and it is the seventh, and it is the greatest of souls in rank, and the most perfect in glory, yet its ascent never ceases; because the perfect accepts perfection, so it continues to ascend until it witnesses the Truth, exalted, before the cosmos. And witnessing Him, exalted, before everything is what is called among them direct vision (muʿāyana), and this is the essence of certainty (ʿayn al-yaqīn), after it has attained knowledge of certainty (ʿilm al-yaqīn), which is knowledge of Him, exalted, through proofs, then truth of certainty (ḥaqq al-yaqīn), which is witnessing Him, exalted, in everything without incarnation (ḥulūl) or union (ittiḥād), without connection or separation, like a mirror in which you see your face without the face's incarnation in it nor union, and this is a taste-witnessing (mashhad dhawqī) that none perceives except its people.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage defines the seventh stage (al-kāmila) and explains the three levels of certainty. It states that in this station, spiritual struggle is complete because perfection has become innate. The perfect soul is the greatest and most complete, yet it continues to ascend because perfection accepts further perfection. It keeps rising until it witnesses God before all things. This witnessing 'before everything' is called ʿayn al-yaqīn (the eye of certainty), which follows ʿilm al-yaqīn (knowledge through proofs). Then comes ḥaqq al-yaqīn (truth of certainty), which is witnessing God in all things without incarnation, union, connection, or separation. The author uses the analogy of a mirror: you see your face in it without the face entering the mirror. This is a direct experiential knowledge (dhawq) that only its true knowers understand.

Key Terms
كاملة
علم اليقين
عين اليقين
حق اليقين
معاينة
ذوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'witnessing God in everything' means God literally enters creation (pantheism).
Correction: The text explicitly denies incarnation (ḥulūl) and union (ittiḥād). The mirror analogy shows manifest reflection without physical presence.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to explain witnessing God without incarnation?
A) Water and ice
B) A mirror and a face
C) The sun and its rays
D) A seal and wax

Key Takeaway
Certainty deepens from rational proof to direct witnessing, culminating in seeing God in everything without incarnation, as in a mirror.
