The Perfect Soul: Constant Presence and Rare Attainment
Describes the state of the perfect soul and its rarity among seekers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics of the perfect soul and why achieving such a station is exceedingly rare.

Core Idea
Perfect souls are the rarest of the rare among believers.

In this passage, Imam Dardir describes the highest station of the perfect soul. Such a person never ceases worship, as it has become second nature—every movement is a good deed, every breath an act of worship. Yet he also warns that such perfect souls are extremely rare. Let us explore the nature of this station and understand its rarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Notice the flow from describing the perfect soul's constant worship to the quote and then the rarity statement.
2
Identify the three aspects of worship
The passage says worship is done with the tongue, heart, and limbs. Reflect on how all three become natural for the perfect soul.
This shows the comprehensive nature of their devotion.
3
Understand the rarity layers
The author lists three groups: few who journey to Allah, few who reach, and few who are perfect. This pyramid shows how rare the perfect soul is.
Use this to internalize the difficulty of the path.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصاحب هذا المقام لا يفتر عن العبادة؛ لأنها صارت طبعه، إما باللسان وإمّا بالجنان وإما بالأركان، فحركاته حسنات، وأنفاسه عبادات، ولذا قال سيدي مُحمَّدُ وفا أبو سيدي علي وفا رضي الله عنهما: وبعد الفنا بالله كن كيفما تشا * فعلمك لا جهل وفعلك لا وزر فهو محفوظ مِنَ الوُقوع في المخالفات لحضوره دائما مع الله في جميع الحالاتِ. واعلم أنَّ الكاملين في الناسِ مِنْ أقل الأقل، إذ السالكون إلى اللهِ تعالى مِنَ المؤمنين قليلون، والواصلون منهم قليلون والكاملون منهم قليلون، إذ السير إلى الله تعالى.
And the possessor of this station does not slacken in worship; because it has become his nature, whether with the tongue, heart, or limbs. So his movements are good deeds, and his breaths are acts of worship. For this reason, my master Muḥammad Wafā, the father of my master ʿAlī Wafā, may Allah be pleased with them, said: 'After annihilation in Allah, be however you wish, for your knowledge is free of ignorance and your act free of sin.' He is protected from falling into violations because of his constant presence with Allah in all states. And know that the perfect ones among people are the least of the least; for those who journey to Allah among the believers are few, and those who reach are few, and those who are perfect are few. Indeed, the journey to Allah is [arduous].
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage describes the state of the perfect soul (kāmila) at the highest station. Such a person never ceases worship, because it has become second nature—through speech, inner devotion, or physical acts. Every movement is a good deed, every breath is worship. The author quotes the Sufi master Muḥammad Wafā, who says that after annihilation in Allah, one is protected from sin and ignorance. This protection comes from constant presence with Allah. Then the author emphasizes the rarity: among believers, few are travelers on the path; among them, few reach the goal; and among those, few become perfect. The journey to Allah is difficult and few complete it.

Key Terms
كامل
حضور مع الله
محفوظ
قليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One may think that the perfect soul is sinless in a legal sense, like prophets.
Correction: The text says the perfect soul is 'protected from falling into violations' due to constant presence with Allah, not that it is infallible like prophets. It is a state of divine preservation, not inherent sinlessness.

Checkpoint
According to the text, how does the author describe the number of perfect souls among people?
A) They are the majority
B) They are the least of the least
C) They are about half
D) They are unknown

Key Takeaway
The perfect soul is one who is constantly present with Allah and protected from sin, yet such souls are the rarest of the rare—only a few journey, fewer reach, and fewer still become perfect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the perfect soul is as rare as the text describes, what does that say about your own spiritual journey? Are you even among the 'few who journey', or have you become complacent? What concrete step will you take today to begin or intensify your journey?
?
The passage says every movement and breath of the perfect soul is worship. Examine your last 24 hours: how many of your movements and breaths were truly worship? What does that gap reveal about your presence with Allah? Commit to one small habit to increase your awareness of Him.
?
The quote says after annihilation, one can 'be however you wish' because knowledge is free of ignorance and act free of sin. Are you willing to pursue that state, knowing it requires total surrender? What is the one attachment you are most afraid to let go of? Pray for the strength to release it.

The Rarity of the Perfected and the Difficulty of the Path
Imam Dardeer explains rarity of perfected and difficulty of path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the perfected are extremely rare and the severe difficulty of the spiritual path that only a few can traverse.

Core Idea
The path to perfection is arduous; only the very fewest achieve it.

Imam Dardeer offers a sobering perspective on the spiritual journey. He emphasizes that among believers, few even begin the path, fewer reach, and even fewer attain perfection. This is not meant to discourage but to highlight the magnitude of sincere effort required. In this passage, he names the obstacles and quotes a poignant verse that captures the peril.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall meaning, then read the English translation. Notice the emphasis on rarity and difficulty.
The language is strong: 'the very fewest of the few.'
2
Identify the stages of rarity
The passage lists three layers: few travelers, few who reach, few perfected. Write them down and note why each group is small.
The ultimate perfection is rarest of all.
3
Reflect on the obstacles
What makes the path so difficult? Look at the words: arduous, high aspiration, perfect sincerity, abandoning attachments, deserts, perils. Consider how these apply to your own journey.
The path requires leaving behind what is familiar and comfortable.
4
Analyze the poetic verse
The verse describes a journey to a beloved (Su'ad). Identify the symbols: mountains, death-threats, barefoot, no mount, empty hand, terrifying road. How does this mirror the spiritual path?
The verse summarizes human helplessness without divine aid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنَّ الكاملين في الناسِ مِنْ أقل الأقل، إذ السالكون إلى اللهِ تعالى مِنَ المؤمنين قليلون، والواصلون منهم قليلون والكاملون منهم قليلون، إذ السير إلى الله تعالى خاتمة: في التصوف مت جدا لا يقدر عليه إلا ذو همة علية وصدق كامل، إذ ترك المألوفاتِ مِنَ الطعام المال وحُبِّ الجاهِ وسائرِ الشهواتِ لا يقدِرُ عليه إلا القليلُ مِنَ الأبطال، والمنام وجمع والطريق فيها مفاوزُ ومهلكات، فالناجي فيها قليل، ولذا قيلَ: كيف الوصول إلى سُعاد ودونَها * قُلَلُ الجِبالِ وبينَهُنَّ حُتوفُ والرّجُلُ حافية وما لي مركب * واليد صفر والطريق مخوف
And know that the perfected ones among people are the very fewest of the few. Indeed, those who travel to Allah Most High from among the believers are few, and those who reach are few, and the perfected among them are few. Indeed, the journey to Allah Most High, conclusion on tasawwuf, is very arduous; none can undertake it except one of high aspiration and perfect sincerity. Indeed, abandoning customary habits of food, wealth, love of status, and all other desires—only a few of the champions can do it. And sleep and gathering? and the path contains deserts and perils, so the one saved in it is few. Therefore, it was said: 'How to reach Su'ad? Between her and me are mountain peaks, and between them are death-threats. The man is barefoot, and I have no mount, and my hand is empty, and the road is terrifying.'
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage warns about the extreme rarity of those who reach perfection. The author states that the perfected are the very fewest of the few. Few believers travel the path, few reach, and few become perfect. The journey to Allah is extremely difficult; only those with high aspiration and perfect sincerity can undertake it. Abandoning worldly attachments like food, wealth, and status is possible only for a few heroic souls. The path is full of deserts and perils, so few are saved. The author quotes a poetic verse that laments the difficulty of reaching the beloved (Su'ad), symbolizing the spiritual goal. The path is perilous, the traveler is unprovided, and the road is frightening.

Key Terms
al-kamilun
salikun
al-mu'minun
mujahada
tark al-ma'lufat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rarity of the perfected implies that spiritual perfection is unattainable or that one should despair.
Correction: The rarity does not indicate impossibility but stresses the need for sincere effort, high aspiration, and reliance on Allah. The path is difficult but not inaccessible; it requires complete dedication.

Checkpoint

A) Because they are naturally gifted
B) Because the path to Allah is extremely difficult and requires high aspiration
C) Because they are not interested
D) Because Allah does not grant perfection to many

Key Takeaway
The path to spiritual perfection is extremely difficult, requiring high aspiration and sincere effort, and only the very fewest achieve it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The poet describes being barefoot, empty-handed, on a terrifying road. Does this reflect your own spiritual state? If not, what comforts are you relying on that may actually be obstacles?
?
The path requires high aspiration and perfect sincerity. Look at your daily actions: is your aspiration high enough to sacrifice your love of status or comfort? What would it mean for you to have perfect sincerity in even one small deed today?

Balancing Fear and Hope in Health and Illness
Imam Dardeer instructs on balancing fear and hope in health and illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a believer should balance fear of Allah and hope in His mercy, and why this balance shifts between health and illness.

Core Idea
Fear and hope are like two wings; both are necessary, but which dominates depends on your state.

Imam Dardeer offers a profound spiritual instruction on the relationship between fear and hope. He uses a powerful analogy to show that both are essential, yet their proportions change according to our circumstances. This lesson unpacks that wisdom, showing how the balance between khawf and raja' guides the believer on their journey to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic verse and its commentary, then the literal translation. Let the author's words sink in before analysis.
Notice how the verse itself commands making fear prevail over hope.
2
Understand the analogy of the two wings
Imam Dardeer explains that fear and hope are like a bird's two wings. Reflect on why both are needed for spiritual flight.
If one wing is lost, the bird falls. So neither fear nor hope can be abandoned.
3
Note the instruction for health
In health, fear should dominate over hope. The author compares fear to a whip that drives one to worship and purifies the heart.
This is not a permanent state but a tool for self-discipline.
4
Note the instruction for illness
When illness comes and death approaches, hope should prevail over fear, because one is arriving at the Generous Lord.
Hope here is grounded in Allah's mercy, not denial of reality.
5
Reflect on the wisdom of the shift
Consider why the balance changes. Fear motivates action in strength; hope comforts in weakness. Both are needed, but at different times.
This teaches that spiritual states are dynamic, not static.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٠ - وغلّب الخَوفَ على الرجاءِ * وسَرْ مَولاكَ بِلا تَناءِ (وغلّب) في حال اشتغالِكَ بالذَّكر المذكور (الخَوفَ) مِنَ اللهِ تعالى ما دُمتَ في حال الصحة (على الرجاء) في رحمته وعفوه). يُريد أنه لا بُدَّ للعَبدِ مِنَ الخَوفِ والرجاء معا؛ لأنهما كجَناحَي الطائر، متى فَقَدَ أحدهما سقَطَ، إلا أنه في حال الصحة والسلامة ينبغي تغليب جانب الخوف على جانب الرجاء؛ لأنه كالسوط ينساقُ به إلى الاعتناء بالعبادة، وبه تزولُ الرعوناتُ النفسية عن القلب إنْ شاءَ اللهُ تعالى. فإذا نزل به المَرَضُ وأَشْرَفَ على الموتِ فينبغي تغليب جانبِ الرجاء على الخَوفِ؛ لأنه حالُ القدوم على الكريم.
60 - And make fear prevail over hope, and journey to your Lord without distance. (He says) 'make fear prevail' in the case of your engagement in the aforementioned remembrance (the fear) of Allah Most High as long as you are in a state of health (over hope) in His mercy and forgiveness. He means that the servant must have both fear and hope together because they are like the two wings of a bird; if he loses one, he falls. Except that in a state of health and safety, the side of fear should be made to prevail over the side of hope because it is like a whip by which one is driven to attend to worship, and by it the psychic frivolities depart from the heart, if Allah wills. So if illness befalls him and he is on the verge of death, he should make the side of hope prevail over fear because that is the state of arriving at the Generous One.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage gives a spiritual instruction on balancing fear (khawf) and hope (raja'). The author comments on the verse: 'Make fear prevail over hope, and journey to your Lord without distance.' He explains that during health, one should give preponderance to fear of Allah over hope for mercy. This is because fear acts like a whip that drives the servant to engage in worship and purifies the heart from frivolities. However, when illness comes and death approaches, one should make hope prevail over fear, because that is the state of arriving before the Generous Lord. The author emphasizes that both fear and hope are necessary, like the two wings of a bird; losing one causes a fall. The balance shifts based on one's spiritual and physical state.

Key Terms
khawf
raja'
dhikr
'ibada
mawt
al-karim

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One should abandon fear entirely when ill and only have hope.
Correction: The passage says hope should prevail, but fear remains present; both are necessary. The emphasis shifts, not the presence.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use for the necessity of both fear and hope?
A) Two wings of a bird
B) Two sides of a coin
C) Two pillars of a building
D) Two oars of a boat

Key Takeaway
A believer must maintain both fear and hope, with fear driving worship in health and hope comforting in illness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your current state of health, are you using the 'whip' of fear to drive you to worship, or has comfort led to complacency? What is one specific act of obedience you have been neglecting that you will recommit to starting today?
?
When you face illness or a trial, do your thoughts lean toward despair or a false sense of security? How will you actively strengthen your hope in Allah's generosity today, while honestly acknowledging your shortcomings?
?
Both fear and hope require intentional balancing. Which of these two 'wings' is weaker in your spiritual life right now? Name one concrete step you will take before the day ends to strengthen that wing.

The True Meaning of Gratitude (Shukr)
Dardeer defines shukr as directing all blessings to their intended purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive definition of gratitude to Allah as encompassing belief, action, and speech.

Core Idea
Gratitude is using every blessing for its intended purpose.

Gratitude is often misunderstood as mere verbal thanks. However, classical scholars like Imam Dardeer teach that true gratitude involves the heart, the limbs, and the tongue. This lesson unpacks that comprehensive definition from the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how the author defines shukr as directing all blessings to their purpose.
2
Identify the three components
The author mentions belief (i'tiqad), service (khidma), and speech (nutq). Find these in the text.
3
Understand outward and inward blessings
The passage distinguishes between outward blessings (hearing, sight) and inward blessings (faith, knowledge). Reflect on why both are included.
4
Apply the lesson
Think of one blessing from Allah and ask yourself: Am I using it for its intended purpose?

The second: gratitude to the Benefactor, Majestic and Exalted, which is: the servant's directing all that Allah has bestowed upon him, such as intellect, hearing, sight, tongue, and others, to that for which they were created. And to it he pointed in his saying: 62 - And be grateful for His bounties, and be patient in His trial. 'And be grateful for His bounties' (آلائه) is plural of 'ilan' (إلَى) like 'zabi' (ظبي), meaning blessing, i.e., be grateful for His blessings which He has bestowed upon you, whether outward like hearing, sight, and soundness of limbs, or inward like faith and knowledge. Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the second topic in the conclusion on Sufism: gratitude (shukr) to the Benefactor (Allah). The author defines shukr as using all the blessings Allah has given—intellect, hearing, sight, tongue, etc.—for their intended purpose. He then explains the poetic line 'And be grateful for His bounties, and be patient in His trial.' The word 'آلائه' means blessings, both outward (like senses and health) and inward (like faith and knowledge). 'شكورا' (grateful) means abundant gratitude, which the author explains as comprising three elements: belief in the heart that all blessings come from Allah, service with the limbs, and speech with the tongue. The passage ends incomplete at the bottom of the page, but the intended meaning is clear: the servant should acknowledge that no blessing exists except from Allah.

The Three Dimensions of Gratitude to the Benevolent
Defines gratitude as using blessings in their intended purposes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive nature of gratitude (shukr) as encompassing belief, speech, and action, and its endless depth according to the Sufi perspective.

Core Idea
True gratitude involves the whole person: heart, tongue, and limbs.

Gratitude is often thought of as merely saying 'thank you'. However, in Islamic theology, it is far deeper—it is the proper use of every blessing from Allah. This passage from Imam Dardir explains that gratitude has three essential dimensions: inner conviction, verbal acknowledgment, and physical obedience. It also reveals that true gratitude is rare and infinite, as even the ability to be grateful is a gift from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of shukr
Read the definition carefully: shukr is directing all of Allah's blessings—both outward (hearing, sight, limbs) and inward (faith, knowledge)—towards the purposes for which they were created.
2
Identify the three dimensions
Notice how the author breaks gratitude into three categories: belief in the heart (i'tiqad), speech with the tongue (nutq), and action with the limbs (amal). Each dimension must be present.
These correspond to the three types of servitude mentioned in the passage.
3
Reflect on the conclusion about endless gratitude
The passage concludes that gratitude is infinite and that even the ability to repent and be grateful is itself a blessing. Contemplate the hadith and verse about the rarity of true shukr.
This highlights the importance of seeking Allah's help (tawfiq) to be truly grateful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: شُكرُ المُنعِم جلَّ وعزَّ، وهو: صرفُ العبدِ جميع ما أَنْعَمَ الله به عليه، مِنْ عقل وسمْعِ وبَصَرٍ ولِسَانٍ وغَيْرِها، إلى ما خُلِقَ لأَجْلِه، وإليه أشار بقوله: وكُنْ على آلائه شَكورا * وكُنْ على بلائه صبورا. وكُنْ على آلائه) جمع «أني» كـ «ظَبي»، بمعنى النعمة، أي: كُنْ على نعمائه التي أنعمها عليك، ظاهريّةً كانتْ كالسمع والبصر وسلامة الأعضاء، أو باطنيّة، كالإيمان والعلم، (شكورا) أي: كثير الشكر، فهو يرجع إلى اعتقادِ بالجَنانِ، وخدمةٍ بالأركان، ونُطْقَ باللسان، بأنْ يعتقد أنْ لا نعمة إلا منه تعالى، وينطق بلسانه بأنه لا إله إلا هو، وبغيرِه مِنَ الأذكار، ويعمَلَ بجَوارِحِه كُلَّ ما واجبة كانت أو مندوبة. خاتمة : في التصوف طُلِبَ مِنْهُ مِنَ المأموراتِ، ومِنَ النعم التي يجبُ الشَّكرُ عليها التوفيق للتّوبة، والشُّكْرُ على الشُّكْرِ، فَالشَّكْرُ لا نهاية له، ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام (سُبْحانَكَ لا تُحصي ثناء عليك أنت كما ثبت على نفْسِك))، والشُّكْرُ بهذا الاعتبار عزيز جدا؛ لأنه طَريقُ الصِّدِّيقين، ولذا قال تعالى: ﴿وَقَلِيلٌ مِّنْ عِبَادِيَ الشَّكُورُ﴾
The second: Gratitude to the Benefactor, Majestic and Exalted, and it is: the servant turning all that Allah has bestowed upon him, from intellect, hearing, sight, tongue, and others, to that for which they were created. And to it he alluded by his saying: 'And be grateful for His favors, and be patient upon His trial.' 'And be grateful for His favors' (آلائه) is the plural of 'أني' like 'ظبي', meaning blessing. That is, be grateful for His blessings which He has bestowed upon you, whether outward like hearing, sight, and soundness of limbs, or inward like faith and knowledge. 'Shakūran' i.e., abundantly grateful, for it returns to belief in the heart, service with the limbs, and speech with the tongue: that he believes that no blessing is except from Him the Exalted, and speaks with his tongue that there is no god but He, and with other remembrances, and acts with his limbs everything commanded, whether obligatory or supererogatory. Conclusion: On Sufism: what is required of him from the commanded acts, and among the blessings for which gratitude is obligatory is the success (tawfīq) for repentance, and gratitude upon gratitude. So gratitude has no end. Therefore he (peace and blessings upon him) said: 'Glory be to You, I cannot enumerate praise upon You; You are as You have established upon Yourself.' And gratitude in this consideration is very rare, because it is the path of the truthful. Hence the Exalted said: 'And few of My servants are grateful.'
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines gratitude (shukr) as directing all blessings—both outward (hearing, sight, limbs) and inward (faith, knowledge)—to their intended purposes. The author explains that gratitude involves three aspects: inner belief (that all blessings come from Allah), verbal acknowledgment (saying La ilaha illallah and other dhikr), and bodily action (performing obligations and supererogatory acts). Then, in a brief 'Conclusion on Sufism', he highlights that even the ability to repent is a blessing requiring gratitude, and that gratitude upon gratitude is endless, citing a hadith and a Quranic verse to emphasize its rarity.

شكر
نعمة
توفيق
ثناء

Correction: The passage shows gratitude must also include heartfelt belief and physical action.

C) Three: belief, speech, and action
D) Four: intellect, hearing, sight, tongue

Key Takeaway
Gratitude is a comprehensive act of heart, tongue, and limbs, and even that is only possible through Allah's help.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
True gratitude is rare ('few of My servants are grateful'). Be honest: are you among the few? What would need to change in your daily routine for your heart, tongue, and limbs to consistently reflect shukr? Write down one concrete action.

Definition of Ridha and the Call to Submission
Dardeer defines ridha and explains a verse commanding submission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual station of ridha (contentment) as defined by Imam Dardeer, and how it involves active submission to God's decrees without objection.

Core Idea
True contentment is leaving your will for God's will.

Imam Dardeer now defines the fourth station on the spiritual path: ridha, or contentment. This station is not passive resignation but an active turning away from one's own desires to embrace the pleasure of Allah. The accompanying verse urges the seeker to be fully submitted to God in all matters. In this lesson, we will unpack this definition and its implications for the believer's life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Note the concise definition and the poet's command.
2
Understand the definition of ridha
Identify the core phrase: 'exiting from one's own pleasure by entering into the pleasure of his Lord'. Notice the two actions: submission (taslim) and entrustment (tafwid).
This is the heart of the lesson.
3
Reflect on submission without objection
Consider what it means to be pleased with God's decrees without turning away or objecting. How does this relate to the promise of safety from afflictions?
The verse ends with 'so that you may be safe'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٤ - فكُنْ لَهُ مُسلّما كن تسلَما * واتبع سبيل الناسكين العلما والرابع: الرضا، وهو: الخروجُ عنْ رِضا نفسه بالدخول في رِضا ربِّه، بالتسليم للأحكام الأزلية، والتفويض للتدبيرات الأبدية، بلا إعراض ولا اعتراض. وإليه أشار بقوله مُفرّعًا على ما قبله (فكُنْ) أَيُّها الطالب لرضا مولاه، (له) تعالى والتسليم (مُسَلَّما) في كُلِّ ما قَدَّرَه وقضاه، أو أَمَرَ بِهِ مِنْ أحكام الدين أو نهى عنه، بأن ترضى بذلك مِنْ غَيْرِ إعْراض أو اعتراض، (كي) أَيْ: لَأَجَلِ أَنَّ (تسْلَما) مِنْ آفَاتِ الدُّنيا والآخرة.
64 - So be submitted to Him, and you will be safe, and follow the path of the devout scholars. And the fourth: contentment (al-riḍā), which is: exiting from one's own pleasure by entering into the pleasure of his Lord, by submission to the eternal decrees, and entrusting to the everlasting arrangements, without turning away or objecting. And he pointed to it by his saying, branching from what preceded: 'So be' – O seeker of your Lord's pleasure – 'submitted' to Him, exalted, in everything that He has determined and decreed, or commanded of religious rulings or prohibited, by being pleased with that without turning away or objecting, 'so that' you may 'be safe' from the afflictions of this world and the Hereafter.

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth station, ridha (contentment). The author first quotes the verse urging submission to God. The definition is then given: ridha is leaving one's own pleasure to enter into God's pleasure, through submission to eternal decrees and entrustment to everlasting arrangements, without turning away or objecting. The author then explains that the verse 'so be submitted' refers to this: the seeker must be submitted to God in everything He has decreed or commanded or prohibited, by being pleased with it without objection, in order to be safe from afflictions.

?

The Station of Al-Rida (Satisfaction)
Definition of al-rida with verse interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual station of al-rida (satisfaction) as defined by Imam Dardir, including its meaning and the importance of submission to divine decrees.

Core Idea
True satisfaction is abandoning your own will for your Lord's.

In the journey of spiritual purification, the seeker reaches a station where personal desires are replaced by complete contentment with Allah's will. This lesson explores al-rida, defined by Imam Dardir as exiting one's own satisfaction to enter into the Lord's satisfaction through submission and trust. The accompanying verse from the poem reinforces this concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's definition and explanation sink in.
The passage includes a definition and a verse interpretation.
2
Identify the key components of rida
Look for the elements: exiting one's own satisfaction, entering into the Lord's satisfaction, submission to eternal decrees, entrusting everlasting arrangements, and the absence of turning away or objection.
These components form the core of the station.
3
Understand the purpose
The verse explains that being submissive leads to safety from afflictions. Reflect on how rida brings peace and protection.
4
Reflect on application
Consider how you can practice rida in your daily life, especially in accepting divine decrees and following religious rulings without complaint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٤ - فكُنْ لَهُ مُسلّما كن تسلما * واتبع سبيل الناسكين العلما
والرابع: الرضا، وهو: الخروجُ عنْ رِضا نفسه بالدخول في رِضا ربِّه، بالتسليم للأحكام الأزلية، والتفويض للتدبيرات الأبدية، بلا إعراض ولا اعتراض. وإليه أشار بقوله مُفرّعًا على ما قبله (فكُنْ) أَيُّها الطالب لرضا مولاه، (له) تعالى والتسليم (مُسَلَّما) في كُلِّ ما قَدَّرَه وقضاه، أو أَمَرَ بِهِ مِنْ أحكام الدين أو نهى عنه، بأن ترضى بذلك مِنْ غَيْرِ إعْراض أو اعتراض، (كي) أَيْ: لَأَجَلِ أَنَّ (تسْلَما) مِنْ آفَاتِ الدُّنيا والآخرة.
64. So be to Him submissive, you will be safe, and follow the path of the devout scholars.
The fourth: al-rida (satisfaction), which is: exiting from one's own satisfaction by entering into the satisfaction of one's Lord, through submission to the eternal decrees and entrusting to the everlasting arrangements, without turning away or objection. And to it he alluded by his statement, branching from what preceded: "So be (فكُنْ) O seeker of your Lord's satisfaction, to Him (له) the Exalted and submission (مُسَلَّما) in everything He has predestined and decreed, or commanded of religious rulings or prohibited, by being satisfied with that without turning away or objection, so that (كي) i.e., in order that (تسْلَما) you may be safe from the afflictions of this world and the Hereafter."
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth station in the spiritual path: al-rida (divine satisfaction). The author defines rida as abandoning one's own will and satisfaction in favor of the Lord's satisfaction. This is achieved by submitting to the eternal decrees (al-ahkaam al-azaliyya) and entrusting the everlasting arrangements (al-tadbiiraat al-abadiyya) to Allah without aversion or protest. The verse (from the earlier poem) "So be to Him submissive, you will be safe" is interpreted as a command to the seeker to be completely surrendered in all matters of predestination and legislation, both commands and prohibitions, and to be content with whatever comes, in order to gain safety from worldly and otherworldly afflictions.

Key Terms
الرضا
التسليم
التفويض
الأحكام الأزلية
التدبيرات الأبدية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-rida means passive resignation without any effort or action.
Correction: The passage defines rida as active submission and entrustment to Allah's decrees and commands, which includes obeying religious duties and prohibitions, not mere passivity.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of al-rida according to the passage?
A) Exiting from one's own satisfaction to enter into the satisfaction of one's Lord
B) Increasing one's worship and devotion
C) Acquiring knowledge of the divine essence
D) Following a spiritual guide

Key Takeaway
Al-rida is the station where one's will aligns with Allah's will through submission to His eternal decrees, leading to safety in both worlds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your life are you still clinging to your own satisfaction rather than Allah's, even when you know what He wants? What is one decree you need to submit to right now, and what practical step will you take today to practice that submission?
?
Do you ever internally object to any of Allah's religious rulings or prohibitions? If so, how can you cultivate the station of al-rida that requires being satisfied with them without turning away or objection?
?
What is the 'safety from afflictions' you most need right now—peace in your heart, protection from a trial, or something else? Are you truly convinced that al-rida—exiting from your own satisfaction into your Lord's—is the only path to that safety? If you are, what is holding you back from fully embracing it?

Necessity of Following a Verified Spiritual Guide
The author asserts the necessity of following a verified spiritual guide and lists his signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of seeking a qualified spiritual guide and recognize the signs of a true shaykh as outlined by Imam Dardhir.

Core Idea
Without a spiritual guide, one cannot ascend to Allah's proximity, no matter how much one worships.

Imam Dardhir continues describing the stations of the spiritual path. The fifth station is the necessity of attaching oneself to a verified guide (shaykh 'aarif) who has been trained in an unbroken chain back to the Prophet. Many believers underestimate the danger of spiritual self-reliance. In this passage, the author issues a stark warning and then provides practical signs to distinguish a true guide from a pretender.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without attempting analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
The passage is dense; take your time.

Notice that the passage first discusses the necessity of a guide and the danger of ignoring it, then lists the signs of a true shaykh. Mark these sections.
3
Reflect on the warning
Meditate on the saying: 'Whoever has no sheikh, his sheikh is Satan.' Consider why personal worship and knowledge are insufficient without a guide.
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.
4
Memorize the signs of a true shaykh
Write down the list of signs from the passage: generosity, good character, compassion, detachment from world, absence of pretension, not complaining, humility, and blessing on his companions.
These signs help discern a verified guide.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامِسُ : اتِّباعُ شَيخ عارف قد سلك طريقَ أَهْلِ اللهِ على يدِ شَيخ كذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى رسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ومَنْ لم يصحب شيخا يدُله على الطريق إلى الله، واستقل بما عارف عِندَه مِنْ عبادة أو علم فقد تعرَّضَ لإغراء الشيطان له، ولهذا قيلَ: «مَنْ لا شَيخ له فالشَّيطانُ شَيخه». وبالجملةِ مَنْ لم يَسْلُكْ على يدِ شَيخ عارف فلا يُمكنه الترقي إلى منازلِ القُربِ) ولو أتى بعبادةِ الثَّقَلَين. وعلامته (۳): السَّخاءُ، وحُسنُ الخُلُقِ، والشفَقةُ على خَلْقِ الله تعالى، وعَدَمُ انكبابه على جمع الدُّنيا، وعدم الدعوى، ولو بالتكلّم بمُصطَلَحِ القَومِ إلا لأمْرِ اقتضى ذلك، وعدمُ الشكوى مِنْ ضيق الدُّنيا، أو مِنْ إعراض الناس عنه، وأنْ يُرى عليه مخايل الذُّلِّ والانكِسارِ وحُبِّ الخُمول، وأن تظهر على أصحابه البركةُ والصلاح.
The fifth: Following a sheikh who is an arif (gnostic), who has traversed the path of the people of Allah under the guidance of a sheikh similarly until it reaches the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And whoever does not accompany a sheikh who guides him to the path to Allah, and depends solely on what he possesses of worship or knowledge, has exposed himself to the temptation of Satan. Hence it is said: "Whoever has no sheikh, his sheikh is Satan." In brief, whoever does not travel under the guidance of a gnostic sheikh cannot ascend to the stations of proximity (to Allah), even if he performs the worship of both humans and jinn. And his signs: generosity, good character, compassion for Allah's creation, not focusing on accumulating worldly wealth, absence of pretension (da'wa) even when speaking the terminology of the people (of tasawwuf) except when necessary, not complaining about worldly hardships or people's disregard, that signs of humility, brokenness, and love of obscurity be seen on him, and that blessing and righteousness appear on his companions.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth station: following a verified spiritual guide (shaykh 'aarif). The author emphasizes that the guide must have himself been trained by a chain of masters reaching back to the Prophet. He warns that without such a guide, a person is vulnerable to Satan's deception, even if he possesses knowledge or worship. The well-known saying "Whoever has no sheikh, his sheikh is Satan" is quoted. The author then lists the signs of a true shaykh: he should be generous, good-natured, compassionate, detached from the world, free from self-claims, not complaining, humble, and his followers should show blessing and righteousness.

Correction: The passage declares that whoever does not follow a verified sheikh cannot ascend to the stations of nearness, even with the worship of both humans and jinn, and is vulnerable to Satan's deception.

Path of the Devout Scholars and the First Group of Later Scholars
Author explains 'path of devout scholars' and begins classification of later scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of 'the path of the devout scholars' and how later scholars are classified into groups, starting with the scholars of practical rulings.

Core Idea
The path of the righteous predecessors is creed, knowledge, and action.

This lesson unpacks the phrase 'follow the path of the devout scholars' from the earlier poem. The author explains who these devout scholars are and what their path consists of. Then he begins to classify the later imams who came after them, describing the first group: those who dedicated themselves to explaining the practical rulings of the Shariah.

Identify the three components of the path

4

The author mentions that later imams are divided into three groups, but only the first group is described here.
The text ends mid-sentence, so only the first group is mentioned.

And this is taken from our saying: "And follow in your journey the path of the devout (naasikeen, pl. of naasik, meaning worshipper) scholars ('ulama, pl. of 'aalim), i.e., the one knowledgeable of the Shar'i rulings upon which the soundness of the religion depends, whether creedal or practical." And what is meant by them is the righteous predecessors (salaf al-saalih) and those who followed them in goodness. Their path is confined to creed (i'tiqaad), knowledge ('ilm), and action ('amal) in accordance with knowledge. Then those who came after them from the Imams of the Ummah, whose following is beloved, are divided into three groups: a group that dedicated itself to explaining the practical Shar'i rulings — they are the four Imams and others among the mujtahids, but only the schools of the four Imams have become established as the accepted (mardiyya) schools.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage provides a gloss on the line from the earlier poem: "Follow the path of the devout scholars." The author explains that "devout" (naasikeen) means worshippers, and "scholars" ('ulama) means those who know the Shar'i rulings — both creedal and practical. By "them" he means the righteous predecessors (salaf) and their followers. Their path consists of three elements: correct creed, knowledge, and action according to knowledge. Then he classifies later imams into three groups. The passage mentions only the first group, which is the group dedicated to explaining practical rulings — these are the four Imams and other mujtahids, but among them only the four madhhabs have become established as the accepted schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The path of the devout scholars is simply following one of the four madhhabs.
Correction: The passage defines the path as consisting of correct creed, knowledge, and action; the four madhhabs are the established schools for practical rulings, but the path itself is broader.

Key Takeaway
The path of the devout scholars combines correct creed, knowledge, and action, and the later scholars are classified into groups, with the first being the four Imams who specialized in practical rulings.

The Necessity of a Spiritual Guide and Its Signs
Dardeer asserts necessity of a shaykh and lists his signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a qualified spiritual guide is essential for spiritual progress and what signs indicate a true guide.

Core Idea
Without a guide, Satan becomes your shaykh.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer emphasizes the critical role of a qualified spiritual guide (shaykh) in the path to Allah. He warns against self-reliance and describes the signs that distinguish a true guide from a pretender.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on necessity
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the strong warning about not having a shaykh.
The saying 'No shaykh, Satan is his shaykh' is key.
2
Identify the consequence
What happens to someone who does not accompany a shaykh? The text says he exposes himself to Satan's deception.
3
Examine the signs of a true shaykh
The passage lists several signs: generosity, good character, compassion, detachment, no pretension, no complaint, humility, and blessing on companions.
These signs help distinguish a genuine guide from a fake.
4
Reflect on the importance
Why are these signs important? They show that the shaykh is selfless and focused on Allah, not on worldly gain or status.
5
Connect to the broader theme
This lesson sets the foundation for understanding the necessity of following a chain of transmission in tasawwuf.
This leads into the next lesson about the elite groups.

الخامِسُ: اتِّباعُ شَيخٍ عارفٍ قد سلك طريقَ أَهْلِ اللهِ على يدِ شَيخٍ كذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى رسولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم، ومَنْ لم يصحب شيخاً يدُلُّه على الطريق إلى الله، واستقلَّ بما عنده مِنْ عبادةٍ أو علمٍ فقد تعرَّضَ لإغراء الشيطان له، ولهذا قيل: «مَنْ لا شَيخَ له فالشَّيطانُ شَيخُه». وبالجملةِ مَنْ لم يَسْلُكْ على يدِ شَيخٍ عارفٍ فلا يُمكنه الترقي إلى منازلِ القُربِ ولو أتى بعبادةِ الثَّقَلَين. وعلامتُهُ: السَّخاءُ، وحُسنُ الخُلُقِ، والشفَقةُ على خَلْقِ الله تعالى، وعَدَمُ انكبابه على جمع الدُّنيا، وعدمُ الدعوى، ولو بالتكلّم بمُصطَلَحِ القَومِ إلا لأمْرٍ اقتضى ذلك، وعدمُ الشكوى مِنْ ضيق الدُّنيا أو مِنْ إعراض الناس عنه، وأنْ يُرى عليه مخايل الذُّلِّ والانكِسارِ وحُبِّ الخُمول، وأن تظهر على أصحابه البركةُ والصلاح، وهذا مأخوذ من قولنا: (واتَّبَعْ) في سَيرِكَ ( سبيلَ) أي: طريقَ (الناسِكين) جمع «ناسك»، أي: عابد، (العُلَما) جمع «عالم»، وهو: العارفُ بالأحكام الشرعية التي عليها مدار صحة الدين، اعتقاديةً كانت أو عمليَّة، والمراد بهم السلف الصالحُ ومَنْ تبعهم بإحْسانٍ، وسبيلهم منحصر في اعتقادٍ وعِلْمٍ وعملٍ على طبق العِلْمِ. ومَنْ جاءَ بعدَهم مِنْ أئمّةِ الأُمَّةِ الذين يجب اتِّباعُهم على ثلاثِ فِرَقٍ: فرقةٌ نصَّبتْ نفسَها لبيان الأحكام الشرعية العملية، وهم الأئمة الأربعةُ وغيرُهم مِنَ المُجتهِدين، لكِنْ لم يستقِرَّ مِنَ المذاهبِ المَرْضِيَّةِ سوى مذاهب الأئمة الأربعة. وفرقةٌ نصَّبتْ نفسَها للاشتغال ببيان العقائد التي كان عليها السلف، وهم الأشعري والماتريدي ومَنْ تبعهما. وفرقةٌ نصَّبتْ نفسَها للاشتغال بالعَمَلِ والمجاهدات على طبق ما ذهب إليه الفرقتان المتقدمتان، وهم أبو القاسم الجنيد ومَنْ تبعه. فهؤلاء الفِرَقُ الثلاثةُ هُم خواصُّ الأُمَّةِ المحمدية، ومَنْ عداهم مِنْ جميعِ الفِرَقِ على ضلال، وإنْ كانَ البَعْضُ منهم يُحكَمُ له بالإسلام، فالناجي مَنْ كان في عقيدته على طبق ما بيَّنَه أهلُ السُّنَّة، وقلَّدَ في الأحكام العَمَلِيَّةِ إماماً مِنَ الأئمة الأربعةِ المرضيَّة، ثُمَّ تمامُ النِّعمةِ والنجاة في سُلوكِ مَسلكِ الجُنَيدِ وأتباعه بعدَ أَنْ أَحْكَمَ دينَه على طبق ما بيَّنَه الفريقان المتَقَدِّمان. ومَنْ سَلَكَ مَسلكَه القُطْبُ الربّانيُّ الإمام سيدي أحمدُ بنُ الرفاعي وأتباعه، والقطب الرباني الإمام سيدي عبد القادر الجيلاني وأتباعه، والقُطبُ الرباني السيد أحمد البدوي وأتباعه، والقُطبُ الرباني السيد إبراهيم الدسوقي وأتباعه، والقُطبُ الربانِيُّ السيدُ عليُّ أبو الحسن الشاذلي وأتباعه.
The fifth: Following a gnostic shaykh who has traveled the path of the people of Allah under the hand of a similar shaykh until he reaches the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Whoever does not accompany a shaykh who guides him to the path to Allah, and relies on what he himself has of worship or knowledge, has exposed himself to the deception of Satan for him, and for this it was said: 'He who has no shaykh, Satan is his shaykh.' In summary, whoever does not travel under the hand of a gnostic shaykh cannot ascend to the stations of proximity, even if he performs the worship of both thaqalayn (jinn and humans). And his sign: generosity, good character, compassion for Allah's creatures, not being preoccupied with accumulating worldly goods, absence of pretension—even by speaking in the terminology of the folk unless a matter necessitates it—absence of complaint about worldly hardship or people turning away from him, that one sees on him signs of humility, brokenness, and love of obscurity, and that blessing and righteousness appear on his companions. This is taken from our saying: 'And follow in your journey the path of the devotees (nāsikīn), plural of nāsik, i.e., worshipper, the scholars ('ulamā), plural of 'ālim, who is the knower of the legal rulings upon which the soundness of religion depends, whether creedal or practical. And by them is meant the righteous predecessors and those who follow them in excellence. Their path is comprised of creed, knowledge, and action in accordance with knowledge.' And those who came after them from the imams of the Ummah whose following is obligatory are three groups: A group that devoted itself to explaining the practical legal rulings—they are the four imams and others among the mujtahids, but only the schools of the four imams have become established among the approved schools. And a group that devoted itself to explaining the creeds which the predecessors held—they are al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi and those who follow them. And a group that devoted itself to spiritual practice and spiritual struggles (mujāhadāt) in accordance with what the two preceding groups held—they are Abu al-Qasim al-Junayd and those who follow him. These three groups are the elite of the Muhammadan Ummah. Whoever is other than them from all the sects is in error, even if some of them are judged to be Muslim. The saved person is the one whose creed is in accordance with what Ahl al-Sunnah explained, and who imitates in practical rulings an imam from the four approved imams. Then the completion of grace and salvation lies in traversing the path of al-Junayd and his followers after having perfected his religion in accordance with what the two preceding groups explained. And those who traveled his path: the supreme spiritual pole (quṭb), the imam, my master Ahmad ibn al-Rifa'i and his followers; the supreme spiritual pole, the imam, my master 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani and his followers; the supreme spiritual pole, al-Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi and his followers; the supreme spiritual pole, al-Sayyid Ibrahim al-Dusuqi and his followers; and the supreme spiritual pole, al-Sayyid 'Ali Abu al-Hasan al-Shadhili and his followers.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion on tasawwuf (spiritual wayfaring). It begins by establishing the necessity of having a spiritual guide (shaykh) who is a gnostic (ʿārif) and who has himself travelled the path under a qualified shaykh, with an unbroken chain back to the Prophet (peace be upon him). The consequence of not having such a guide is that the seeker falls prey to Satan, as indicated by the famous saying: 'He who has no shaykh, Satan is his shaykh.' Even if one performs immense worship, without a guide one cannot reach the stations of nearness to Allah. Next, the author describes the signs (ʿalāma) of a true shaykh: generosity, good character, compassion, detachment from worldly accumulation, absence of pretension (even refraining from using Sufi terminology unless necessary), not complaining about hardship or people's rejection, and displaying humility, brokenness, and love of obscurity. Moreover, his companions should exhibit blessing and righteousness. The author then traces this concept to the Qur'anic command: 'And follow the path of the devotees and the scholars' (paraphrased). He explains that 'devotees' (nāsikīn) means worshippers, and 'scholars' (ʿulamā') means those who know the legal rulings that uphold religion, both creedal and practical. By these, he means the righteous predecessors (salaf ṣāliḥ) and their followers. Their path comprises three elements: correct creed, knowledge, and action in accordance with knowledge. Thereafter, he divides those who came after this early generation into three groups, all of which are obligatory to follow. The first group dedicated itself to explaining practical legal rulings; they are the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad) and other mujtahids, but only the schools of these four have become established. The second group devoted itself to explaining the creed that the predecessors held; they are al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi and their followers. The third group focused on spiritual practice and struggles (mujāhadāt) in accordance with the first two groups; they are Abu al-Qasim al-Junayd and his followers. These three groups are the elite (khuwwāṣ) of the Prophet's Ummah. Anyone outside these groups is in error, though some may still be considered Muslims. Salvation requires correct creed according to Ahl al-Sunnah, following one of the four imams in practical rulings, and then perfecting one's religion by following the path of al-Junayd (i.e., tasawwuf). Finally, the author lists several later spiritual poles (aqṭāb) who followed al-Junayd's path: Ahmad al-Rifaʿi, ʿAbd al-Qadir al-Jilani, Ahmad al-Badawi, Ibrahim al-Dusuqi, and ʿAli Abu al-Hasan al-Shadhili, along with their followers. This establishes a clear hierarchy of knowledge and practice, integrating fiqh, kalam, and tasawwuf as complementary disciplines.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That one can attain closeness to Allah without a qualified spiritual guide, relying solely on personal effort or book knowledge.
Correction: The passage clearly states that without a shaykh, one cannot ascend to the stations of proximity and is exposed to Satan's deception.

Checkpoint

C) He becomes a follower of al-Junayd automatically.
D) He is considered a scholar of the Ummah.

Key Takeaway
A sincere seeker must find a qualified guide; his signs include generosity, humility, and detachment, and without him, Satan becomes the guide.

The Three Elite Groups of the Ummah
Dardeer identifies the three elite groups and later spiritual poles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of scholars that form the elite of the Muslim Ummah and their roles in preserving religion.

Core Idea
The saved person follows the four imams, Ash'ari and Maturidi, and Junayd.

Continuing from the necessity of a guide, Imam Dardeer now identifies the specific groups that must be followed after the salaf. He delineates the three elite groups: the jurists, the creedal theologians, and the spiritual masters, and emphasizes that salvation lies in adhering to all three.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the three groups
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the author defines the path of the salaf as comprised of creed, knowledge, and action.
2
Identify the three groups
Find the description of each group: the four imams (fiqh), al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi (creed), and al-Junayd (spirituality).
These are the elite (khuwwāṣ) of the Ummah.
3
Understand the hierarchy
The passage states that salvation requires correct creed, following a madhhab, and then traversing the path of Junayd. This shows the integration of all three.
4
Note the later poles
The author lists five later spiritual poles as examples of those who followed Junayd's path: al-Rifa'i, al-Jilani, al-Badawi, al-Dusuqi, and al-Shadhili.
This shows the living tradition.
5
Reflect on the warning
The passage warns that anyone outside these three groups is in error, even if they might still be Muslims.
This emphasizes the importance of adhering to the mainstream Sunni tradition.

الخامِسُ: اتِّباعُ شَيخٍ عارفٍ قد سلك طريقَ أَهْلِ اللهِ على يدِ شَيخٍ كذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى رسولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم، ومَنْ لم يصحب شيخاً يدُلُّه على الطريق إلى الله، واستقلَّ بما عنده مِنْ عبادةٍ أو علمٍ فقد تعرَّضَ لإغراء الشيطان له، ولهذا قيل: «مَنْ لا شَيخَ له فالشَّيطانُ شَيخُه». وبالجملةِ مَنْ لم يَسْلُكْ على يدِ شَيخٍ عارفٍ فلا يُمكنه الترقي إلى منازلِ القُربِ ولو أتى بعبادةِ الثَّقَلَين. وعلامتُهُ: السَّخاءُ، وحُسنُ الخُلُقِ، والشفَقةُ على خَلْقِ الله تعالى، وعَدَمُ انكبابه على جمع الدُّنيا، وعدمُ الدعوى، ولو بالتكلّم بمُصطَلَحِ القَومِ إلا لأمْرٍ اقتضى ذلك، وعدمُ الشكوى مِنْ ضيق الدُّنيا أو مِنْ إعراض الناس عنه، وأنْ يُرى عليه مخايل الذُّلِّ والانكِسارِ وحُبِّ الخُمول، وأن تظهر على أصحابه البركةُ والصلاح، وهذا مأخوذ من قولنا: (واتَّبَعْ) في سَيرِكَ ( سبيلَ) أي: طريقَ (الناسِكين) جمع «ناسك»، أي: عابد، (العُلَما) جمع «عالم»، وهو: العارفُ بالأحكام الشرعية التي عليها مدار صحة الدين، اعتقاديةً كانت أو عمليَّة، والمراد بهم السلف الصالحُ ومَنْ تبعهم بإحْسانٍ، وسبيلهم منحصر في اعتقادٍ وعِلْمٍ وعملٍ على طبق العِلْمِ. ومَنْ جاءَ بعدَهم مِنْ أئمّةِ الأُمَّةِ الذين يجب اتِّباعُهم على ثلاثِ فِرَقٍ: فرقةٌ نصَّبتْ نفسَها لبيان الأحكام الشرعية العملية، وهم الأئمة الأربعةُ وغيرُهم مِنَ المُجتهِدين، لكِنْ لم يستقِرَّ مِنَ المذاهبِ المَرْضِيَّةِ سوى مذاهب الأئمة الأربعة. وفرقةٌ نصَّبتْ نفسَها للاشتغال ببيان العقائد التي كان عليها السلف، وهم الأشعري والماتريدي ومَنْ تبعهما. وفرقةٌ نصَّبتْ نفسَها للاشتغال بالعَمَلِ والمجاهدات على طبق ما ذهب إليه الفرقتان المتقدمتان، وهم أبو القاسم الجنيد ومَنْ تبعه. فهؤلاء الفِرَقُ الثلاثةُ هُم خواصُّ الأُمَّةِ المحمدية، ومَنْ عداهم مِنْ جميعِ الفِرَقِ على ضلال، وإنْ كانَ البَعْضُ منهم يُحكَمُ له بالإسلام، فالناجي مَنْ كان في عقيدته على طبق ما بيَّنَه أهلُ السُّنَّة، وقلَّدَ في الأحكام العَمَلِيَّةِ إماماً مِنَ الأئمة الأربعةِ المرضيَّة، ثُمَّ تمامُ النِّعمةِ والنجاة في سُلوكِ مَسلكِ الجُنَيدِ وأتباعه بعدَ أَنْ أَحْكَمَ دينَه على طبق ما بيَّنَه الفريقان المتَقَدِّمان. ومَنْ سَلَكَ مَسلكَه القُطْبُ الربّانيُّ الإمام سيدي أحمدُ بنُ الرفاعي وأتباعه، والقطب الرباني الإمام سيدي عبد القادر الجيلاني وأتباعه، والقُطبُ الرباني السيد أحمد البدوي وأتباعه، والقُطبُ الرباني السيد إبراهيم الدسوقي وأتباعه، والقُطبُ الربانِيُّ السيدُ عليُّ أبو الحسن الشاذلي وأتباعه.
The fifth: Following a gnostic shaykh who has traveled the path of the people of Allah under the hand of a similar shaykh until he reaches the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Whoever does not accompany a shaykh who guides him to the path to Allah, and relies on what he himself has of worship or knowledge, has exposed himself to the deception of Satan for him, and for this it was said: 'He who has no shaykh, Satan is his shaykh.' In summary, whoever does not travel under the hand of a gnostic shaykh cannot ascend to the stations of proximity, even if he performs the worship of both thaqalayn (jinn and humans). And his sign: generosity, good character, compassion for Allah's creatures, not being preoccupied with accumulating worldly goods, absence of pretension—even by speaking in the terminology of the folk unless a matter necessitates it—absence of complaint about worldly hardship or people turning away from him, that one sees on him signs of humility, brokenness, and love of obscurity, and that blessing and righteousness appear on his companions. This is taken from our saying: 'And follow in your journey the path of the devotees (nāsikīn), plural of nāsik, i.e., worshipper, the scholars ('ulamā), plural of 'ālim, who is the knower of the legal rulings upon which the soundness of religion depends, whether creedal or practical. And by them is meant the righteous predecessors and those who follow them in excellence. Their path is comprised of creed, knowledge, and action in accordance with knowledge.' And those who came after them from the imams of the Ummah whose following is obligatory are three groups: A group that devoted itself to explaining the practical legal rulings—they are the four imams and others among the mujtahids, but only the schools of the four imams have become established among the approved schools. And a group that devoted itself to explaining the creeds which the predecessors held—they are al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi and those who follow them. And a group that devoted itself to spiritual practice and spiritual struggles (mujāhadāt) in accordance with what the two preceding groups held—they are Abu al-Qasim al-Junayd and those who follow him. These three groups are the elite of the Muhammadan Ummah. Whoever is other than them from all the sects is in error, even if some of them are judged to be Muslim. The saved person is the one whose creed is in accordance with what Ahl al-Sunnah explained, and who imitates in practical rulings an imam from the four approved imams. Then the completion of grace and salvation lies in traversing the path of al-Junayd and his followers after having perfected his religion in accordance with what the two preceding groups explained. And those who traveled his path: the supreme spiritual pole (quṭb), the imam, my master Ahmad ibn al-Rifa'i and his followers; the supreme spiritual pole, the imam, my master 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani and his followers; the supreme spiritual pole, al-Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi and his followers; the supreme spiritual pole, al-Sayyid Ibrahim al-Dusuqi and his followers; and the supreme spiritual pole, al-Sayyid 'Ali Abu al-Hasan al-Shadhili and his followers.

Criticism of False Sufis
Dardeer condemns false Sufis for following desires and exploiting charity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how false Sufis deceive people by following their desires and exploiting charity.

Core Idea
False Sufis follow desires and demand charity; true spirituality is selflessness.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer exposes the hypocrisy of those who claim spiritual status but actually exploit others. He describes how they have fallen back due to envy and desire, and how they manipulate charity into a custom. This critique prepares the ground for the true path of the fuqara.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of their fall
Notice how the author says they retreated because they followed their own desires and were led by Satan. This is a spiritual diagnosis.
The line of poetry highlights their envy-based preference for blindness.
2
Identify their corrupt practice
They take charity as a custom and demand it, threatening to expose those who don't comply. This is a sign of their falsehood.
3
Recognize their deception
They claim Allah confirms their claims, but this is a delusion. The author rejects this firmly in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل تأخروا ورجعوا القهقرى لأنهم تبعوا هوى أنفسهم، والشيطان يقودهم إلى كل ما يحبه منهم كما قال:
وعن مذهبي لما استحَبُّوا العمى على الـ* هُدى حَسَدًا مِنْ عِندِ أَنفُسِهِم ضَلُّوا
حتى صارَ مِنْ أو أكرمهم بكرامة أخلاقهم أن مَنْ تصدّق عليهم بـ
اتخذوا ذلك عادةً، وطالبوا بها مَنْ فَعَلَ معَهم الإحسان حتى يُضيقوا عليه المسالك، ويقولون: أعطنا عادتنا وإلا نتشَوَّف عليك، فيوهمون الناس أنهم أرباب أحوال، وأنَّ الله تعالى يُصدِّقُهم في المقال.
كلَّا
ما هذه طريقةُ الفُقَراءِ أهل اللهِ! إِنَّما طريقتهم التَّواضُعُ والانكسارُ وحُبُّ الحمول والعفة والزهد والورع والإيثار والتَّوَكُلُ.
وأما هؤلاء فهُمْ أشرار الناس يأكلون أموال الناس بالباطل، ويدعون المراتب العليّة، وهم في الدرَكاتِ السُّفْلِيّةِ، وقد كثروا في هذا الزمانِ حتى ملئوا طباق الأرضِ وفي كل قطر ومكان، نعوذ بالله منهم.
But they fell behind and retreated backwards because they followed their own desires, and Satan leads them to everything he loves from them, as he said: 'And with my doctrine, when they preferred blindness over guidance, out of envy from their own souls, they went astray.' Until there became from those of noble character that whoever gives charity to them takes that as a custom, and they demand it from whoever does good to them, until they narrow the paths upon him, and they say: 'Give us our custom, otherwise we will show off against you.' They delude people that they are masters of states and that Allah Almighty confirms them in speech. No! This is not the way of the poor, the people of Allah! Their way is humility, brokenness, love of bearing burdens, chastity, asceticism, scrupulousness, selflessness, and trust. As for these, they are the wicked of people, consuming people's wealth unjustly, claiming high ranks while they are in low depths, and they have become abundant in this age until they fill the layers of the earth and in every region and place. We seek refuge in Allah from them.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a condemnation of false claimants to Sufism and a clarification of the true path of the 'fuqara' (the poor in spirit, i.e., true Sufis). The author begins by stating that these people have fallen backward because they followed their own desires and allowed Satan to lead them. He then quotes a line of poetry indicating that their envy caused them to prefer blindness to guidance. He describes how they have turned charity into a habit, demanding it from those who help them, and threatening to expose them if not given. They deceive people into believing they are masters of spiritual states and that Allah confirms their claims. The author firmly rejects this with 'Kalla!' (No!). He then states that this is not the way of the true 'fuqara' of Allah. Their way is characterized by humility, brokenness, love of bearing burdens, chastity, asceticism, scrupulousness, selflessness, and trust in Allah. In contrast, these false ones are the wicked of people: they consume wealth unjustly, claim high spiritual ranks while actually being in low depths, and have proliferated greatly. The passage ends with a prayer for refuge from them.

عادة
أرباب أحوال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that demanding gifts and showing off are signs of spiritual rank.
Correction: The author clarifies that such behavior is actually a sign of being led by desire and Satan.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about those who demand charity as a custom?
A) They are following the way of the fuqara.
B) They are led by their desires and Satan.
C) They are humble.
D) They are to be honored.

Key Takeaway
False Sufis have fallen back by following desires, turning charity into a demand, and claiming divine confirmation; this is not the way of Allah's people.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act of charity or kindness, do you ever find yourself expecting something in return—even if just recognition? How does the false Sufis' demand for charity as a 'habit' reveal a subtle form of the same disease in your own heart? This week, commit to one act of charity that no one will ever know about.
?
The false Sufis preferred blindness over guidance due to envy. Is there any area in your life where you knowingly choose a lesser good (or even a sin) because you resent the guidance of Allah or the success of others? Ask Allah to purify your heart from hasad and give you the courage to follow the truth even when it is painful.
?
The impostors claimed that Allah 'confirms their statements.' Have you ever used religious language or claimed spiritual experiences to gain status in the eyes of others? Be honest: in what specific situation can you renounce that need for approval and instead seek only Allah's acceptance?

The True Path of the Fuqara
Dardeer describes the virtues of true fuqara and contrasts them with false claimants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the true qualities of the fuqara (people of Allah): humility, brokenness, and other virtues.

Core Idea
The true fuqara embody humility, brokenness, chastity, and trust in Allah.

After condemning false claimants, Imam Dardeer now clarifies what the path of the true fuqara actually entails. He lists essential virtues and contrasts them with the wickedness of those who consume wealth unjustly. This passage gives a concise definition of authentic Sufism.

Guided Path
1
Read the rejection 'Kalla'
Note the forceful negation. The author emphatically denies that the false behavior is the way of the fuqara.
2
List the virtues of the true fuqara
The author enumerates humility, brokenness, love of bearing burdens, chastity, asceticism, scrupulousness, selflessness, and trust in Allah. Reflect on each.
These are the core attributes of a true spiritual seeker.
3
Contrast with the false ones
The author then describes the false ones as wicked, consuming wealth unjustly, and claiming high ranks while in low depths.
This contrast reinforces the genuine path.
4
Note the proliferation of false ones
The author observes that such people have become abundant and fills the earth, and ends with a prayer for refuge.

بل تأخروا ورجعوا القهقرى لأنهم تبعوا هوى أنفسهم، والشيطان يقودهم إلى كل ما يحبه منهم كما قال:
وعن مذهبي لما استحَبُّوا العمى على الـ* هُدى حَسَدًا مِنْ عِندِ أَنفُسِهِم ضَلُّوا
حتى صارَ مِنْ أو أكرمهم بكرامة أخلاقهم أن مَنْ تصدّق عليهم بـ
اتخذوا ذلك عادةً، وطالبوا بها مَنْ فَعَلَ معَهم الإحسان حتى يُضيقوا عليه المسالك، ويقولون: أعطنا عادتنا وإلا نتشَوَّف عليك، فيوهمون الناس أنهم أرباب أحوال، وأنَّ الله تعالى يُصدِّقُهم في المقال.
كلَّا
ما هذه طريقةُ الفُقَراءِ أهل اللهِ! إِنَّما طريقتهم التَّواضُعُ والانكسارُ وحُبُّ الحمول والعفة والزهد والورع والإيثار والتَّوَكُلُ.
وأما هؤلاء فهُمْ أشرار الناس يأكلون أموال الناس بالباطل، ويدعون المراتب العليّة، وهم في الدرَكاتِ السُّفْلِيّةِ، وقد كثروا في هذا الزمانِ حتى ملئوا طباق الأرضِ وفي كل قطر ومكان، نعوذ بالله منهم.
But they fell behind and retreated backwards because they followed their own desires, and Satan leads them to everything he loves from them, as he said: 'And with my doctrine, when they preferred blindness over guidance, out of envy from their own souls, they went astray.' Until there became from those of noble character that whoever gives charity to them takes that as a custom, and they demand it from whoever does good to them, until they narrow the paths upon him, and they say: 'Give us our custom, otherwise we will show off against you.' They delude people that they are masters of states and that Allah Almighty confirms them in speech. No! This is not the way of the poor, the people of Allah! Their way is humility, brokenness, love of bearing burdens, chastity, asceticism, scrupulousness, selflessness, and trust. As for these, they are the wicked of people, consuming people's wealth unjustly, claiming high ranks while they are in low depths, and they have become abundant in this age until they fill the layers of the earth and in every region and place. We seek refuge in Allah from them.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a condemnation of false claimants to Sufism and a clarification of the true path of the 'fuqara' (the poor in spirit, i.e., true Sufis). The author begins by stating that these people have fallen backward because they followed their own desires and allowed Satan to lead them. He then quotes a line of poetry indicating that their envy caused them to prefer blindness to guidance. He describes how they have turned charity into a habit, demanding it from those who help them, and threatening to expose them if not given. They deceive people into believing they are masters of spiritual states and that Allah confirms their claims. The author firmly rejects this with 'Kalla!' (No!). He then states that this is not the way of the true 'fuqara' of Allah. Their way is characterized by humility, brokenness, love of bearing burdens, chastity, asceticism, scrupulousness, selflessness, and trust in Allah. In contrast, these false ones are the wicked of people: they consume wealth unjustly, claim high spiritual ranks while actually being in low depths, and have proliferated greatly. The passage ends with a prayer for refuge from them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that demanding gifts and showing off are signs of spiritual rank.
Correction: The author clarifies that the true way is humility, brokenness, and selflessness, not demands.

Checkpoint
What are the qualities of the true fuqara according to the author?
A) Demanding charity and showing off.
B) Humility, brokenness, chastity, etc.
C) Following desires.
D) Claiming high ranks.

Key Takeaway
The true fuqara are defined by humility, brokenness, and other virtues, not by demanding rights or showing off; false ones are wicked and abundant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage warns against consuming people's wealth unjustly. Is there any way you are taking from others (time, attention, resources) without right, while claiming a high spiritual status?
?
The false fuqara have become abundant. Look honestly at your own circle: do you recognize anyone who matches the negative description? What does that mean for your own sincerity?

The Withdrawal of True Saints in Times of Corruption
Dardeer quotes his teacher and explains the withdrawal of true saints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why true saints may withdraw from public guidance when corruption becomes widespread, and how their hiddenness serves divine wisdom.

Core Idea
When corruption prevails, true saints entrust the matter to Allah and withdraw.

Imam Dardeer, quoting his teacher al-Sayyid al-Bakri, describes a critical moment in spiritual history: the era when false claims and corruption became so rampant that the genuine people of Allah chose to close the doors of guidance. This lesson explores their decision and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the poetic quote and the prose commentary.
2
Understand the poetry
What does al-Sayyid al-Bakri's verse say about the state of the time? Identify the key points: the end of evil? the bitterness? the lack of deterrence? the abandonment of religion?
The poetry sets the scene for the response.
3
Identify the response
What did the people of Allah do in response to the abundance and corruption? Look for the verbs: they 'closed the doors' and 'entrusted the matter to the Lord'. Reflect on the significance of these actions.
Their response is passive and trustful, not aggressive.
4
Reflect on the outcome
What happened to the true saints? They became hidden, only known to those specially favored by Allah. Think about why this hiddenness is a sign of their sincerity.
The passage ends with a note on divine selection.
5
Connect to broader theology
How does this passage inform our understanding of saintly behavior in difficult times? Consider the balance between public duty and trust in Allah.
This connects to the concept of 'tawakkul' and spiritual discretion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أُستاذنا السيد البكري في الفية التصرف:
وقد نها في ذا الزمان شرهُمْ * حتى سما في الناس جدا مرهم
.
ولم يكُنْ هُمْ هُنا مَنْ يرْدعُ * مِنْ أَجْلِ ذا الدين الحنيفي ودعوا
ولما نظر أهل الله إلى كثرتهم، وكثرة فسادهم، واختِلالِ عقائدهم أغلقوا أبوابَ زوايا الإرشاد وفوَّضوا الأمر إلى ربِّ العباد، واختلفوا في الناس فلم يعرفهم إلَّا مَنْ خصه الله بالأنوار الإلهية والسعادة السرمدية.
Our teacher al-Sayyid al-Bakri said in his Alfiyyat al-Tasarruf: 'And indeed their evil in this time ended, until their bitterness became very high among people... And there was no one here to deter them, because of this the Hanifi religion they abandoned.' And when the people of Allah saw their abundance, the abundance of their corruption, and the confusion of their beliefs, they closed the doors of the corners of guidance and entrusted the matter to the Lord of servants, and they differed concerning the people, and none knew them except those whom Allah singled out with divine lights and eternal felicity.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents a poetic quote from the author's teacher, al-Sayyid al-Bakri, followed by the author's own commentary. The poetry describes how the evil of false Sufis has increased and their bitterness has become great among the people, and that there is no one to deter them for the sake of the true religion (al-Hanifiyya). The author then explains that when the true people of Allah (the saints) observed the great number, corruption, and confused beliefs of these false claimants, they responded by closing the doors of the 'zawaya' (corners, places of spiritual teaching) and leaving the matter to Allah, the Lord of servants. As a result, they became hidden; only those whom Allah has specially favored with divine lights and eternal happiness can recognize them.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: True saints must always be publicly engaged in teaching and reform.
Correction: As this passage shows, when corruption becomes overwhelming, true saints may withdraw and entrust the matter to Allah, becoming hidden except to those specially favored.

Checkpoint
What did the people of Allah do when they saw the abundance and corruption of false claimants?
A) They openly fought them and exposed their errors.

C) They joined them to reform from within.
D) They wrote books condemning them.

Key Takeaway
In times of overwhelming corruption, true saints may choose to withdraw from public guidance, leaving the matter to Allah, and only those divinely favored can recognize them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
How do you react when those you consider spiritual guides seem hidden or inactive? Does it shake your trust, or does it increase your reliance on Allah alone? Tonight, ask yourself: am I seeking guidance from Allah directly, or am I overly attached to visible figures?

The Seeker's Path: Taqwa, Shaykh, and Self-Sacrifice
Dardeer gives guidance to one who desires the path of tawhid and the need for a shaykh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the essential steps and qualities required for a sincere seeker of tawhid, as outlined by Imam Dardeer, including the crucial role of a gnostic shaykh and the necessity of self-sacrifice.

Core Idea
The path to tawhid requires a shaykh, taqwa, and offering your very self, not just wealth.

Dardeer addresses the sincere seeker whose soul longs for the path of abstraction (tajrid) and immersion in tawhid. He lays out a clear sequence: beginning with God-consciousness and reliance on Allah, seeking the means through the Prophet, and then finding a qualified shaykh. The passage emphasizes complete submission to the shaykh and the ultimate sacrifice of one's self. This lesson unpacks each element of this spiritual roadmap.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial prerequisites
Notice that Dardeer begins with three preconditions: taqwa, resorting to Allah, and tawassul through the Prophet. These are the foundations before even seeking a shaykh.
Tawassul is a legitimate means in this context.
2
Recognize the role of the gnostic shaykh
The passage describes the shaykh as a nurturer who purifies the soul and leads the seeker to the 'wine of love.' Reflect on why a living guide is necessary.
The shaykh is described as 'arif' – a knower of Allah.
3
Learn the attitude of submission
When the seeker meets the shaykh, he must be 'like a corpse in his hands' – complete surrender. This is a powerful metaphor for trust and obedience.
4
Appreciate the call to self-sacrifice
The passage contrasts giving wealth with giving one's self. The poetry emphasizes that true generosity is offering your soul, not your money.
This guards against the misconception that spiritual progress can be bought.
5
Reflect on the overall journey
The passage ends with gratitude and seriousness. See how all these elements form a coherent path from desire to immersion in tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلى مَنْ تشوّقتْ نفْسُه إلى سُلوكِ طريق التجريد، حتى يستغرق في بحار التوحيد، مُلازمةُ التَّقْوى والالتجاء إلى اللهِ والتَّوَسُّلُ إليه برسوله عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ في أن يجمَعَه على شَيخِ عارفٍ يُربّيه، ويُخْرِجُه مِنَ الظُّلُماتِ النَّفْسِيةِ، ويُصَفِّيه ويسقيه مِنْ خَمرِ المحبّة ويُصافيه.
فإذا علمَ اللهُ صِدقَكَ أطْلَعَكَ عليه، فإذا اجتمعت به فشُدَّ يدَكَ عليه، وكُنْ كالميت بين يديه، وقُلِ الْحَمْدُ للهِ الَّذِي هَدَانَا هَذَا وَمَا كُنَّا لِنَهْتَدِيَ لَوْلا أَنْ هَدَانَا اللَّهُ ﴾ ثُمَّ خُذْ في الجد والابتهال، وجُدْ بَنَفْسِكَ لا بالمالِ كما قالَ:
فنافس ببذل النفس فيها أخا الهوى * فَإِنْ قبلتها مِنكَ يا حبَّذا البذْلُ
ومَنْ لم يجد في حُبِّ نُعْمَ بنفسه * ولو جادَ بالدُّنْيا إليه انتهى البُخْلُ
So upon one whose soul longs to traverse the path of abstraction until he becomes immersed in the seas of tawhid (divine unity), he must adhere to taqwa (God-consciousness), resort to Allah, and seek intercession through His Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him), that Allah may bring him together with a gnostic shaykh who will nurture him, bring him out of the darknesses of the soul, purify him, give him to drink from the wine of love, and be his intimate friend. When Allah knows your sincerity, He will make you find him. When you meet him, then grasp him firmly, be like a corpse in his hands, and say: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided us to this; we would not have been guided if Allah had not guided us.' Then take up seriousness and supplication, and be generous with your self, not with wealth, as he said: 'So vie in giving your self in it, O brother of desire; if it accepts from you, O how excellent is the gift! And whoever does not find himself in the love of Nu'm, even if he gives the whole world, stinginess ends at him.'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a piece of spiritual advice for the sincere seeker. The author outlines the prerequisites and steps for one whose soul yearns to journey on the path of 'tajrid' (abstraction from worldly attachments) and immersion in the seas of tawhid (divine unity). First, the seeker must adhere to taqwa, take refuge in Allah, and seek the means (tawassul) through the Prophet. Then he should pray to be brought together with a knowledgable shaykh (murabbi) who can nurture him, remove the darkness of the lower self, purify him, and give him the wine of love. When Allah sees the seeker's sincerity, He will cause him to find such a shaykh. Upon meeting him, the seeker must cling to him, be like a corpse in his hands (i.e., complete submission), and thank Allah for guidance. Then the seeker must be serious and supplicate, and sacrifice his very self (not just wealth) in the path. The passage concludes with a poetic illustration that the true competition is in offering one's soul, not wealth.

Key Terms

توحيد
تقوى
توسل
