Seeking Protection from Spiritual Cut-offs and Purifying Intention
Author explains supplication and enumerates spiritual cut-offs with correct intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various spiritual cut-offs that distract from worship and the importance of purifying one's intention to worship Allah for His own sake.

Core Idea
Worship for reward is a spiritual cutter; pure worship is for Allah alone.

The author explains a supplication asking Allah to protect from everything that cuts off the heart from Him. He then warns against hidden cut-offs, including worship motivated by reward or spiritual openings, and emphasizes that true worship is for Allah's essence alone. This lesson unpacks these teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the supplication and explanation
Start by reading the poetic supplication and its explanation. Notice the posture of humility (ذُل) mentioned.
The supplication is addressed to Allah as a broken-hearted servant.
2
Identify the types of cut-offs
List the cut-offs that occupy the heart from worship: love of wealth, children, status, desires, and also pride, hatred, hypocrisy, and self-admiration. Note the Quranic verses cited.
Worship for reward or spiritual openings is also included as a cutter.
3
Understand the correct intention
Contrast the wrong intention (worship for reward or opening) with the correct one (worship for Allah's essence and obedience). The author explains that openings come from grace, veils from justice.
The servant has no right to demand divine favors.
4
Reflect on Ibn Ata'illah's wisdom
Read the concluding quote from Ibn Ata'illah and see how it reinforces the lesson: focus on your own faults rather than seeking hidden knowledge.
This aligns with the idea of self-purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقُلْ بدلّ: ربِّ لا تقطعني * عنكَ بقاطع ولا تحرمني -- ٦٩ - مِنْ سُرِّكَ الأبهى المزيل للعمى * واختِمُ بخَير يا رحيمَ الرُّحَما ** (وقُلْ) مُتَضرعًا إلى ربِّكَ قَولًا مُلْتَبسًا (بذُلٌ)، فإِنَّ اللهَ تعالى عِندَ المُنكَسِرةِ قلوبهم: يا (رب لا تقطعني عنك بقاطع) مِنْ كُلِّ فِتنة يشْتَغِلُ القَلْبُ بها عنِ العُبوديَّةِ، مِنْ حُبِّ المالِ والولد والجاءِ والشهَواتِ إِنَّمَا أَمْوَالُكُمْ وَأَوْلَادُكُمْ فِتْنَةٌ ﴾ ، ﴿زُيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ حُبُّ الشَّهَوَاتِ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ وَالْبَنِينَ (٢) الآية، ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُواْ لاَ تُلْهِكُمْ أَمْوَالُكُمْ وَلَا أَوْلَادُكُمْ عَن ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فَأُولئِكَ هُمُ الْخَاسِرُونَ ﴾ (٣) (Y), ومِنَ القواطع الكبر والحقد والرياء والعُجْبُ ، ومنها: العبادة لأجل حصول هو ثَواب، أو حُصولِ فتْحِ لَدُنْي؛ ليكونَ مِنْ أولياء الله، وإنما شأنهم أن يعبدوا اللهَ تعالى لذاته وامتثالا لأمره ونهيه، ثُمَّ إِنْ  َحصَلَ لهم فتح فذلك مِنْ فَضْلِه، وإنْ حُجِبوا فذلك مِنْ عدله؛ إذْ لَيسَ للعبد على مولاه حقٌّ، وإنما الحق له تعالى على العبد. فالعَبدُ مطلوب بأن يُخلص نفْسَه مِنَ الرُّعوناتِ النفْسيّة، ولَيسَ على الله تعالى أنْ يهبه المعارِفَ القُدْسيّة. والذي يعبُدُه لذلك معْدودٌ عِندَهم مِنْ عَبيدِ السوءِ الذين إذا لم يؤجَروا يعملوا، وهذا ينافي كونَه عبدًا مُحْضًا. قال العارف بالله تعالى ابنُ عَطاءِ اللهِ السَّكَنْدَريُّ فِي الحِكَم: «تشَوُّفُكَ إلى ما بطنَ فيكَ مِنَ العُيوبِ، خَيْرٌ مِنْ تشَوُفِكَ إلى ما حُجِبَ عنك مِنَ الغُيوبِ».
And say with humility: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter, and do not deprive me of Your most beautiful secret that removes blindness, and conclude with good, O Most Merciful of the merciful. (And say) humbly to your Lord a word clothed in lowliness, for Allah Almighty is with those whose hearts are broken: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter from every trial that occupies the heart from worship, such as love of wealth, children, status, and desires: 'Indeed your wealth and children are a trial', 'Adorned for people is the love of desires from women and children' (verse), 'O you who believe, let not your wealth and children divert you from the remembrance of Allah, and whoever does that, they are the losers.' And among the cut-offs are pride, hatred, hypocrisy, and self-admiration. And among them is worship for the sake of obtaining reward or obtaining an opening from God, so that one might be among the saints. Rather, their affair is to worship Allah Almighty for His essence and in obedience to His command and prohibition. Then, if they obtain an opening, it is from His grace, and if they are veiled, it is from His justice, since the servant has no right over his Master; rather, the right belongs to Him Almighty over the servant. The servant is required to purify his soul from egotistical follies, and it is not upon Allah Almighty to grant him sacred knowledge. And whoever worships Him for that reason is counted among them as a bad servant who works only if they are rewarded, and this contradicts being a pure servant. The knower of Allah Almighty, Ibn Ata'illah al-Sakandari, said in the Hikam: 'Your concern for what is hidden of your faults is better than your concern for what is hidden from you of unseen matters.'
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the poet's supplication and an exhortation to purify one's intention in worship. The author begins by quoting the poetic line: 'And say with humility: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter' and explains that the supplication is to be made with lowliness, for Allah is with the broken-hearted. He then enumerates the 'cutters' (qawati') that distract the heart from worship: love of wealth, children, status, and desires, citing Quranic verses to support this. He adds other spiritual diseases like pride, hatred, hypocrisy, and self-admiration. Crucially, he includes worship performed for the sake of reward or spiritual openings (fath) as one of these cut-offs. The proper way of the saints is to worship Allah for His own sake and in obedience to His command, not for any gain. If an opening comes, it is grace; if not, it is justice. The servant's duty is to purify his soul, and Allah is not obliged to grant mystical knowledge. Worship motivated by reward is blameworthy, making one a 'bad servant'. The passage concludes with a quote from Ibn Ata'illah emphasizing that self-criticism is more beneficial than seeking hidden knowledge of the unseen.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Requesting spiritual openings in worship is always wrong.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the problem is making openings the motive for worship, not the request itself. Openings can come from Allah's grace if one's intention is pure.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct intention in worship?
A) To obtain spiritual openings
B) To avoid punishment
C) For Allah's essence and obedience to His command
D) To become a saint

Key Takeaway
Worship must be for Allah alone, not for reward or spiritual openings; the servant's duty is self-purification, not demanding divine favors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever honestly examined the hidden motives behind your daily prayers, charity, or dhikr? If you removed all hope of reward or spiritual feeling, would you still do them? What does your answer reveal about the state of your heart?
?
Which of the spiritual cut-offs listed in this passage—wealth, status, desire for reward—is currently most active in distracting you from pure worship? What concrete step will you take this week to sever it?
?
The author says the servant has no right over Allah to demand openings or knowledge. When you pray for guidance or closeness, do you feel entitled to receive it? Can you accept worship without ever feeling any spiritual sweetness, trusting that Allah's justice is perfect?

intermediate

Objection: Asking for Spiritual Openings vs. Worship for Them
The author answers an objection by distinguishing between supplication for openings and worship motivated by openings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the critical distinction between permissible supplication for Allah's grace and blameworthy worship motivated by the desire for that grace.

Core Idea
Asking Allah for openings is worship; worshipping for openings is not.

The author anticipates a potential objection: if seeking spiritual openings through worship is condemned, why command the seeker to ask for them? This passage provides a nuanced answer, distinguishing between the act of supplication (which is itself a form of worship) and the act of worship that is performed for the sake of obtaining something. Understanding this distinction is key to purifying one's intention.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the imagined objection and the author's response. Note how the author reframes the question.
The objection might seem to create a contradiction; the author clarifies by distinguishing two activities.
2
Identify the two activities
Notice the difference between 'طلب الفتح' (requesting opening) as supplication and 'العبادة من أجل الفتح' (worship for opening) as a transactional act.
The key is the intention behind each.
3
Reflect on the evidence
The author cites examples from the Quran and Sunnah: obligatory supplication for guidance (al-Fatiha) and recommended supplications for worldly needs. These are acts of worship, not blameworthy.
This shows that asking itself is commanded and rewarded.
4
Grasp the key principle
Understand that the blameworthy act is to perform worship primarily to obtain something, not the act of asking itself.
The author says 'this is other than worship for the sake of obtaining something.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يُقالُ : إذا كانتِ العِبادةُ مِنْ أَجْلِ الفتْحِ مِنَ القَواطع، فَكَيفَ يصح أنْ تأْمُرَه طلبه بقولِكَ وقُلْ بذل ربِّ لا تقطعني عنكَ بقاطع»؟! لأَنا نقولُ: طَلَبُ الفتح فيض فضل الله تعالى لا في مُقابلة شَيءٍ، لكِنْ معَ الاستقامةِ أَمْرٌ مطلوب شرعًا، عَطلَبكَ منه سَعَةَ الرِّزْقِ وصِحْةَ البدنِ والشفاءَ مِنَ الأمْراضِ الحِسَيَةِ، ألا ترى أنه أوجَبَ عليك طلب الهداية في كُلِّ يَوم وليلة سَبْعَ عشرةَ مَرَّةً في قوله تعالى: اهْدِنَا الصِّرَاطَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ (۱) ، وطلَبَ مِنكَ ندبًا غَيرَ ذلك في النَّوافل كثيرًا بلا حد؟! وهذا غَيرُ العِبادةِ لأَجْلِ حُصولِ شَيءٍ، فإنّها ليست طريقة المقربين ، فَافُهُمْ ).
It is not said: If worship for the sake of opening is among the cut-offs, then how is it valid that you command him to request it by your saying: 'And say with humility: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter'? For we say: Requesting opening is a flow of the grace of Allah Almighty, not in exchange for anything, but with uprightness it is a matter sought legally. And He asked you for ample provision, health of body, and cure from physical illnesses. Do you not see that He obligated you to ask for guidance every day and night seventeen times in His saying: 'Guide us to the straight path' (1), and He asked you supererogatorily for much of that in the nawafil without limit? And this is other than worship for the sake of obtaining something, for that is not the way of the near ones, so understand.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. The objector raises a potential contradiction: if worship motivated by seeking spiritual openings (fath) is condemned as a 'cutter', then how can the author command the supplicant to ask for exactly that (i.e., 'do not cut me off from Your openings')? The author answers by distinguishing between two things: (1) asking Allah for an opening as a prayer, which is a request for His grace and is permissible—even commendable if accompanied by uprightness; and (2) worshipping with the intention of obtaining that opening, which is blameworthy. The author supports this by noting that Allah commands us to ask for guidance (in al-Fatiha) and encourages asking for worldly needs like provision and health. Such requests are not equivalent to worshipping for reward. The latter is the way of the 'near ones' (muqarrabun), but the former is simply supplication. The key point is the distinction between the act of worship (which should be for Allah alone) and the act of supplication (which is itself a form of worship and permissible).

Key Terms
فتح
عبادة من أجل الفتح
طلب الفتح
استقامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any request for worldly or spiritual gain from Allah is blameworthy and contradicts pure worship.
Correction: The author clarifies that asking (du'a) is encouraged and even commanded, while worship motivated by the desire for gain is what is blameworthy. Supplication itself is an act of worship.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between blameworthy worship and permissible asking according to the author?
A) The intention behind the action
B) The number of times one asks
C) The type of request (spiritual vs. worldly)
D) The status of the person asking

Key Takeaway
The difference lies in intention: asking (du'a) is worship and encouraged, but performing other acts of worship with the primary aim of obtaining something is blameworthy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever performed an act of worship hoping for a specific spiritual benefit, like a feeling or an opening? Did that expectation distract you from the pure act of worship itself?
?
When you ask Allah for guidance in every rak'ah, do you consider that request itself an act of worship, or just a means to an end? How does the distinction in this lesson change how you recite al-Fatiha?
?
Is there any area of your worship where you find yourself 'bargaining' with Allah—I will pray more if I get something in return? How can you shift to worshipping purely for Allah's sake?
